{{short description|Impact of COVID-19 on political systems}}
{{Use dmy dates|date=May 2020}}
[[File:World elections altered.svg|thumb|upright=1.5|Countries with at least one election date altered]]
{{COVID-19 pandemic sidebar|expanded=issues}}
The [[COVID-19 pandemic]] has impacted international relations and affected the political systems of multiple countries, causing suspensions of legislative activities, isolation or deaths of multiple politicians and reschedulings of elections due to fears of spreading the virus. The pandemic has triggered broader debates about political issues such as the relative advantages of democracy and autocracy,<ref>{{cite journal |last1= Ang |first1= Yuen Yuen |date= 2020 |title= When COVID-19 meets centralized, personalized power |url= https://www.nature.com/articles/s41562-020-0872-3 |journal= Nature Human Behavior |volume= 4 |issue= 5 |pages= 445–447 |doi= 10.1038/s41562-020-0872-3 |pmid= 32273583 |s2cid= 215532797 }}</ref><ref>{{cite journal |last1= Stasavage |first1= David |date= 2020 |title= Democracy, Autocracy, and Emergency Threats: Lessons for COVID-19 From the Last Thousand Years |url= https://doi.org/10.1017/S0020818320000338 |journal= International Organization |pages= 1–17 |doi= 10.1017/S0020818320000338 }}</ref> how states respond to crises,<ref>{{cite journal |last1= Lipscy |first1= Phillip |date= 2020 |title= COVID-19 and the Politics of Crisis |url= https://www.cambridge.org/core/journals/international-organization/article/covid19-and-the-politics-of-crisis/CFEB29F225E5238F29C3233E873F0485 |journal= International Organization |pages= 1–30 |doi= 10.1017/S0020818320000375 |s2cid= 225135699 }}</ref> politicization of beliefs about the virus,<ref>{{cite journal |last1= Druckman |first1= James |last2= Klar |first2= Samara |date= 2020 |title= How Affective Polarization Shapes Americans' Political Beliefs: A Study of Response to the COVID-19 Pandemic |url= https://www.cambridge.org/core/journals/journal-of-experimental-political-science/article/how-affective-polarization-shapes-americans-political-beliefs-a-study-of-response-to-the-covid19-pandemic/B52D17EA47CCC436E8B1B3E008CA2A79 |journal= Journal of Experimental Political Science |pages= 1–12 |doi= 10.1017/XPS.2020.28 |s2cid= 222312130 }}</ref> and the adequacy of existing frameworks of international cooperation.<ref>{{cite journal |last1= Fazal |first1= Tanisha |date= 2020 |title= Health Diplomacy in Pandemical Times |url= https://www.cambridge.org/core/journals/international-organization/article/health-diplomacy-in-pandemical-times/A82469023B94AA29F23A52AF0C4B3F27 |journal= International Organization |pages= 1–20 |doi= 10.1017/S0020818320000326 |s2cid= 229265358 }}</ref>

==General impacts==
[[File:Krajské volby 2020, Olomouc.jpg|thumb|Anti-pandemic precautions during the 2020 Czech regional elections]]
The response to the pandemic has resulted in unprecedented expansion of government power. Advocates of small government worry that the state will be reluctant to give up that power once the crisis is over, as has often been the case historically.<ref>''The Economist'', March 28th 2020, page 7.</ref>

===Leader popularity===

There is evidence that the pandemic has caused a [[Rally 'round the flag effect|rally-round-the-flag effect]] in many countries, with government approval ratings rising in [[Italy]] (+27 percentage points), Germany (+11), France (+11), and the United Kingdom.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://europeelects.eu/2020/04/02/rally-around-the-flag-corona-and-voting-behaviour-in-europe/|title=EU Parliament Projection: Corona Rallies Europeans Around the Flag|last=Schminke|first=Tobias Gerhard|date=2 April 2020|website=[[Europe Elects]]|language=en|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref><ref name=":1">{{cite web|url=https://www.vox.com/2020/3/31/21199702/rally-round-the-flag-coronavirus|title=Trump's coronavirus poll bump, explained|last=Yglesias|first=Matthew|date=31 March 2020|website=Vox|language=en|access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://voxeu.org/article/rallying-effect-lockdowns|title=COVID-19 lockdowns have increased support for incumbents, trust in government, and satisfaction with democracy|last=Bol|first=Damien Giani, Marco, Blais, André, Loewen, Peter John|date=7 May 2020|website=[[VoxEU]]|language=en|access-date=11 July 2020}}</ref> In the United States, President [[Donald Trump]] has seen a 6-point drop in approval,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.gallup.com/poll/308675/trump-job-rating-slides-satisfaction-tumbles.aspx|title=Trump's Job rating slides; U.S. satisfaction tumbles|last=McCarthy|first=Justin|date=16 April 2020|website=Gallup|language=en|access-date=21 April 2020}}</ref> while state governors have seen increases as high as 55 points for New York Governor [[Andrew Cuomo]], 31 points for North Carolina Governor [[Roy Cooper]], and 30 points for Michigan Governor [[Gretchen Whitmer]].<ref name=":1" />

===States of emergency===

At least 84 countries have declared a state of emergency in response to the pandemic, leading to fears about misuse of power.<ref name=":5">{{Cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/international/2020/04/23/would-be-autocrats-are-using-covid-19-as-an-excuse-to-grab-more-power|title=Would-be autocrats are using covid-19 as an excuse to grab more power|work=The Economist|access-date=27 April 2020|issn=0013-0613}}</ref> [[Reporters Without Borders]] has claimed that 38 countries have restricted [[freedom of the press]] as a result.<ref name=":5" /> Other examples include banning mass protests, postponing elections or holding them while the opposition cannot effectively campaign, selectively enforcing lockdown rules on political opponents, handing out relief payments to political supporters, or scapegoating minorities.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/leaders/2020/04/23/autocrats-see-opportunity-in-disaster|title=Autocrats see opportunity in disaster|work=The Economist|access-date=27 April 2020|issn=0013-0613}}</ref> Many countries have also unveiled large-scale [[surveillance]] programs for [[contact tracing]], leading to worries about their impact on [[privacy]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://carnegieendowment.org/2020/03/31/beware-implications-of-coronavirus-surveillance-pub-81411|title=Beware the Implications of Coronavirus Surveillance|last=Feldstein|first=Steven|website=Carnegie Endowment for International Peace|language=en|access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref>

==Impact on international relations==
{{main|Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on international relations}}

===European Union===
{{main|European Union response to the COVID-19 pandemic}}
The Spanish Prime Minister [[Pedro Sánchez]] stated that "If we don't propose now a unified, powerful and effective response to this economic crisis, not only the impact will be tougher, but its effects will last longer and we will be putting at risk the entire European project", while the Italian Prime Minister [[Giuseppe Conte]] commented that "the whole European project risks losing its raison d'être in the eyes of our own citizens".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.euronews.com/2020/03/28/eu-will-lose-its-raison-d-etre-if-it-fails-to-help-during-covid-19-crisis-italy-s-pm-warns|title=EU will lose its 'raison d'etre' if it fails to help during COVID-19 crisis, Italy's PM warns|date=28 March 2020}}</ref> From 4 to 19 March, Germany banned the export of [[personal protective equipment]],<ref>{{cite news |title=Germany bans export of medical protection gear due to coronavirus |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/health-coronavirus-germany-exports/germany-bans-export-of-medical-protection-gear-due-to-coronavirus-idUSL8N2AX3D9 |access-date=2 April 2020 |work=Reuters |date=4 March 2020 |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Germany lifts export ban on medical equipment over coronavirus |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-germany-exports/germany-lifts-export-ban-on-medical-equipment-over-coronavirus-idUSKBN2162SH |access-date=2 April 2020 |work=Reuters |date=19 March 2020 |language=en}}</ref> and France also restricted exports of medical equipment, drawing criticism from EU officials who called for solidarity.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Tsang |first1=Amie |title=E.U. Seeks Solidarity as Nations Restrict Medical Exports |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/07/business/eu-exports-medical-equipment.html |access-date=2 April 2020 |work=The New York Times |date=7 March 2020}}</ref> Many [[Schengen Area]] countries closed their borders to stem the spread of the virus.<ref name=wtimes>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus Is a Critical Test for the European Union |url=https://time.com/5805783/coronavirus-european-union/ |access-date=2 April 2020 |work=Time |language=en}}</ref>

====Jointly issued debt====
{{main|corona bonds}}
Debates over how to respond to the epidemic and its economic fallout have opened up a rift between [[Northern Europe|Northern]] and [[Southern Europe]]an member states, reminiscent of debates over the 2010s [[European debt crisis]].<ref name=":0">{{cite web|url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/03/30/coronavirus-pandemic-europe-north-south-eurobond/|title=Fighting Pandemic, Europe Divides Again Along North and South Lines|last=Johnson|first=Keith|website=Foreign Policy|language=en-US|access-date=2 April 2020}}</ref> Nine EU countries—Italy, France, Belgium, Greece, Portugal, Spain, Ireland, Slovenia and Luxembourg—called for "[[corona bonds]]" (a type of [[eurobond (eurozone)|eurobond]]) in order to help their countries to recover from the epidemic, on 25 March. Their letter stated, "The case for such a common instrument is strong, since we are all facing a symmetric external shock."<ref>{{cite news |last1=Amaro |first1=Silvia |title=Nine European countries say it is time for 'corona bonds' as virus death toll rises |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2020/03/25/nine-eu-countries-say-its-time-for-corona-bonds-as-virus-deaths-rise.html |access-date=28 March 2020 |work=CNBC |date=25 March 2020 |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=The EU can't agree on how to help Italy and Spain pay for coronavirus relief |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/03/27/economy/corona-bonds-eu/index.html |access-date=28 March 2020 |work=CNN}}</ref> Northern European countries such as  Germany, Austria, Finland, and the Netherlands oppose the issuing of joint debt, fearing that they would have to pay it back in the event of a default. Instead, they propose that countries should apply for loans from the [[European Stability Mechanism]].<ref name="future">{{cite news |title=Italy's future is in German hands |url=https://www.politico.eu/article/coronavirus-italy-future-germany/ |access-date=2 April 2020 |work=POLITICO |date=2 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="Greek" /> Corona bonds were discussed on 26 March 2020 in a [[European Council]] meeting, which dragged out for three hours longer than expected due to the "emotional" reactions of the prime ministers of Spain and Italy.<ref>{{cite news |title=Virtual summit, real acrimony: EU leaders clash over 'corona bonds' |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2020/03/26/virtual-summit-real-acrimony-eu-leaders-clash-over-corona-bonds-151291 |access-date=28 March 2020 |work=POLITICO |language=en}}</ref><ref name=Euronews/> European Council President [[Charles Michel]]<ref name=Greek>{{cite news |last1=Bayer |first1=Lili |title=EU response to corona crisis 'poor,' says senior Greek official |url=https://www.politico.eu/article/eu-response-to-coronavirus-crisis-poor-says-senior-greek-official/ |access-date=2 April 2020 |work=POLITICO |date=1 April 2020}}</ref> and [[European Central Bank]] head [[Christine Lagarde]] have urged the EU to consider issuing joint debt.<ref name=Euronews>{{cite news |title=What are 'corona bonds' and how can they help revive the EU's economy? |url=https://www.euronews.com/2020/03/26/what-are-corona-bonds-and-how-can-they-help-revive-the-eu-s-economy |access-date=28 March 2020 |work=euronews |date=26 March 2020 |language=en}}</ref> Unlike the [[European debt crisis]]—partly caused by the affected countries—southern European countries did not cause the coronavirus pandemic, therefore eliminating the appeal to national responsibility.<ref name="future" />

====Civil liberties====
Sixteen member nations of the European Union issued a statement warning that certain emergency measures issued by countries during the coronavirus pandemic could undermine the principles of rule of law and democracy on 1 April. They announced that they "support the European Commission initiative to monitor the emergency measures and their application to ensure the fundamental values of the Union are upheld."<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.government.nl/documents/diplomatic-statements/2020/04/01/statement-by-belgium-denmark-finland-france-germany-greece-ireland-italy-luxembourg-the-netherlands-portugal-spain-sweden |title=Statement by Belgium, Denmark, Estonia, Finland, France, Germany, Greece, Ireland, Italy, Latvia, Lithuania, Luxembourg, the Netherlands, Portugal, Spain, Sweden |date=1 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404024952/https://www.government.nl/documents/diplomatic-statements/2020/04/01/statement-by-belgium-denmark-finland-france-germany-greece-ireland-italy-luxembourg-the-netherlands-portugal-spain-sweden |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref> The statement does not mention Hungary, but observers believe that it implicitly refers to a Hungarian law granting [[plenary power]] to the Hungarian Government during the coronavirus pandemic. The following day, the Hungarian Government joined the statement.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://444.hu/2020/04/02/trolldiplomacia-a-maximumon-a-magyar-kormany-is-csatlakozott-a-jogallamisagot-vedo-europai-nyilatkozathoz |title=Trolldiplomácia a maximumon: A magyar kormány is csatlakozott a jogállamiságot védő európai nyilatkozathoz |date=2 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://index.hu/belfold/2020/04/02/a_magyar_kormany_is_csatlakozott_ahhoz_kiallashoz_ami_kimondatlanul_ugyan_de_ellene_szol/ |title=A magyar kormány is csatlakozott ahhoz a kiálláshoz, ami kimondatlanul ugyan, de ellene szól |date=2 April 2020}}</ref>

The [[National Assembly (Hungary)|Hungarian parliament]] passed the law granting plenary power to the Government by qualified majority, 137 to 53 votes in favor, on 30 March 2020. After promulgating the law, the [[President of Hungary]], [[János Áder]], announced that he had concluded that the time frame of the Government's authorization would be definite and its scope would be limited.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://nepszava.hu/3072783_megvolt-a-ketharmad-a-kormanyparti-tobbseg-megszavazta-a-felhatalmazasi-torvenyt |title=Megvolt a kétharmad, a kormánypárti többség megszavazta a felhatalmazási törvényt |date=30 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://hvg.hu/itthon/20200330_A_Fideszketharmad_elfogadta_a_felhatalmazasi_torvenyt |title=A Fidesz-kétharmad elfogadta a felhatalmazási törvényt |date=30 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://index.hu/belfold/2020/03/30/koronavirus-torveny_koronavirus_szavazas_parlament/ |title=Megszavazta az Országgyűlés a koronavírus-törvényt, Áder pedig ki is hirdette |date=30 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://444.hu/2020/03/30/ader-janos-mar-ala-is-irta-a-felhatalmazasi-torvenyt |title=Áder János már alá is írta a felhatalmazási törvényt |date=30 March 2020}}</ref> [[Ursula von der Leyen]], the [[President of the European Commission]], stated that she was concerned about the Hungarian emergency measures and that it should be limited to what is necessary and Minister of State [[Michael Roth (politician)|Michael Roth]] suggested that economic sanctions should be used against Hungary.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://news.trust.org/item/20200402100718-9f3pd/ |title=EU executive chief concerned Hungary emergency measures go too far |date=2 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404024630/https://news.trust.org/item/20200402100718-9f3pd/ |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.dailysabah.com/world/europe/eu-sanctions-over-hungarys-virus-measures-should-be-considered-german-official-says |title=EU sanctions over Hungary's virus measures should be considered, German official says |date=3 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404025218/https://www.dailysabah.com/world/europe/eu-sanctions-over-hungarys-virus-measures-should-be-considered-german-official-says |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref>

The heads of thirteen member parties of the [[European People's Party]] (EPP) made a proposal to expunge the Hungarian [[Fidesz]] for the new legislation on 2 April. In response, Viktor Orbán expressed his willingness to discuss any issues relating to Fidesz's membership "once the pandemic is over" in a letter addressed to the Secretary General of EPP [[Antonio López-Istúriz White]]. Referring to the thirteen leading politicians' proposal, Orbán also stated that "I can hardly imagine that any of us having time for fantasies about the intentions of other countries. This seems to be a costly luxury these days."<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://index.hu/kulfold/eurologus/2020/04/03/orban_nincs_idom_most_erre_neppart_kizaras/ |title=Orbán a Néppártnak: Most nincs időm erre! |date=3 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404045745/https://index.hu/kulfold/eurologus/2020/04/03/orban_nincs_idom_most_erre_neppart_kizaras/ |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref> During a video conference of the foreign ministers of the European Union member states on 3 April 2020, Hungarian Minister of Foreign Affairs, [[Péter Szijjártó]], asked for the other ministers to read the legislation itself not its politically motivated presentations in newspapers before commenting on it.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://index.hu/kulfold/eurologus/2020/04/03/szijjarto_jogallamisag_kulugyminiszterek_koronavirus_jarvany_vedekezes |title=Szijjártó looked virtually into the eyes of his critics |date=3 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404033955/https://index.hu/kulfold/eurologus/2020/04/03/szijjarto_jogallamisag_kulugyminiszterek_koronavirus_jarvany_vedekezes |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref>

===Japan–South Korea relations===

[[Japan–South Korea relations]] worsened as a result of the pandemic.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://thediplomat.com/2020/03/covid-19-aggravates-an-already-tense-korea-japan-relationship/|title=COVID-19 Aggravates an Already Tense Korea-Japan Relationship|last=Gibson|first=Jenna|website=thediplomat.com|language=en-US|access-date=30 March 2020}}</ref> After [[Japan]] declared it would start quarantining all arrivals from [[South Korea]], the South Korean government described the move as "unreasonable, excessive and extremely regrettable", and that it couldn't "help but question whether Japan has other motives than containing the outbreak".<ref>{{Cite news|last=Farrer|first=Justin McCurry Martin|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/06/coronavirus-quarantine-plans-ignite-row-between-south-korea-and-japan|title=Coronavirus quarantine plans ignite row between South Korea and Japan|date=6 March 2020|work=The Guardian|access-date=30 March 2020|language=en-GB|issn=0261-3077}}</ref> Some South Korean media have offered opinions to improve relations with Japan through mask assistance to Japan.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.koreatimes.co.kr/www/opinion/2020/05/202_288239.html|date=21 April 2020|title=Face mask aid to Japan|website=The Korea Times|access-date=10 May 2020}}</ref> In addition, some local governments in Japan who did not disclose their names have also announced their intention to purchase masks in Korea.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.sbs.co.kr/news/endPage.do?news_id=N1005761951|title=[단독] 일본 지자체도 "한국 마스크 구입 도와달라"|website=SBS news|date=24 April 2020|language=ko|access-date=10 May 2020}}</ref> When this fact became known, some online commentators in Japan expressed that they would never receive a mask even if it came from Korea, as it would not be free, as it would be a public pressure for concede of the Japanese government if South Korea gave masks to Japan.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.hankookilbo.com/News/Read/202004201543311493|date=20 April 2020|title=한국의 마스크 지원 검토에 일본 누리꾼들 "공짜보다 비싼 건 없다"|language=ko|publisher=Hankook Ilbo|access-date=10 May 2020}}</ref> However, the Korean government has never reviewed the support of masks to Japan, and expressed that it would only proceed with the formally disclosed request of the Japanese government for supply support such as facial mask, following the public opinion of the Korean people.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.koreatimes.co.kr/www/nation/2020/04/356_288762.html|date=29 April 2020|title=Korea-Japan ties getting worse in pandemic|website=The Korea Times|access-date=10 May 2020}}</ref> On the contrary, inside Japan, an editorial was published stating that the Korean government should donate medical supplies like face mask covertly and the Japanese government should accept it casually.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.segye.com/newsView/20200507519400|date=7 May 2020|title=日 칼럼 "한국이 일본에 익명으로 마스크 지원해줄 수는 없을까?"|language=ko|publisher=Segye Ilbo|access-date=10 May 2020}}</ref>

===China===
{{See|China–United States relations#COVID-19}}
The United States has criticised the [[Government of China|Chinese government]] for its handling of the pandemic, which began in the Chinese province of [[Hubei]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/united-states/2020/03/26/relations-between-china-and-america-are-infected-with-coronavirus|title=Relations between China and America are infected with coronavirus|work=The Economist|access-date=30 March 2020|issn=0013-0613}}</ref> In [[Brazil]], the Congressman [[Eduardo Bolsonaro]], son of President [[Jair Bolsonaro]], caused a diplomatic dispute with China when he retweeted a message saying: "The blame for the global coronavirus pandemic has a name and surname: the [[Communist Party of China|Chinese Communist party]]." Yang Wanming, China's top diplomat in Brazil, retweeted a message that said: "The Bolsonaro family is the great poison of this country."<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/19/coronavirus-bolsonaro-son-china-row|title=Bolsonaro's son enrages Beijing by blaming China for coronavirus crisis|date=19 March 2020|work=The Guardian}}</ref>

Some commentators believe the state [[propaganda in China]] is promoting a narrative that China's [[Authoritarianism|authoritarian system]] is uniquely capable of curbing the coronavirus and contrasts that with the chaotic response of the [[Liberal democracy|Western democracies]].<ref>{{cite news |title=China is winning the coronavirus propaganda war |url=https://www.politico.eu/article/coronavirus-china-winning-propaganda-war/ |work=Politico |date=18 March 2020}}</ref><ref name="Foreign Policy">{{cite news |title=China Is Fighting the Coronavirus Propaganda War to Win |url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/03/20/china-coronavirus-propaganda-war-journalists-press-freedom/ |work=Foreign Policy |date=20 March 2020}}</ref><ref name="The Straits Times">{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: China showers Europe with virus aid while sparring with Trump |url=https://www.straitstimes.com/world/europe/coronavirus-china-showers-europe-with-virus-aid-while-sparring-with-trump |work=The Straits Times |date=19 March 2020}}</ref> European Union foreign policy chief [[Josep Borrell]] said that "China is aggressively pushing the message that, unlike the US, it is a responsible and reliable partner."<ref name="bbc-borrell">{{cite news |title=Governments reject Chinese-made equipment |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-52092395 |work=BBC News |date=30 March 2020}}</ref>

The [[Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the People's Republic of China|Chinese Ministry of Foreign Affairs]] has claimed that the United States military is behind the virus.<ref name=":6">{{Cite web|url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-04-30/coronavirus-china-diplomatic-backlash/12198674|title=Coronavirus investigation call has made Australia a target, but we're not alone in feeling China's wrath – ABC News|date=29 April 2020|website=abc.net.au|language=en-AU|access-date=30 April 2020}}</ref> When [[Australia]] suggested an inquiry to better understand the origin of the pandemic and to undermine the [[World Health Organization]], the Chinese ambassador threatened with economic retaliation.<ref name=":6" /> The Chinese embassy to [[France]] has in turn claimed that French nursing homes were ""abandoning their posts overnight … and leaving their residents to die of hunger and disease".<ref name=":6" /> The Chinese government has also tried to directly influence statements of other governments in order to show the country in a more positive light, including in [[Germany]],<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-germany-china-idUSKCN2280JW|title=Germany says China sought to encourage positive COVID-19 comments|date=27 April 2020|work=Reuters|access-date=30 April 2020|language=en}}</ref> and [[Wisconsin]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://wisconsinexaminer.com/2020/04/10/chinese-government-asks-wisconsin-senate-for-a-commendation/|title=Chinese government asks Wisconsin Senate for a commendation|last=Conklin|first=Melanie|date=10 April 2020|website=Wisconsin Examiner|language=en-US|access-date=30 April 2020}}</ref>

[[China]] has sent aid to 82 countries, the [[World Health Organization]], and the [[African Union]], which is considered by some western media as to "counter its negative image in the early stage of the pandemic".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-03-25/china-coronavirus-aid-seeks-to-shift-narrative-from-cover-up/12072296|title='A white jade for friendship': China's push to save countries from COVID-19|last1=Walsh|first1=Michael|last2=Walden|first2=Max|date=25 March 2020|website=ABC News|language=en-AU|access-date=30 March 2020|last3=Zhao|first3=Iris}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Faults in China-supplied coronavirus equipment reported in Europe |url=https://www.irishtimes.com/news/world/europe/faults-in-china-supplied-coronavirus-equipment-reported-in-europe-1.4215628 |work=The Irish Times |date=30 March 2020}}</ref><ref name="intercept-coronavirus"/> According to Yangyang Cheng, a postdoctoral research associate at [[Cornell University]], "The Chinese government has been trying to project Chinese state power beyond its borders and establish China as a global leader, not dissimilar to what the U.S. government has been doing for the better part of a century, and the distribution of medical aid is part of this mission."<ref name="intercept-coronavirus">{{cite news |title=As the U.S. Blames China for the Coronavirus Pandemic, the Rest of the World Asks China for Help |url=https://theintercept.com/2020/03/18/coronavirus-china-world-power/ |work=The Intercept |date=18 March 2020}}</ref> Borrell warned that there is "a geo-political component including a struggle for influence through spinning and the 'politics of generosity'."<ref name="bbc-borrell"/>

Trade in medical supplies between the United States and China has also become politically complicated. Exports of face masks and other medical equipment to China from the United States (and many other countries) spiked in February, according to statistics from [[Trade Data Monitor]], prompting criticism from the ''[[Washington Post]]'' that the United States government failed to anticipate the domestic needs for that equipment.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/health/us-sent-millions-of-face-masks-to-china-early-this-year-ignoring-pandemic-warning-signs/2020/04/18/aaccf54a-7ff5-11ea-8013-1b6da0e4a2b7_story.html |title=U.S. sent millions of face masks to China early this year, ignoring pandemic warning signs |last1=Eilperin |first1=Juliet |last2=Stein |first2=Jeff |last3=Butler |first3=Desmond |last4=Hamburger |first4=Tom |work=Washington Post |date=April 18, 2020 |access-date=June 24, 2020 }}</ref> Similarly, ''[[The Wall Street Journal]]'', citing [[Trade Data Monitor]] to show that China is the leading source of many key medical supplies, raised concerns that [[China–United States trade war|US tariffs on imports from China]] threaten imports of medical supplies into the United States.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/u-s-tariffs-hamper-imports-of-sanitizer-disinfectants-11586683800 |title=U.S. Tariffs Hamper Imports of Sanitizer, Disinfectants, Some Companies Say |last1=Ferek |first1=Katy Stech |last2=Zumbrun |first2=Josh |work=The Wall Street Journal |date=April 12, 2020 |access-date=June 24, 2020 }}</ref>

===United States===

In early March, European Union leaders condemned the United States' decision to restrict travel from Europe to the United States.<ref>{{cite news |title=EU condemns Trump travel ban from Europe as virus spreads |url=https://apnews.com/4552fd280d06cf83c63e4cc9b08fe5ce |work=[[Associated Press]] |date=12 March 2020}}</ref>

The U.S. has come under scrutiny by officials from other countries for allegedly hijacking shipments of crucial supplies meant for other countries.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Toosi |first1=Nahal |title='Lord of the Flies: PPE Edition': U.S. cast as culprit in global scrum over coronavirus supplies |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2020/04/03/ppe-world-supplies-coronavirus-163955 |website=POLITICO |date=3 April 2020}}</ref><ref name=gua-ushi>{{cite web |last1=Jerusalem |first1=Kim Willsher Oliver Holmes in |last2=Istanbul |first2=Bethan McKernan in |last3=Palermo |first3=Lorenzo Tondo in |title=US hijacking mask shipments in rush for coronavirus protection |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/02/global-battle-coronavirus-equipment-masks-tests |website=The Guardian |date=3 April 2020}}</ref>

[[Jean Rottner]], the [[List of current presidents of the regional councils of France and the Corsican Assembly|President]] of France's [[Regional council of Grand Est]], accused the United States of disrupting face mask deliveries by buying at the last minute.<ref>{{Cite news |url=http://www.rfi.fr/en/europe/20200402-china-coronavirus-face-mask-france-stolen-us |title=Face masks from China intended for France 'hijacked' by US at the last minute |date=2 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403204445/http://www.rfi.fr/en/europe/20200402-china-coronavirus-face-mask-france-stolen-us |archive-date=3 April 2020}}</ref> French officials stated that Americans came to the airport tarmac and offered several times the French payment as the shipment was prepared for departure to France.<ref name=gua-ushi/> Justin Trudeau, the Prime Minister of Canada, asked [[Bill Blair (politician)|Bill Blair]], the [[Minister of Public Safety and Emergency Preparedness|Public Safety Minister]], and [[Marc Garneau]], the [[Minister of Transport (Canada)|Transportation Minister]], to investigate allegations that medical supplies originally intended for Canada were diverted to the United States.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://thehill.com/policy/international/americas/490969-trudeau-worried-supplies-meant-for-canada-have-been-diverted-to |title=Trudeau worried supplies meant for Canada have been diverted to US |date=3 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403204813/https://thehill.com/policy/international/americas/490969-trudeau-worried-supplies-meant-for-canada-have-been-diverted-to |archive-date=3 April 2020}}</ref> German politician [[Andreas Geisel]] accused the United States of committing "modern piracy" after reports that 200,000 N95 masks meant for German police were diverted during an en-route transfer between airplanes in Thailand to the United States,<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/03/mask-wars-coronavirus-outbidding-demand |title=US accused of 'modern piracy' after diversion of masks meant for Europe |date=3 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403205041/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/03/mask-wars-coronavirus-outbidding-demand |archive-date=3 April 2020}}</ref> but later changed his statement after he clarified that the mask orders were made through a German firm, not a U.S. firm as earlier stated, and the supply chain issues were under review.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2020/04/04/coronavirus-latest-news/#link-GQ4VHJ7T2ZGQPD3VUWO5W6QZRU |title=Berlin backtracks after accusing U.S. of 'piracy' when 200,000 masks went missing |date=5 April 2020}}</ref>

Due to shortages in coronavirus tests Maryland Governor [[Larry Hogan]] had his wife [[Yumi Hogan]], who was born in South Korea, to speak with the South Korean ambassador and afterwards multiple South Korea companies stated that they would send tests to Maryland.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.msn.com/en-us/news/politics/marylands-governor-a-republican-is-willing-to-spar-with-trump-for-supplies/ar-BB127y8P?li=BBnb7Kz |title=Maryland's Governor, a Republican, Is Willing to Spar With Trump for Supplies |date=3 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406000712/https://www.msn.com/en-us/news/politics/marylands-governor-a-republican-is-willing-to-spar-with-trump-for-supplies/ar-BB127y8P?li=BBnb7Kz |archive-date=6 April 2020}}</ref>

On 2 April 2020, President Trump invoked the [[Defense Production Act of 1950]] to halt exports of masks produced by [[3M]] to Canada and Latin America.<ref name=fm-twu/> Canadian Prime Minister Justin Trudeau said that it would be a mistake for both their countries to limit trade of essential goods or services, including medical supplies and professionals, and remarked that this moves in both directions.<ref name=fm-twu>{{cite web |last1=Forrest |first1=Maura |title=Trudeau warns U.S. against denying exports of medical supplies to Canada |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2020/04/03/3m-warns-of-white-house-order-to-stop-exporting-masks-to-canada-163060 |website=POLITICO |date=3 April 2020}}</ref> The Canadian government has turned to China and other places for crucial medical supplies, while they seek a constructive discussion about the issue with the Trump administration.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Blatchford |first1=Andy |title=Trump's moves to hold medical supplies tip Trudeau to China |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2020/04/04/coronavirus-canada-trudeau-china-164969 |website=POLITICO |date=4 April 2020}}</ref>

In October 2020, the editors of the [[New England Journal of Medicine]] unanimously published an unprecedented editorial calling for the current American leadership to be voted out in the November election, writing "countries were forced to make hard choices about how to respond. Here in the United States, our leaders have failed that test. They have taken a crisis and turned it into a tragedy."<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/10/07/health/nejm-editorial-political-leadership-bn/index.html|title=Prestigious medical journal calls for US leadership to be voted out over Covid-19 failure|first=Jacqueline Howard|last=CNN|website=CNN}}</ref>

In November 2020, Donald Trump lost his bid for reelection to former Vice President [[Joe Biden]], in an election dominated by COVID-19's impact on all aspects of American life. <ref>{{cite web |last1=Bennett AND |first1=Brain |last2=Bernenson |first2=Tessa |title=How Donald Trump Lost The Election |url=https://time.com/5907973/donald-trump-loses-2020-election/ |website=time.com |access-date=17 November 2020 |date=7 November 2020}}</ref>

=== World Health Organization ===
The head of the [[World Health Organization]], [[Tedros Adhanom]], claimed that he had been "severely discriminated against", and had received death threats and racist insults, claiming that "This attack came from [[Taiwan]]".<ref name=":3">{{cite web|url=https://www.smh.com.au/world/asia/taiwan-protests-who-leader-s-accusations-of-taipei-led-racist-campaign-20200409-p54ilz.html|title=Taiwan protests WHO leader's accusations of Taipei-led racist campaign|date=9 April 2020|website=The Sydney Morning Herald|language=en|access-date=10 April 2020}}</ref> The foreign ministry of Taiwan protested this accusation, indicating "strong dissatisfaction and a high degree of regret" and that the Taiwanese people "condemn all forms of discrimination and injustice".<ref name=":3" />

On 7 April 2020, United States President [[Donald Trump]] threatened to cut funding to the WHO.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Shear|first=Michael D.|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/07/us/politics/coronavirus-trump-who.html|title=Trump Attacks W.H.O. Over Criticisms of U.S. Approach to Coronavirus|date=7 April 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=14 April 2020|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref> On 7 July 2020, the [[Trump administration]] announced that the United States would formally withdraw from the WHO.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Hinshaw|first1=Drew|last2=Armour|first2=Stephanie|url= https://www.wsj.com/articles/white-house-says-u-s-has-pulled-out-of-the-world-health-organization-11594150928|title= Trump Moves to Pull U.S. Out of World Health Organization in Midst of Covid-19 Pandemic|date=7 July 2020|work=The Wall Street Journal|access-date=7 July 2020|language=en-US}}</ref>

=== Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development ===
The [[OECD]] Secretary-General [[José Ángel Gurría|Angel Gurría]] wrote that  “This is the third and greatest economic, financial and social shock of the 21st century, and it demands a modern, global effort akin to the last century’s [[Marshall Plan]] and [[New Deal]] – combined.<ref>{{Cite web|title=OECD Secretary-General: coronavirus "war" demands joint action – OECD|url=http://www.oecd.org/newsroom/oecd-secretary-general-coronavirus-war-demands-joint-action.htm|website=oecd.org|access-date=2020-05-07}}</ref>” COVID-19  has  a  strong  regional and global  impact,  calling  for  differentiated  governance and  policy responses from local to international levels. A coordinated response by all  levels  of  government  can  minimize  crisis-management failures.<ref>{{Cite web|title=OECD|url=https://read.oecd-ilibrary.org/view/?ref=128_128287-5agkkojaaa&title=The-territorial-impact-of-covid-19-managing-the-crisis-across-levels-of-government|website=read.oecd-ilibrary.org|access-date=7 May 2020}}</ref>

===International Court of Justice===
The [[International Court of Justice]] (ICJ) planned to discuss Guyana and Venezuela border dispute over [[Guayana Esequiba]] in March 2020. The ICJ also delayed public hearings over [[Maritime border dispute between Kenya and Somalia|maritime border disputes between Somalia and Kenya]] until March 2021.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Latest developments {{!}} Maritime Delimitation in the Indian Ocean (Somalia v. Kenya) {{!}} International Court of Justice|url=https://www.icj-cij.org/en/case/161|access-date=2020-12-01|website=www.icj-cij.org}}</ref> Both hearings were postponed due to the pandemic.<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-03-17|title=Guyana: Hearing of border controversy matter postponed|url=https://www.stlucianewsonline.com/guyana-hearing-of-border-controversy-matter-postponed/|access-date=2020-06-05|website=St. Lucia News Online|language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|date=22 May 2020|title=Maritime Delimitation in the Indian Ocean (Somalia v. Kenya) Public hearings postponed until March 2021|work=International Court of Justice|url=https://www.icj-cij.org/public/files/case-related/161/161-20200522-PRE-01-00-EN.pdf|access-date=1 December 2020}}</ref>

=== Global ceasefire ===
{{Main|Global ceasefire}}
The coronavirus pandemic appears to have worsened conflict dynamics;<ref>{{Cite journal|last=Mustasilta|first=Katariina|date=2020|title=FROM BAD TO WORSE?: The impact(s) of Covid-19 on conflict dynamics|url=http://www.jstor.org/stable/resrep25022|periodical=Conflict Series|publisher=European Union Institute for Security Studies (EUISS)|access-date=1 August 2020}}</ref> it has also led to a United Nations Security Council resolution demanding a global ceasefire. On March 23, 2020, United Nations Secretary-General [[António Guterres]] issued an appeal for a global ceasefire as part of the United Nations' response to the COVID-19 coronavirus pandemic.<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-03-23|title=Transcript of the Secretary-General's virtual press encounter on the appeal for global ceasefire|url=https://www.un.org/sg/en/content/sg/press-encounter/2020-03-23/transcript-of-the-secretary-generals-virtual-press-encounter-the-appeal-for-global-ceasefire|access-date=2020-08-01|website=United Nations Secretary-General|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-03-23|title=COVID-19: UN chief calls for global ceasefire to focus on 'the true fight of our lives'|url=https://news.un.org/en/story/2020/03/1059972|access-date=2020-08-01|website=UN News|language=en}}</ref> On 24 June 2020, 170 UN Member States and Observers signed a non-binding statement in support of the appeal,<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-06-24|title=170 signatories endorse UN ceasefire appeal during COVID crisis|url=https://news.un.org/en/story/2020/06/1066982|access-date=2020-08-01|website=UN News|language=en}}</ref> rising to 172 on 25 June 2020. On 1 July 2020, the UN Security Council passed resolution [[United Nations Security Council Resolution 2532|S/RES/2532 (2020)]], demanding a "general and immediate cessation of hostilities in all situations on its agenda," expressing support for "the efforts undertaken by the Secretary-General and his Special Representatives and Special Envoys in that respect," calling for "all parties to armed conflicts to engage immediately in a durable humanitarian pause" of at least 90 consecutive days, and calling for greater international cooperation to address the pandemic.

==Impact on national politics==
===Belgium===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Belgium}}
On 17 March 2020, [[Sophie Wilmès]] was sworn in as [[Prime Minister of Belgium]]. Seven opposition parties pledged to support the [[Minority government|minority]] [[Wilmès II Government]], in its [[Wilmès I Government|previous composition]], with [[plenary power]] to handle the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Belgium|coronavirus pandemic in Belgium]].<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.hln.be/nieuws/binnenland/sophie-wilmes-legt-eed-af-als-premier~adca7ad7/|title=Sophie Wilmès legt eed af als premier|publisher=Het Laatste Nieuws|date=17 March 2020|language=nl}}</ref>

===Brazil===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Brazil}}

President [[Jair Bolsonaro]] has been criticized for his handling of the crisis.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://slate.com/news-and-politics/2020/03/coronavirus-bolsonaro-brazil-panelaco.html|title=Could the Coronavirus Topple Jair Bolsonaro?|last=Dias|first=Isabela|date=20 March 2020|website=Slate Magazine|language=en|access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref> He has referred to the pandemic as a "fantasy".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://g1.globo.com/politica/noticia/2020/03/10/bolsonaro-diz-que-questao-do-coronavirus-e-muito-mais-fantasia.ghtml|title=Bolsonaro diz que 'pequena crise' do coronavírus é 'mais fantasia' e não 'isso tudo' que mídia propaga|website=G1|language=pt-br|access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref> According to one poll, 64% of Brazilians reject the way Bolsonaro has handled the pandemic, while 44.8% support his [[impeachment]], an all-time high.<ref>[https://brasil.elpais.com/brasil/2020-03-19/gestao-de-bolsonaro-do-coronavirus-e-reprovada-por-64-e-45-se-dizem-a-favor-de-impeachment.html "Gestão de Bolsonaro do coronavírus é reprovada por 64%, e 45% se dizem a favor de impeachment"]. ''El País''. 19 March 2020.</ref> During a speech by the president about the pandemic, many Brazilians participated in a ''[[Cacerolazo|panelaço]]'' protesting the president by banging pots and pans on balconies.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-51955679|title=Brazil coronavirus protesters urge 'Bolsonaro out'|date=19 March 2020|work=BBC News|access-date=22 March 2020|language=en-GB}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|first=Tom |last=Phillips |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/20/jair-bolsonaro-dictatorship-rally-protest-brazil-president-denounced |title=Brazilian president Jair Bolsonaro denounced for joining pro-dictatorship rally &#124; World news |newspaper=The Guardian |access-date=27 April 2020}}</ref>

=== Canada ===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Canada}}
On 13 March 2020, the [[Parliament of Canada]] voted to suspend activity in both houses until 20 April for the [[House of Commons of Canada|House of Commons]] and 21 April for the [[Senate of Canada|Senate]].<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cp24.com/news/parliament-suspends-for-five-weeks-over-covid-19-concerns-1.4851501 |title=Parliament suspends for five weeks over COVID-19 concerns |date=13 March 2020 |work=CP 24 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200315013940/https://www.cp24.com/news/parliament-suspends-for-five-weeks-over-covid-19-concerns-1.4851501 |archive-date=15 March 2020}}</ref>  The House of Commons' Health and Finance committees were granted the ability to hold weekly virtual meetings during the pandemic.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Aiello |first=Rachel |url=https://www.ctvnews.ca/health/coronavirus/house-health-committee-holding-first-virtual-briefing-on-covid-19-efforts-1.4875766 |title=House health committee holding first virtual briefing on COVID-19 efforts |date=31 March 2020 |work=[[CTV News]] |access-date=31 March 2020}}</ref>

The leadership contests of the [[2020 Conservative Party of Canada leadership election|Conservative Party of Canada]], [[2020 Green Party of British Columbia leadership election|Green Party of British Columbia]], [[2020 Quebec Liberal Party leadership election|Quebec Liberal Party]] and [[2020 Parti Québécois leadership election|Parti Québécois]] were postponed.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Canadian Press|first=The|url=https://www.nationalnewswatch.com/2020/03/26/canadian-press-newsalert-conservatives-suspend-partys-leadership-race/|title=Conservatives suspend party's leadership race in face of COVID-19 crisis|date=26 March 2020|work=National Newswatch|access-date=26 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Rothbauer |first=Kevin |title=B.C. Greens suspend leadership race due to COVID-19 |url=https://www.albernivalleynews.com/news/b-c-greens-suspend-leadership-race-due-to-covid-19 |access-date=27 March 2020 |work=Alberni Valley News |date=27 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Quebec Liberal Party suspends its leadership contest due to COVID-19 pandemic |url=https://montreal.ctvnews.ca/quebec-liberal-party-suspends-its-leadership-contest-due-to-covid-19-pandemic-1.4861644 |access-date=29 March 2020 |work=CTV News |agency=Canadian Press |date=20 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=COVID-19: Le Parti Québécois met sa course à la direction en pause |url=https://www.journaldequebec.com/2020/03/28/covid-19-le-parti-quebecois-met-sa-course-a-la-direction-en-pause |access-date=28 March 2020 |work=Le journal de Montreal |date=29 March 2020}}</ref>

===China===
{{see also|COVID-19 pandemic in mainland China}}
Multiple provincial-level administrators of the [[Communist Party of China]] (CPC) were dismissed over their handling of the quarantine efforts in central China. Some experts believe this is likely in a move to protect Communist Party general secretary [[Xi Jinping]] from people's anger over the coronavirus outbreak.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.businessinsider.com/analysis-china-hubei-officials-sacked-xi-jinping-protected-2020-2 |title=China sacked a brace of top officials in Hubei province, likely in a move to protect Xi Jinping from people's anger over the coronavirus outbreak |last=Bostock |first=Bill |work=Business Insider |access-date=26 February 2020 |date=13 February 2020}}</ref> [[Taiwan]] has also voiced concern over being included in any travel ban involving the People's Republic of China due to the "[[one-China policy]]" and [[Political status of Taiwan|Chinese claims]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://medicalxpress.com/news/2020-02-taiwan-china-virus.html |title=Taiwan hits out at China virus travel bans |work=medicalxpress.com |access-date=26 February 2020}}</ref> A few countries have been using the epidemic to build [[Foreign relations of China|political bridges]] with [[Government of China|Beijing]], raising accusations that these countries, which include [[Cambodia]] among others, were putting politics before health.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/02/21/hun-sen-is-more-worried-about-beijing-than-the-coronavirus/ |title=Hun Sen Is More Worried About Beijing Than the Coronavirus |last=Wilson |first=Audrey |work=[[Foreign Policy]] |access-date=3 March 2020}}</ref> Existing [[China–United States trade war|tensions]] between the United States and China may have delayed a coordinated effort to combat the outbreak in Wuhan.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.atlanticcouncil.org/event/peering-around-the-corner-the-geopolitics-of-the-coronavirus/ |title=Peering around the corner: The geopolitics of the coronavirus |work=[[Atlantic Council]] |access-date=3 March 2020}}</ref>

Outlets such as ''[[Politico]]'', ''[[Foreign Policy]]'', and [[Bloomberg News|Bloomberg]] have reported that efforts from China to send aid to other countries and claim without evidence that the virus originated in the United States are a [[Propaganda in China|propaganda]] push for global influence while deflecting blame for its handling of the outbreak.<ref name="politico-corona">{{cite news|url=https://www.politico.eu/article/coronavirus-china-winning-propaganda-war/|title=China is winning the coronavirus propaganda war|date=18 March 2020|work=Politico}}</ref><ref name="Foreign Policy"/><ref name="The Straits Times"/>

==== Hong Kong ====
{{see also|COVID-19 pandemic in Hong Kong|Hong Kong national security law}}
[[2019–20 Hong Kong protests|Protests in Hong Kong]] strengthened due to fears of immigration from mainland China.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.channelnewsasia.com/news/asia/wuhan-virus-hong-kong-protests-china-12348984 |title=Hong Kong protesters torch planned Wuhan virus quarantine building |publisher=[[Channel NewsAsia]] |access-date=26 February 2020}}</ref> In order to crackdown Hong Kong protests, China drift a new Hong Kong national security law which have drawn international concerns.

===Hungary===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Hungary}}

The [[National Assembly (Hungary)|Hungarian Parliament]] gave the government [[plenary power]] which authorizes it to override acts and to [[rule by decree]] to the extent that is "necessary and proportional" in order to ''"''prevent, manage, and eradicate the epidemic and to avoid and mitigate its effects".<ref name=":2">{{cite web|url=https://index.hu/english/2020/03/30/hungary_coronavirus_act_parliament_viktor_orban_fidesz_sweeping_powers_indefinite_term/|title=Hungarian Coronavirus Act passes, granting Viktor Orbán unprecedented emergency powers|last=Zoltán|first=Kovács|date=30 March 2020|website=index.hu|language=en|access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref> The law prescribes that the government is to report back to the parliament, or if it's unable to convene, to its speaker and the leaders of the parliamentary groups, regularly about the measures it has taken.<ref name=":2" /> The law also suspends [[by-elections]] and referendums for the duration of the emergency.<ref>{{cite web|last=Liu |first=Abraham |url=https://www.politico.eu/article/hungary-viktor-orban-rule-by-decree/ |title=Hungary's Viktor Orbán wins vote to rule by decree |work=Politico |access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref><ref name=":2" /> The [[Constitutional Court of Hungary]] is authorized to hold sessions via electronic communications networks.<ref name=":2" /> The act also criminalizes "statements known to be false or statements distorting true facts" with 1 to 5 years imprisonment "if done in a manner capable of hindering or derailing the effectiveness of the response effort".<ref name=":2" /> The opposition had demanded a 90-day [[Sunset provision|sunset clause]] to the emergency powers in return for its support, but had its amendments voted down and therefore opposed the act.<ref name=":2" />

[[Human Rights Watch]] described the legislation, as an authoritarian takeover, due to the rule of decree without parliamentary or judicial scrutiny and for criminal penalties for the publishing of "false" or "distorted" facts, and gave support to the European Commission using [[Article 7 of the Treaty on European Union|Article 7]] against Hungary. Criticism and concern regarding the decree stemmed from existing [[democratic backsliding|backsliding]] of Hungarian democracy under the premiership of [[Viktor Orbán]] and his majority-ruling [[Fidesz]] party since Orbán began his second tenure as [[Prime Minister of Hungary|Prime Minister]] in 2010. Orbán has been accused by opposition leaders and other critics of his premiership of shifting Hungary towards [[authoritarianism]] by centralizing legislative and executive power through [[Constitution of Hungary#2011 Constitution|Constitutional reforms]] passed in 2011 and 2013, curbing civil liberties, restricting freedom of speech to the extent that some independent media outlets once critical of his rule have since been acquired by allies of Orbán, and weakening other institutional [[separation of powers|checks on Orbán's power]] including the Constitutional Court and judiciary. Critics of the Orbán/Fidesz government expressed concern that the emergency plenary powers may not be rescinded once the pandemic subsides, and could be abused to dubiously prosecute independent journalists critical of his coronavirus response or his governance more broadly, and curtail other freedoms of speech and expression. Some observers suggest that any significant misuse of or, once the crisis subsides, failure to rescind the plenary powers by Orbán government could place Hungary at great risk of becoming the European Union's first [[dictatorship]], in violation of E.U. regulations. (Turkey's proposed E.U. membership has been held up and advocates have urged the Union to terminate the proposal, because of human rights violations under [[President of Turkey|President]] [[Recep Tayyip Erdogan]]'s government.)<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2020/04/01/hungarys-authoritarian-takeover-puts-european-union-risk#|title=Hungary's Authoritarian Takeover Puts European Union at Risk|date=1 April 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404030627/https://www.hrw.org/news/2020/04/01/hungarys-authoritarian-takeover-puts-european-union-risk|archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/victor-orbans-power-grab-in-hungry-heightens-fears-of-dictatorship-in-eu-83h3g9lpm|title=Victor Orban's power grab in Hungary heightens fears of dictatorship in EU|date=2 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://balkaninsight.com/2020/03/31/hungary-no-longer-a-democracy-after-coronavirus-law/|title=HUNGARY 'NO LONGER A DEMOCRACY' AFTER CORONAVIRUS LAW|date=31 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.rfi.fr/en/europe/20200401-how-coronavirus-legislation-could-create-the-eu-s-first-dictatorship|title=How coronavirus legislation could create the EU's first dictatorship|date=1 April 2020}}</ref> A petition against the legislation was signed by over 100,000 people. [[Péter Jakab]], the president of the opposition party [[Jobbik]], said that the bill put Hungarian democracy in quarantine. Nézőpont, a pro-government polling agency, conducted a poll that showed that 90% of Hungarians supported extending emergency measures and 72% supported strengthening the criminal code.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-52095500 |title=Coronavirus: Hungary government gets sweeping powers |date=30 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200330144929/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-52095500 |archive-date=30 March 2020}}</ref>

In response to news reports about the state of emergency being a danger to democracy, Foreign Minister [[Péter Szijjártó]] called them "fake news and lies" and stated that the measures that Hungary had adopted were not unprecedented in Europe. He specifically stated that there were unfounded reports in mainstream media about the government's unlimited authorization and the closing down of the Parliament.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://edition.cnn.com/videos/tv/2020/04/09/peter-szijjarto-hungary-foreign-minister-amanpour-viktor-orban-democracy.cnn|title=Szijjártó: "Fake news and lies" spread on Hungary|date=10 April 2020}}</ref>

European Commission vice-president Věra Jourová after a thorough examination confirmed that Hungary's recently adopted emergency measures do not break any EU rules yet.<ref>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TDp24_MCC-8</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://euobserver.com/tickers/148218|title=[Ticker] Jourova: Hungary decree law does not break EU rules yet|website=EUobserver}}</ref>

===Iran===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Iran}}
The [[Government of the Islamic Republic of Iran]] has been heavily affected by the virus.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/middle_east/coronavirus-pummels-iran-leadership-as-data-show-spread-is-far-worse-than-reported/2020/03/04/7b1196ae-5c9f-11ea-ac50-18701e14e06d_story.html |title=Coronavirus pummels Iran leadership as data show spread is far worse than reported |last=Cunningham |first=Erin |work=[[The Washington Post]] |access-date=15 March 2020}}</ref> The spread of the virus has raised questions about the future survival of the regime.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.nationalreview.com/2020/03/will-irans-regime-survive-coronavirus/ |title=Will Iran's Regime Survive Coronavirus? |date=12 March 2020 |work=[[National Review]] |access-date=15 March 2020}}</ref> Iran's President [[Hassan Rouhani]] wrote a public letter to world leaders asking for help, saying that his country doesn't have access to international markets due to the [[United States sanctions against Iran]].<ref>{{cite news |title=U.S. sanctions 'severely hamper' Iran coronavirus fight, Rouhani says |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-iran/us-sanctions-severely-hamper-iran-coronavirus-fight-rouhani-idUSKBN2110HL |work=Reuters |date=14 March 2020}}</ref> On 3 March 2020, [[Islamic Consultative Assembly|Iranian Parliament]] was shut down after having 23 of the 290 members of parliament reported to have had tested positive for the virus.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.businessinsider.com/8-percent-iran-parliament-has-coronavirus-it-released-54000-prisoners-2020-3|title=8% of Iran's parliament has the coronavirus, and it released 54,000 prisoners as the country descends into chaos|last=Haltiwanger|first=John|name-list-style=vanc|website=Business Insider|access-date=4 March 2020|date=3 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200304001925/https://www.businessinsider.com/8-percent-iran-parliament-has-coronavirus-it-released-54000-prisoners-2020-3|archive-date=4 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

===Israel===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Israel}}

After facing political deadlock since the [[April 2019 Israeli legislative election|legislative election]] held on 9 April 2019, Israel held two more elections in 2020, which ended with Netanyahu forming the [[Thirty-fifth government of Israel]].

On 28 March 2020, the [[United Nations]] Special Coordinator for the [[Middle East]] Peace Process, [[Nickolay Mladenov]] praised the Israel and [[Palestinian National Authority|Palestinian authorities]] for their coordination in tackling the [[Coronavirus disease 2019|COVID-19]] pandemic. Mladenov appreciated the response strategy, especially for focusing on [[Gaza Strip|Gaza]], as the region faces a relatively substantial risk of the disease spreading. Since the start of the [[COVID-19 pandemic|novel coronavirus crisis]], Israel permitted the entry of significant medical and aid supplies inside Gaza.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.un.org/en/story/2020/03/1060572|title=COVID-19: UN envoy hails strong Israel-Palestine cooperation|access-date=28 March 2020|website=UN News}}</ref>

===Kosovo===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Kosovo}}

On 18 March, Interior Minister Agim Veliu was sacked due to his support for declaring a state of emergency to handle the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Kosovo|coronavirus pandemic]] which would have given power to the Kosovo Security Council chaired by [[Hashim Thaçi]]. The [[Democratic League of Kosovo]], the junior partner leader of the coalition, filed a no-confidence vote motion in retaliation for the sacking and on 25 March eighty two members of the [[Assembly of the Republic of Kosovo|Kosovo Assembly]] voted in favor of the motion.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://balkaninsight.com/2020/03/19/kosovos-crisis-hit-govt-threatened-with-no-confidence-vote/ |title=Kosovo's Crisis-Hit Govt Threatened with No-Confidence Vote |date=19 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326004128/https://balkaninsight.com/2020/03/19/kosovos-crisis-hit-govt-threatened-with-no-confidence-vote/ |archive-date=26 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.trtworld.com/europe/kosovo-govt-toppled-by-no-confidence-vote-amid-coronavirus-34859 |title=Kosovo govt toppled by no-confidence vote amid coronavirus |date=25 March 2020 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326004241/https://www.trtworld.com/europe/kosovo-govt-toppled-by-no-confidence-vote-amid-coronavirus-34859 |archive-date=26 March 2020 |access-date=26 March 2020 }}</ref>

===Slovenia===

On its 1st Session on 13 March 2020, immediately following its confirmation, the [[13th Government of Slovenia|13th Government]] set up an informal Crisis Management Staff (CMS) of the Republic of Slovenia in order to contain and manage the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Slovenia|COVID-19 epidemic]]. Head of the Staff was Prime Minister [[Janez Janša]] and its secretary was former [[Slovenian Intelligence and Security Agency|SOVA]] director [[Andrej Rupnik]]. CMS was composed of all government members (prime minister and ministers) and other experts and civil servants in an advisory capacity.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.gov.si/novice/2020-03-14-1-redna-seja-vlade-republike-slovenije/|title=1. redna seja Vlade Republike Slovenije {{!}} GOV.SI|website=Portal GOV.SI|language=sl|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> Head of the Health Group was [[Bojana Beovič]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.gov.si/novice/2020-03-14-spremenjeno-diagnosticiranje-za-realnejse-nacrtovanje-ukrepov-za-obvladovanje-epidemije/|title=Spremenjeno diagnosticiranje za realnejše načrtovanje ukrepov za obvladovanje epidemije {{!}} GOV.SI|website=Portal GOV.SI|language=sl|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> [[Jelko Kacin]], former minister and ambassador to [[NATO]], was the official spokesman of the Staff, he had a similar role during the [[Ten-Day War|1991 Slovenian war of independence]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.24ur.com/novice/slovenija/na-kriznem-stabu-o-morebitnih-novih-ukrepih-vec-znanih-obrazov-tudi-jelko-kacin.html|title=Govorec kriznega štaba Kacin: V nedeljo sestanek direktorjev bolnišnic|website=24ur.com|language=sl|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref>

Crisis Management Staff was abolished on 24 March 2020 after the political transition was completed, its functions were transferred on the responsible ministries. Health Experts Group was transferred under the Ministry of Health. Kacin became the official government spokesperson on the topic.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.gov.si/novice/2020-03-24-6-redna-seja-vlade-republike-slovenije/|title=6. redna seja Vlade Republike Slovenije {{!}} GOV.SI|website=Portal GOV.SI|language=sl|access-date=24 March 2020}}</ref>

Government never proposed the declaration of emergency to the National Assembly, which would suspend the Assembly's powers and transfer them to the President of the Republic [[Borut Pahor]] to rule by decrees with the force of law, which are still subject to the National Assembly's approval once it gains its powers back. The provision is only applicable if the National Assembly is unable to meet in the session.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.us-rs.si/en/about-the-court/legal-basis/constitution/|title=Constitution of the Republic of Slovenia|date=11 April 2020|website=Constitutional Court of the Republic of Slovenia}}</ref> Assembly however passed a Rules of Procedure Amendment to enable itself a "long-distance" session using technology.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rtvslo.si/slovenija/poslanci-podprli-spremembe-referendumskega-zakona-naklonjeni-tudi-sejam-na-daljavo/519755|title=Poslanci podprli spremembe referendumskega zakona, naklonjeni tudi sejam na daljavo|website=RTVSLO.si|language=sl|access-date=11 April 2020}}</ref>

===South Korea===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in South Korea}}

Diplomatic [[Japan–South Korea relations|relations between Japan and South Korea]] worsened, as South Korea criticized Japan's "ambiguous and passive quarantine efforts", after Japan announced anybody coming from South Korea will be placed in two weeks’ quarantine at government-designated sites.<ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus quarantine plans ignite row between South Korea and Japan |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/06/coronavirus-quarantine-plans-ignite-row-between-south-korea-and-japan |work=The Guardian |date=6 March 2020 |access-date=15 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200308134434/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/06/coronavirus-quarantine-plans-ignite-row-between-south-korea-and-japan |archive-date=8 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

Following the outbreak of the virus in South Korea over 1,450,000 people signed a petition supporting the impeachment of President [[Moon Jae-in]] due to him sending masks and medical supplies to China to aid them in their response to the virus outbreak.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/03/09/moon-jae-in-china-coronavirus-impeachment-south-korea-president/ |title=South Korea's President Tried to Help China Contain the Coronavirus. Now People Want Him Impeached. |date=9 March 2020 |work=[[Foreign Policy]] |access-date=15 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200312080924/https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/03/09/moon-jae-in-china-coronavirus-impeachment-south-korea-president/ |archive-date=12 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> Moon administration's continuing handling of the crisis has however been noted in other sectors of the Korean society and internationally. An opinion poll by Gallup Korea in March 2020 showed Moon's approval rating rising by 5% to 49%.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.gallup.co.kr/dir/GallupKoreaDaily/GallupKoreaDailyOpinion_392(20200313).pdf|title=데일리 오피니언 제392호(2020년 3월 2주) – 총선 기대, 차기 정치 지도자, 코로나19, 마스크 관련 인식|work=한국갤럽|date=13 March 2020}}</ref>

In April 2020, Moon's [[Democratic Party of Korea|Democratic Party]] won a record landslide in the country's [[Legislative elections in South Korea|legislative election]] for [[List of members of the National Assembly (South Korea), 2020–2024|21st session until 2024]].<ref>{{cite web| title=Moon's Democrats win South Korea general election in landslide| date= 16 April 2020| work=Nikkei Asian Review| url=https://asia.nikkei.com/Spotlight/South-Korea-election/Moon-s-Democrats-win-South-Korea-general-election-in-landslide| access-date=10 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.upi.com/Top_News/World-News/2020/04/16/Ruling-party-sweeps-to-landslide-victory-in-South-Korean-elections/7011587025642/| work= United Press Agency |title= Ruling party sweeps to landslide victory in South Korean elections| date= 16 April 2020| access-date= 10 May 2020}}</ref>

===Spain===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Spain}}

On 12 March 2020, the [[Congress of Deputies]] voted to suspend activity for a week after multiple members had tested positive for the virus.<ref name="vox infections">{{Cite news |url=https://english.elpais.com/society/2020-03-13/more-spanish-politicians-confirm-they-have-been-infected-with-the-coronavirus.html |title=More Spanish politicians confirm they have been infected with the coronavirus |date=9 March 2020 |work=El Pais |access-date=13 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200316212824/https://english.elpais.com/society/2020-03-13/more-spanish-politicians-confirm-they-have-been-infected-with-the-coronavirus.html |archive-date=16 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> When the [[Congress of Deputies (Spain)|Congress of Deputies]] approved the extension of the [[State of Alarm]] on 18 March, it was the first time that opposition parties [[Popular Party (Spain)|Popular Party]] and [[Vox (Spain)|Vox]] had supported the government in a vote while separatist parties, such as [[Catalan Republican Left]], abstained from the vote.<ref name="opposition" />

The response to the coronavirus has been complicated by the fact that [[Pedro Sánchez]] is leading  [[PSOE]] (in coalition with [[Unidas Podemos]]) [[minority government]] which is counting on support from opposition parties to enact coronavirus measures, especially with regards to economic stimulus. So far, the cabinet is discussing proposals to offer zero-interest loans to tenants to pay rent so that smaller landlords who depend on rent income can stay afloat. PP leader [[Pablo Casado]] complained that the government was not keeping him informed of developments on the coronavirus. [[Ciudadanos]] leader [[Inés Arrimadas]] said that she supports the government's actions.<ref name=opposition>{{cite news |title=Government counting on opposition support for coronavirus measures despite lack of dialogue |url=https://english.elpais.com/politics/2020-03-31/government-counting-on-opposition-support-for-coronavirus-measures-despite-lack-of-dialogue.html?rel=mas |access-date=1 April 2020 |work=EL PAÍS |date=31 March 2020 |language=en}}</ref>

=== United Kingdom === 
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in the United Kingdom}} 
The timeline of the COVID-19 pandemic in the UK highlights both successes and failures in the government's response to containing and then controlling the disease, but will also highlight their political and social actions which have had a series of mixed results.

On the 5th March, Health minister [[Nadine Dorries]] was the first parliamentarian to show COVID-19 symptoms.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-51827356|title=Health minister tests positive for coronavirus|date=11 March 2020|via=www.bbc.com}}</ref> MP [[Kate Osborne]] showed them some days later.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-england-tyne-51906813|title=Second MP diagnosed with coronavirus|date=16 March 2020|work=BBC News|access-date=18 March 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200317213024/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-england-tyne-51906813|archive-date=17 March 2020}}</ref> On the 13th March, the [[2020 United Kingdom local elections]] were postponed for a year,<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-51876269|title=English local elections postponed over coronavirus|date=13 March 2020|work=BBC News|access-date=13 March 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200313194513/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-51876269|archive-date=13 March 2020}}</ref> the longest postponement of democratic elections in the UK since the [[interwar period]].<ref>{{Cite web|title=StackPath|url=https://www.instituteforgovernment.org.uk/explainers/delaying-elections|access-date=2020-12-01|website=www.instituteforgovernment.org.uk}}</ref> In late March, the [[Parliament of the United Kingdom|UK]], [[Scottish Parliament|Scottish]] and [[Welsh Parliament]]s scaled back their activities.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Syal|first=Rajeev|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/apr/01/uk-set-up-virtual-parliament-during-coronavirus-shutdown|title=UK to set up virtual parliament during coronavirus shutdown|date=1 April 2020|work=The Guardian|access-date=7 April 2020 |issn=0261-3077}}</ref>

On the 23rd March, a national lockdown is announced by Boris Johnson in an attempt to reduce the spread of COVID-19, where all non-essential business is told to shut down, households prevented from mixing and limited outdoor interaction. <ref>{{Cite web|title=Prime Minister's statement on coronavirus (COVID-19): 23 March 2020|url=https://www.gov.uk/government/speeches/pm-address-to-the-nation-on-coronavirus-23-march-2020|access-date=2020-12-09|website=GOV.UK|language=en}}</ref> A financial support package is announced on the 26th March which should cover 80% of self-employed earnings over the past three years. <ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-03-26|title=Coronavirus: UK government unveils aid for self-employed|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-52053914|access-date=2020-12-10}}</ref>

On 27th March, both [[Prime Minister of the United Kingdom|Prime Minister]] [[Boris Johnson]] and [[Secretary of State for Health and Social Care]] [[Matt Hancock]] announced that they had tested positive for the virus.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://metro.co.uk/2020/03/27/health-secretary-matt-hancock-tests-positive-coronavirus-12466332/|title=Coronavirus strikes heart of Government as PM and health secretary test positive|date=27 March 2020|work=Metro|access-date=27 March 2020}}</ref> On the same day, [[Labour Party (UK)|Labour Party]] MP [[Angela Rayner]], the [[Shadow Secretary of State for Education]], confirmed she had been suffering symptoms and was self-isolating.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.itv.com/news/granada/2020-03-27/north-west-mp-angela-rayner-says-she-is-self-isolating/|title=North West MP Angela Rayner says she is self-isolating|date=27 March 2020|work=ITV News|access-date=27 March 2020}}</ref> Chief Medical Officer [[Chris Whitty]] also reported suffering from symptoms and would be self-isolating, while continuing to advise the UK government.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://news.sky.com/story/coronavirus-chief-medical-officer-chris-whitty-self-isolates-with-symptoms-11964697|title=Coronavirus: Chief medical officer Chris Whitty self-isolates with symptoms|date=27 March 2020|work=Sky News|access-date=27 March 2020}}</ref>

The 28th March marked the first death of a frontline NHS worker,<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-03-29|title=NHS consultant dies from Covid-19|url=http://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/29/first-nhs-consultant-dies-from-covid-19|access-date=2020-12-09|website=the Guardian|language=en}}</ref> with Amged El-Hawrani, a 55-year-old consultant dying after testing positive for coronavirus. 

On 30th March the Prime Minister's senior adviser [[Dominic Cummings#COVID-19 pandemic|Dominic Cummings]] was reported to be self-isolating after experiencing coronavirus symptoms. He had been at Downing Street on 27th March and was stated to have developed symptoms over 28th and 29th March.<ref name="guardian20200330">{{cite news|last=Syal|first=Rajeev|date=30 March 2020|title=Dominic Cummings self-isolates after experiencing coronavirus symptoms|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/mar/30/dominic-cummings-self-isolates-after-experiencing-coronavirus-symptoms}}</ref> 

On 2nd April, the world reaches 1 million confirmed cases of coronavirus,<ref>{{Cite web|last=Feuer|first=Will|date=2020-04-02|title=Worldwide coronavirus cases reach 1 million, doubling in a week as death toll tops 50,000|url=https://www.cnbc.com/2020/04/02/worldwide-coronavirus-cases-reach-1-million-doubling-in-a-week.html|access-date=2020-12-09|website=CNBC|language=en}}</ref> according to [[Johns Hopkins University]], with Boris Johnson coming out of self-isolation on the same day. A new Labour leader is elected on the 4th April, [[Keir Starmer|Sir Keir Starmer]] replacing [[Jeremy Corbyn]] as the [[Labour Party (UK)|Labour Party]]'s leader, amidst growing cases and deaths in the UK. Over the coming days, the Prime Minister is moved back into hospital with worsening conditions, and is placed into intensive care as a precautionary measure,<ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-04-07|title=Coronavirus: Boris Johnson moved to intensive care as symptoms worsen|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-52192604|access-date=2020-12-09}}</ref> but later moved back onto the standard COVID wards.

On the 8th April, the first major cracks in government policy appear as various medical associations speak-out about the dangerously low levels of [[Personal protective equipment|PPE]] available which is endangering patients health.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Bateman|first=Matthew|title=Doctors forced into impossible situations as NHS staff report dangerously low levels of PPE|url=https://www.bma.org.uk/bma-media-centre/doctors-forced-into-impossible-situations-as-nhs-staff-report-dangerously-low-levels-of-ppe|access-date=2020-12-09|website=The British Medical Association is the trade union and professional body for doctors in the UK.|language=en-gb}}</ref> The government is criticised later that month with a [[BBC]] report coming out suggesting ministers failed to organise PPE to be stockpiled, and that advice was ignored when they were told to fill the gap in missing equipment by their own advisers, putting at risk both patients and staff to the virus. <ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-04-28|title=Coronavirus: UK failed to stockpile crucial PPE|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/newsbeat-52440641|access-date=2020-12-09}}</ref> On the 23rd April, millions of people become eligible  for a coronavirus test after a large expansion went underway for [[Key worker|essential workers]] and their households, <ref>{{Cite web|title=Coronavirus testing extended to all essential workers in England who have symptoms|url=https://www.gov.uk/government/news/coronavirus-testing-extended-to-all-essential-workers-in-england-who-have-symptoms|access-date=2020-12-09|website=GOV.UK|language=en}}</ref> and on the same day the first element of human trials in the UK for the virus [[vaccine]] begin, lead by [[University of Oxford|Oxford University]].<ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-04-23|title=Coronavirus: First patients injected in UK vaccine trial|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/health-52394485|access-date=2020-12-09}}</ref>
