''El País''. 19 March 2020.</ref> During a speech by the president about the pandemic, many Brazilians participated in a ''[[Cacerolazo|panelaço]]'' protesting the president by banging pots and pans on balconies.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-51955679|title=Brazil coronavirus protesters urge 'Bolsonaro out'|date=19 March 2020|work=BBC News|access-date=22 March 2020|language=en-GB}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|first=Tom |last=Phillips |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/20/jair-bolsonaro-dictatorship-rally-protest-brazil-president-denounced |title=Brazilian president Jair Bolsonaro denounced for joining pro-dictatorship rally &#124; World news |newspaper=The Guardian |access-date=27 April 2020}}</ref>

=== Canada ===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Canada}}
On 13 March 2020, the [[Parliament of Canada]] voted to suspend activity in both houses until 20 April for the [[House of Commons of Canada|House of Commons]] and 21 April for the [[Senate of Canada|Senate]].<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cp24.com/news/parliament-suspends-for-five-weeks-over-covid-19-concerns-1.4851501 |title=Parliament suspends for five weeks over COVID-19 concerns |date=13 March 2020 |work=CP 24 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200315013940/https://www.cp24.com/news/parliament-suspends-for-five-weeks-over-covid-19-concerns-1.4851501 |archive-date=15 March 2020}}</ref>  The House of Commons' Health and Finance committees were granted the ability to hold weekly virtual meetings during the pandemic.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Aiello |first=Rachel |url=https://www.ctvnews.ca/health/coronavirus/house-health-committee-holding-first-virtual-briefing-on-covid-19-efforts-1.4875766 |title=House health committee holding first virtual briefing on COVID-19 efforts |date=31 March 2020 |work=[[CTV News]] |access-date=31 March 2020}}</ref>

The leadership contests of the [[2020 Conservative Party of Canada leadership election|Conservative Party of Canada]], [[2020 Green Party of British Columbia leadership election|Green Party of British Columbia]], [[2020 Quebec Liberal Party leadership election|Quebec Liberal Party]] and [[2020 Parti Québécois leadership election|Parti Québécois]] were postponed.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Canadian Press|first=The|url=https://www.nationalnewswatch.com/2020/03/26/canadian-press-newsalert-conservatives-suspend-partys-leadership-race/|title=Conservatives suspend party's leadership race in face of COVID-19 crisis|date=26 March 2020|work=National Newswatch|access-date=26 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Rothbauer |first=Kevin |title=B.C. Greens suspend leadership race due to COVID-19 |url=https://www.albernivalleynews.com/news/b-c-greens-suspend-leadership-race-due-to-covid-19 |access-date=27 March 2020 |work=Alberni Valley News |date=27 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Quebec Liberal Party suspends its leadership contest due to COVID-19 pandemic |url=https://montreal.ctvnews.ca/quebec-liberal-party-suspends-its-leadership-contest-due-to-covid-19-pandemic-1.4861644 |access-date=29 March 2020 |work=CTV News |agency=Canadian Press |date=20 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=COVID-19: Le Parti Québécois met sa course à la direction en pause |url=https://www.journaldequebec.com/2020/03/28/covid-19-le-parti-quebecois-met-sa-course-a-la-direction-en-pause |access-date=28 March 2020 |work=Le journal de Montreal |date=29 March 2020}}</ref>

===China===
{{see also|COVID-19 pandemic in mainland China}}
Multiple provincial-level administrators of the [[Communist Party of China]] (CPC) were dismissed over their handling of the quarantine efforts in central China. Some experts believe this is likely in a move to protect Communist Party general secretary [[Xi Jinping]] from people's anger over the coronavirus outbreak.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.businessinsider.com/analysis-china-hubei-officials-sacked-xi-jinping-protected-2020-2 |title=China sacked a brace of top officials in Hubei province, likely in a move to protect Xi Jinping from people's anger over the coronavirus outbreak |last=Bostock |first=Bill |work=Business Insider |access-date=26 February 2020 |date=13 February 2020}}</ref> [[Taiwan]] has also voiced concern over being included in any travel ban involving the People's Republic of China due to the "[[one-China policy]]" and [[Political status of Taiwan|Chinese claims]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://medicalxpress.com/news/2020-02-taiwan-china-virus.html |title=Taiwan hits out at China virus travel bans |work=medicalxpress.com |access-date=26 February 2020}}</ref> A few countries have been using the epidemic to build [[Foreign relations of China|political bridges]] with [[Government of China|Beijing]], raising accusations that these countries, which include [[Cambodia]] among others, were putting politics before health.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/02/21/hun-sen-is-more-worried-about-beijing-than-the-coronavirus/ |title=Hun Sen Is More Worried About Beijing Than the Coronavirus |last=Wilson |first=Audrey |work=[[Foreign Policy]] |access-date=3 March 2020}}</ref> Existing [[China–United States trade war|tensions]] between the United States and China may have delayed a coordinated effort to combat the outbreak in Wuhan.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.atlanticcouncil.org/event/peering-around-the-corner-the-geopolitics-of-the-coronavirus/ |title=Peering around the corner: The geopolitics of the coronavirus |work=[[Atlantic Council]] |access-date=3 March 2020}}</ref>

Outlets such as ''[[Politico]]'', ''[[Foreign Policy]]'', and [[Bloomberg News|Bloomberg]] have reported that efforts from China to send aid to other countries and claim without evidence that the virus originated in the United States are a [[Propaganda in China|propaganda]] push for global influence while deflecting blame for its handling of the outbreak.<ref name="politico-corona">{{cite news|url=https://www.politico.eu/article/coronavirus-china-winning-propaganda-war/|title=China is winning the coronavirus propaganda war|date=18 March 2020|work=Politico}}</ref><ref name="Foreign Policy"/><ref name="The Straits Times"/>

==== Hong Kong ====
{{see also|COVID-19 pandemic in Hong Kong|Hong Kong national security law}}
[[2019–20 Hong Kong protests|Protests in Hong Kong]] strengthened due to fears of immigration from mainland China.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.channelnewsasia.com/news/asia/wuhan-virus-hong-kong-protests-china-12348984 |title=Hong Kong protesters torch planned Wuhan virus quarantine building |publisher=[[Channel NewsAsia]] |access-date=26 February 2020}}</ref> In order to crackdown Hong Kong protests, China drift a new Hong Kong national security law which have drawn international concerns.

===Hungary===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Hungary}}

The [[National Assembly (Hungary)|Hungarian Parliament]] gave the government [[plenary power]] which authorizes it to override acts and to [[rule by decree]] to the extent that is "necessary and proportional" in order to ''"''prevent, manage, and eradicate the epidemic and to avoid and mitigate its effects".<ref name=":2">{{cite web|url=https://index.hu/english/2020/03/30/hungary_coronavirus_act_parliament_viktor_orban_fidesz_sweeping_powers_indefinite_term/|title=Hungarian Coronavirus Act passes, granting Viktor Orbán unprecedented emergency powers|last=Zoltán|first=Kovács|date=30 March 2020|website=index.hu|language=en|access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref> The law prescribes that the government is to report back to the parliament, or if it's unable to convene, to its speaker and the leaders of the parliamentary groups, regularly about the measures it has taken.<ref name=":2" /> The law also suspends [[by-elections]] and referendums for the duration of the emergency.<ref>{{cite web|last=Liu |first=Abraham |url=https://www.politico.eu/article/hungary-viktor-orban-rule-by-decree/ |title=Hungary's Viktor Orbán wins vote to rule by decree |work=Politico |access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref><ref name=":2" /> The [[Constitutional Court of Hungary]] is authorized to hold sessions via electronic communications networks.<ref name=":2" /> The act also criminalizes "statements known to be false or statements distorting true facts" with 1 to 5 years imprisonment "if done in a manner capable of hindering or derailing the effectiveness of the response effort".<ref name=":2" /> The opposition had demanded a 90-day [[Sunset provision|sunset clause]] to the emergency powers in return for its support, but had its amendments voted down and therefore opposed the act.<ref name=":2" />

[[Human Rights Watch]] described the legislation, as an authoritarian takeover, due to the rule of decree without parliamentary or judicial scrutiny and for criminal penalties for the publishing of "false" or "distorted" facts, and gave support to the European Commission using [[Article 7 of the Treaty on European Union|Article 7]] against Hungary. Criticism and concern regarding the decree stemmed from existing [[democratic backsliding|backsliding]] of Hungarian democracy under the premiership of [[Viktor Orbán]] and his majority-ruling [[Fidesz]] party since Orbán began his second tenure as [[Prime Minister of Hungary|Prime Minister]] in 2010. Orbán has been accused by opposition leaders and other critics of his premiership of shifting Hungary towards [[authoritarianism]] by centralizing legislative and executive power through [[Constitution of Hungary#2011 Constitution|Constitutional reforms]] passed in 2011 and 2013, curbing civil liberties, restricting freedom of speech to the extent that some independent media outlets once critical of his rule have since been acquired by allies of Orbán, and weakening other institutional [[separation of powers|checks on Orbán's power]] including the Constitutional Court and judiciary. Critics of the Orbán/Fidesz government expressed concern that the emergency plenary powers may not be rescinded once the pandemic subsides, and could be abused to dubiously prosecute independent journalists critical of his coronavirus response or his governance more broadly, and curtail other freedoms of speech and expression. Some observers suggest that any significant misuse of or, once the crisis subsides, failure to rescind the plenary powers by Orbán government could place Hungary at great risk of becoming the European Union's first [[dictatorship]], in violation of E.U. regulations. (Turkey's proposed E.U. membership has been held up and advocates have urged the Union to terminate the proposal, because of human rights violations under [[President of Turkey|President]] [[Recep Tayyip Erdogan]]'s government.)<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2020/04/01/hungarys-authoritarian-takeover-puts-european-union-risk#|title=Hungary's Authoritarian Takeover Puts European Union at Risk|date=1 April 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404030627/https://www.hrw.org/news/2020/04/01/hungarys-authoritarian-takeover-puts-european-union-risk|archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/victor-orbans-power-grab-in-hungry-heightens-fears-of-dictatorship-in-eu-83h3g9lpm|title=Victor Orban's power grab in Hungary heightens fears of dictatorship in EU|date=2 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://balkaninsight.com/2020/03/31/hungary-no-longer-a-democracy-after-coronavirus-law/|title=HUNGARY 'NO LONGER A DEMOCRACY' AFTER CORONAVIRUS LAW|date=31 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.rfi.fr/en/europe/20200401-how-coronavirus-legislation-could-create-the-eu-s-first-dictatorship|title=How coronavirus legislation could create the EU's first dictatorship|date=1 April 2020}}</ref> A petition against the legislation was signed by over 100,000 people. [[Péter Jakab]], the president of the opposition party [[Jobbik]], said that the bill put Hungarian democracy in quarantine. Nézőpont, a pro-government polling agency, conducted a poll that showed that 90% of Hungarians supported extending emergency measures and 72% supported strengthening the criminal code.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-52095500 |title=Coronavirus: Hungary government gets sweeping powers |date=30 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200330144929/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-52095500 |archive-date=30 March 2020}}</ref>

In response to news reports about the state of emergency being a danger to democracy, Foreign Minister [[Péter Szijjártó]] called them "fake news and lies" and stated that the measures that Hungary had adopted were not unprecedented in Europe. He specifically stated that there were unfounded reports in mainstream media about the government's unlimited authorization and the closing down of the Parliament.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://edition.cnn.com/videos/tv/2020/04/09/peter-szijjarto-hungary-foreign-minister-amanpour-viktor-orban-democracy.cnn|title=Szijjártó: "Fake news and lies" spread on Hungary|date=10 April 2020}}</ref>

European Commission vice-president Věra Jourová after a thorough examination confirmed that Hungary's recently adopted emergency measures do not break any EU rules yet.<ref>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TDp24_MCC-8</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://euobserver.com/tickers/148218|title=[Ticker] Jourova: Hungary decree law does not break EU rules yet|website=EUobserver}}</ref>

===Iran===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Iran}}
The [[Government of the Islamic Republic of Iran]] has been heavily affected by the virus.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/middle_east/coronavirus-pummels-iran-leadership-as-data-show-spread-is-far-worse-than-reported/2020/03/04/7b1196ae-5c9f-11ea-ac50-18701e14e06d_story.html |title=Coronavirus pummels Iran leadership as data show spread is far worse than reported |last=Cunningham |first=Erin |work=[[The Washington Post]] |access-date=15 March 2020}}</ref> The spread of the virus has raised questions about the future survival of the regime.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.nationalreview.com/2020/03/will-irans-regime-survive-coronavirus/ |title=Will Iran's Regime Survive Coronavirus? |date=12 March 2020 |work=[[National Review]] |access-date=15 March 2020}}</ref> Iran's President [[Hassan Rouhani]] wrote a public letter to world leaders asking for help, saying that his country doesn't have access to international markets due to the [[United States sanctions against Iran]].<ref>{{cite news |title=U.S. sanctions 'severely hamper' Iran coronavirus fight, Rouhani says |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-iran/us-sanctions-severely-hamper-iran-coronavirus-fight-rouhani-idUSKBN2110HL |work=Reuters |date=14 March 2020}}</ref> On 3 March 2020, [[Islamic Consultative Assembly|Iranian Parliament]] was shut down after having 23 of the 290 members of parliament reported to have had tested positive for the virus.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.businessinsider.com/8-percent-iran-parliament-has-coronavirus-it-released-54000-prisoners-2020-3|title=8% of Iran's parliament has the coronavirus, and it released 54,000 prisoners as the country descends into chaos|last=Haltiwanger|first=John|name-list-style=vanc|website=Business Insider|access-date=4 March 2020|date=3 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200304001925/https://www.businessinsider.com/8-percent-iran-parliament-has-coronavirus-it-released-54000-prisoners-2020-3|archive-date=4 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

===Israel===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Israel}}

After facing political deadlock since the [[April 2019 Israeli legislative election|legislative election]] held on 9 April 2019, Israel held two more elections in 2020, which ended with Netanyahu forming the [[Thirty-fifth government of Israel]].

On 28 March 2020, the [[United Nations]] Special Coordinator for the [[Middle East]] Peace Process, [[Nickolay Mladenov]] praised the Israel and [[Palestinian National Authority|Palestinian authorities]] for their coordination in tackling the [[Coronavirus disease 2019|COVID-19]] pandemic. Mladenov appreciated the response strategy, especially for focusing on [[Gaza Strip|Gaza]], as the region faces a relatively substantial risk of the disease spreading. Since the start of the [[COVID-19 pandemic|novel coronavirus crisis]], Israel permitted the entry of significant medical and aid supplies inside Gaza.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.un.org/en/story/2020/03/1060572|title=COVID-19: UN envoy hails strong Israel-Palestine cooperation|access-date=28 March 2020|website=UN News}}</ref>

===Kosovo===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Kosovo}}

On 18 March, Interior Minister Agim Veliu was sacked due to his support for declaring a state of emergency to handle the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Kosovo|coronavirus pandemic]] which would have given power to the Kosovo Security Council chaired by [[Hashim Thaçi]]. The [[Democratic League of Kosovo]], the junior partner leader of the coalition, filed a no-confidence vote motion in retaliation for the sacking and on 25 March eighty two members of the [[Assembly of the Republic of Kosovo|Kosovo Assembly]] voted in favor of the motion.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://balkaninsight.com/2020/03/19/kosovos-crisis-hit-govt-threatened-with-no-confidence-vote/ |title=Kosovo's Crisis-Hit Govt Threatened with No-Confidence Vote |date=19 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326004128/https://balkaninsight.com/2020/03/19/kosovos-crisis-hit-govt-threatened-with-no-confidence-vote/ |archive-date=26 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.trtworld.com/europe/kosovo-govt-toppled-by-no-confidence-vote-amid-coronavirus-34859 |title=Kosovo govt toppled by no-confidence vote amid coronavirus |date=25 March 2020 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326004241/https://www.trtworld.com/europe/kosovo-govt-toppled-by-no-confidence-vote-amid-coronavirus-34859 |archive-date=26 March 2020 |access-date=26 March 2020 }}</ref>

===Slovenia===

On its 1st Session on 13 March 2020, immediately following its confirmation, the [[13th Government of Slovenia|13th Government]] set up an informal Crisis Management Staff (CMS) of the Republic of Slovenia in order to contain and manage the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Slovenia|COVID-19 epidemic]]. Head of the Staff was Prime Minister [[Janez Janša]] and its secretary was former [[Slovenian Intelligence and Security Agency|SOVA]] director [[Andrej Rupnik]]. CMS was composed of all government members (prime minister and ministers) and other experts and civil servants in an advisory capacity.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.gov.si/novice/2020-03-14-1-redna-seja-vlade-republike-slovenije/|title=1. redna seja Vlade Republike Slovenije {{!}} GOV.SI|website=Portal GOV.SI|language=sl|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> Head of the Health Group was [[Bojana Beovič]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.gov.si/novice/2020-03-14-spremenjeno-diagnosticiranje-za-realnejse-nacrtovanje-ukrepov-za-obvladovanje-epidemije/|title=Spremenjeno diagnosticiranje za realnejše načrtovanje ukrepov za obvladovanje epidemije {{!}} GOV.SI|website=Portal GOV.SI|language=sl|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> [[Jelko Kacin]], former minister and ambassador to [[NATO]], was the official spokesman of the Staff, he had a similar role during the [[Ten-Day War|1991 Slovenian war of independence]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.24ur.com/novice/slovenija/na-kriznem-stabu-o-morebitnih-novih-ukrepih-vec-znanih-obrazov-tudi-jelko-kacin.html|title=Govorec kriznega štaba Kacin: V nedeljo sestanek direktorjev bolnišnic|website=24ur.com|language=sl|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref>

Crisis Management Staff was abolished on 24 March 2020 after the political transition was completed, its functions were transferred on the responsible ministries. Health Experts Group was transferred under the Ministry of Health. Kacin became the official government spokesperson on the topic.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.gov.si/novice/2020-03-24-6-redna-seja-vlade-republike-slovenije/|title=6. redna seja Vlade Republike Slovenije {{!}} GOV.SI|website=Portal GOV.SI|language=sl|access-date=24 March 2020}}</ref>

Government never proposed the declaration of emergency to the National Assembly, which would suspend the Assembly's powers and transfer them to the President of the Republic [[Borut Pahor]] to rule by decrees with the force of law, which are still subject to the National Assembly's approval once it gains its powers back. The provision is only applicable if the National Assembly is unable to meet in the session.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.us-rs.si/en/about-the-court/legal-basis/constitution/|title=Constitution of the Republic of Slovenia|date=11 April 2020|website=Constitutional Court of the Republic of Slovenia}}</ref> Assembly however passed a Rules of Procedure Amendment to enable itself a "long-distance" session using technology.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rtvslo.si/slovenija/poslanci-podprli-spremembe-referendumskega-zakona-naklonjeni-tudi-sejam-na-daljavo/519755|title=Poslanci podprli spremembe referendumskega zakona, naklonjeni tudi sejam na daljavo|website=RTVSLO.si|language=sl|access-date=11 April 2020}}</ref>

===South Korea===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in South Korea}}

Diplomatic [[Japan–South Korea relations|relations between Japan and South Korea]] worsened, as South Korea criticized Japan's "ambiguous and passive quarantine efforts", after Japan announced anybody coming from South Korea will be placed in two weeks’ quarantine at government-designated sites.<ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus quarantine plans ignite row between South Korea and Japan |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/06/coronavirus-quarantine-plans-ignite-row-between-south-korea-and-japan |work=The Guardian |date=6 March 2020 |access-date=15 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200308134434/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/06/coronavirus-quarantine-plans-ignite-row-between-south-korea-and-japan |archive-date=8 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

Following the outbreak of the virus in South Korea over 1,450,000 people signed a petition supporting the impeachment of President [[Moon Jae-in]] due to him sending masks and medical supplies to China to aid them in their response to the virus outbreak.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/03/09/moon-jae-in-china-coronavirus-impeachment-south-korea-president/ |title=South Korea's President Tried to Help China Contain the Coronavirus. Now People Want Him Impeached. |date=9 March 2020 |work=[[Foreign Policy]] |access-date=15 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200312080924/https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/03/09/moon-jae-in-china-coronavirus-impeachment-south-korea-president/ |archive-date=12 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> Moon administration's continuing handling of the crisis has however been noted in other sectors of the Korean society and internationally. An opinion poll by Gallup Korea in March 2020 showed Moon's approval rating rising by 5% to 49%.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.gallup.co.kr/dir/GallupKoreaDaily/GallupKoreaDailyOpinion_392(20200313).pdf|title=데일리 오피니언 제392호(2020년 3월 2주) – 총선 기대, 차기 정치 지도자, 코로나19, 마스크 관련 인식|work=한국갤럽|date=13 March 2020}}</ref>

In April 2020, Moon's [[Democratic Party of Korea|Democratic Party]] won a record landslide in the country's [[Legislative elections in South Korea|legislative election]] for [[List of members of the National Assembly (South Korea), 2020–2024|21st session until 2024]].<ref>{{cite web| title=Moon's Democrats win South Korea general election in landslide| date= 16 April 2020| work=Nikkei Asian Review| url=https://asia.nikkei.com/Spotlight/South-Korea-election/Moon-s-Democrats-win-South-Korea-general-election-in-landslide| access-date=10 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.upi.com/Top_News/World-News/2020/04/16/Ruling-party-sweeps-to-landslide-victory-in-South-Korean-elections/7011587025642/| work= United Press Agency |title= Ruling party sweeps to landslide victory in South Korean elections| date= 16 April 2020| access-date= 10 May 2020}}</ref>

===Spain===
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in Spain}}

On 12 March 2020, the [[Congress of Deputies]] voted to suspend activity for a week after multiple members had tested positive for the virus.<ref name="vox infections">{{Cite news |url=https://english.elpais.com/society/2020-03-13/more-spanish-politicians-confirm-they-have-been-infected-with-the-coronavirus.html |title=More Spanish politicians confirm they have been infected with the coronavirus |date=9 March 2020 |work=El Pais |access-date=13 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200316212824/https://english.elpais.com/society/2020-03-13/more-spanish-politicians-confirm-they-have-been-infected-with-the-coronavirus.html |archive-date=16 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> When the [[Congress of Deputies (Spain)|Congress of Deputies]] approved the extension of the [[State of Alarm]] on 18 March, it was the first time that opposition parties [[Popular Party (Spain)|Popular Party]] and [[Vox (Spain)|Vox]] had supported the government in a vote while separatist parties, such as [[Catalan Republican Left]], abstained from the vote.<ref name="opposition" />

The response to the coronavirus has been complicated by the fact that [[Pedro Sánchez]] is leading  [[PSOE]] (in coalition with [[Unidas Podemos]]) [[minority government]] which is counting on support from opposition parties to enact coronavirus measures, especially with regards to economic stimulus. So far, the cabinet is discussing proposals to offer zero-interest loans to tenants to pay rent so that smaller landlords who depend on rent income can stay afloat. PP leader [[Pablo Casado]] complained that the government was not keeping him informed of developments on the coronavirus. [[Ciudadanos]] leader [[Inés Arrimadas]] said that she supports the government's actions.<ref name=opposition>{{cite news |title=Government counting on opposition support for coronavirus measures despite lack of dialogue |url=https://english.elpais.com/politics/2020-03-31/government-counting-on-opposition-support-for-coronavirus-measures-despite-lack-of-dialogue.html?rel=mas |access-date=1 April 2020 |work=EL PAÍS |date=31 March 2020 |language=en}}</ref>

=== United Kingdom === 
{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in the United Kingdom}} 
The timeline of the COVID-19 pandemic in the UK highlights both successes and failures in the government's response to containing and then controlling the disease, but will also highlight their political and social actions which have had a series of mixed results.

On the 5th March, Health minister [[Nadine Dorries]] was the first parliamentarian to show COVID-19 symptoms.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-51827356|title=Health minister tests positive for coronavirus|date=11 March 2020|via=www.bbc.com}}</ref> MP [[Kate Osborne]] showed them some days later.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-england-tyne-51906813|title=Second MP diagnosed with coronavirus|date=16 March 2020|work=BBC News|access-date=18 March 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200317213024/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-england-tyne-51906813|archive-date=17 March 2020}}</ref> On the 13th March, the [[2020 United Kingdom local elections]] were postponed for a year,<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-51876269|title=English local elections postponed over coronavirus|date=13 March 2020|work=BBC News|access-date=13 March 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200313194513/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-51876269|archive-date=13 March 2020}}</ref> the longest postponement of democratic elections in the UK since the [[interwar period]].<ref>{{Cite web|title=StackPath|url=https://www.instituteforgovernment.org.uk/explainers/delaying-elections|access-date=2020-12-01|website=www.instituteforgovernment.org.uk}}</ref> In late March, the [[Parliament of the United Kingdom|UK]], [[Scottish Parliament|Scottish]] and [[Welsh Parliament]]s scaled back their activities.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Syal|first=Rajeev|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/apr/01/uk-set-up-virtual-parliament-during-coronavirus-shutdown|title=UK to set up virtual parliament during coronavirus shutdown|date=1 April 2020|work=The Guardian|access-date=7 April 2020 |issn=0261-3077}}</ref>

On the 23rd March, a national lockdown is announced by Boris Johnson in an attempt to reduce the spread of COVID-19, where all non-essential business is told to shut down, households prevented from mixing and limited outdoor interaction. <ref>{{Cite web|title=Prime Minister's statement on coronavirus (COVID-19): 23 March 2020|url=https://www.gov.uk/government/speeches/pm-address-to-the-nation-on-coronavirus-23-march-2020|access-date=2020-12-09|website=GOV.UK|language=en}}</ref> A financial support package is announced on the 26th March which should cover 80% of self-employed earnings over the past three years. <ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-03-26|title=Coronavirus: UK government unveils aid for self-employed|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-52053914|access-date=2020-12-10}}</ref>

On 27th March, both [[Prime Minister of the United Kingdom|Prime Minister]] [[Boris Johnson]] and [[Secretary of State for Health and Social Care]] [[Matt Hancock]] announced that they had tested positive for the virus.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://metro.co.uk/2020/03/27/health-secretary-matt-hancock-tests-positive-coronavirus-12466332/|title=Coronavirus strikes heart of Government as PM and health secretary test positive|date=27 March 2020|work=Metro|access-date=27 March 2020}}</ref> On the same day, [[Labour Party (UK)|Labour Party]] MP [[Angela Rayner]], the [[Shadow Secretary of State for Education]], confirmed she had been suffering symptoms and was self-isolating.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.itv.com/news/granada/2020-03-27/north-west-mp-angela-rayner-says-she-is-self-isolating/|title=North West MP Angela Rayner says she is self-isolating|date=27 March 2020|work=ITV News|access-date=27 March 2020}}</ref> Chief Medical Officer [[Chris Whitty]] also reported suffering from symptoms and would be self-isolating, while continuing to advise the UK government.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://news.sky.com/story/coronavirus-chief-medical-officer-chris-whitty-self-isolates-with-symptoms-11964697|title=Coronavirus: Chief medical officer Chris Whitty self-isolates with symptoms|date=27 March 2020|work=Sky News|access-date=27 March 2020}}</ref>

The 28th March marked the first death of a frontline NHS worker,<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-03-29|title=NHS consultant dies from Covid-19|url=http://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/29/first-nhs-consultant-dies-from-covid-19|access-date=2020-12-09|website=the Guardian|language=en}}</ref> with Amged El-Hawrani, a 55-year-old consultant dying after testing positive for coronavirus. 

On 30th March the Prime Minister's senior adviser [[Dominic Cummings#COVID-19 pandemic|Dominic Cummings]] was reported to be self-isolating after experiencing coronavirus symptoms. He had been at Downing Street on 27th March and was stated to have developed symptoms over 28th and 29th March.<ref name="guardian20200330">{{cite news|last=Syal|first=Rajeev|date=30 March 2020|title=Dominic Cummings self-isolates after experiencing coronavirus symptoms|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/mar/30/dominic-cummings-self-isolates-after-experiencing-coronavirus-symptoms}}</ref> 

On 2nd April, the world reaches 1 million confirmed cases of coronavirus,<ref>{{Cite web|last=Feuer|first=Will|date=2020-04-02|title=Worldwide coronavirus cases reach 1 million, doubling in a week as death toll tops 50,000|url=https://www.cnbc.com/2020/04/02/worldwide-coronavirus-cases-reach-1-million-doubling-in-a-week.html|access-date=2020-12-09|website=CNBC|language=en}}</ref> according to [[Johns Hopkins University]], with Boris Johnson coming out of self-isolation on the same day. A new Labour leader is elected on the 4th April, [[Keir Starmer|Sir Keir Starmer]] replacing [[Jeremy Corbyn]] as the [[Labour Party (UK)|Labour Party]]'s leader, amidst growing cases and deaths in the UK. Over the coming days, the Prime Minister is moved back into hospital with worsening conditions, and is placed into intensive care as a precautionary measure,<ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-04-07|title=Coronavirus: Boris Johnson moved to intensive care as symptoms worsen|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-52192604|access-date=2020-12-09}}</ref> but later moved back onto the standard COVID wards.

On the 8th April, the first major cracks in government policy appear as various medical associations speak-out about the dangerously low levels of [[Personal protective equipment|PPE]] available which is endangering patients health.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Bateman|first=Matthew|title=Doctors forced into impossible situations as NHS staff report dangerously low levels of PPE|url=https://www.bma.org.uk/bma-media-centre/doctors-forced-into-impossible-situations-as-nhs-staff-report-dangerously-low-levels-of-ppe|access-date=2020-12-09|website=The British Medical Association is the trade union and professional body for doctors in the UK.|language=en-gb}}</ref> The government is criticised later that month with a [[BBC]] report coming out suggesting ministers failed to organise PPE to be stockpiled, and that advice was ignored when they were told to fill the gap in missing equipment by their own advisers, putting at risk both patients and staff to the virus. <ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-04-28|title=Coronavirus: UK failed to stockpile crucial PPE|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/newsbeat-52440641|access-date=2020-12-09}}</ref> On the 23rd April, millions of people become eligible  for a coronavirus test after a large expansion went underway for [[Key worker|essential workers]] and their households, <ref>{{Cite web|title=Coronavirus testing extended to all essential workers in England who have symptoms|url=https://www.gov.uk/government/news/coronavirus-testing-extended-to-all-essential-workers-in-england-who-have-symptoms|access-date=2020-12-09|website=GOV.UK|language=en}}</ref> and on the same day the first element of human trials in the UK for the virus [[vaccine]] begin, lead by [[University of Oxford|Oxford University]].<ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-04-23|title=Coronavirus: First patients injected in UK vaccine trial|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/health-52394485|access-date=2020-12-09}}</ref>

The 1st May represents a victory for the government as they hit their testing target of 100,000 tests per day on the 30th April, <ref>{{Cite news|last1=Stewart|first1=Heather|last2=Campbell|first2=Denis|date=2020-05-01|title=Hancock says UK hit 100,000 tests amid claims tally is artificially boosted|language=en-GB|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/may/01/ministers-accused-of-changing-covid-19-test-tally-to-hit-100000-goal|access-date=2020-12-09|issn=0261-3077}}</ref> and although this was prior to the death toll in the UK surpassing [[Italy]] on the 5th May, becoming the highest in [[Europe]]. <ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-05-05|title=Coronavirus: UK death toll passes Italy to be highest in Europe|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-52549860|access-date=2020-12-09}}</ref>  The 7th May also brings a new, horrifying statistic regarding black men and women in England and Wales as being more than four times more likely to die from a coronavirus related death than white people,<ref>{{Cite web|title=Coronavirus (COVID-19) related deaths by ethnic group, England and Wales - Office for National Statistics|url=https://www.ons.gov.uk/peoplepopulationandcommunity/birthsdeathsandmarriages/deaths/articles/coronavirusrelateddeathsbyethnicgroupenglandandwales/2march2020to10april2020|access-date=2020-12-09|website=www.ons.gov.uk}}</ref> according to the [[Office for National Statistics|ONS]]. The 10th May is the day where the nation can finally start to breathe again, with lockdown restrictions eased slightly over the course of the next few days and some outdoor shops like Garden Center's finally reopening on the 11th May for the first time since March. <ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-05-13|title=Coronavirus: Some return to work as lockdown eases slightly in England|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-52642222|access-date=2020-12-10}}</ref> The following day on the 12th May, the [[Chancellor of the Exchequer|Chancellor]] extends the furlough scheme until the end of October, but with employers picking up more of the bill as the months progress and economy opens back up. <ref>{{Cite web|title=Chancellor extends furlough scheme until October|url=https://www.gov.uk/government/news/chancellor-extends-furlough-scheme-until-october|access-date=2020-12-10|website=GOV.UK|language=en}}</ref> The first sign of a vaccine appears on the 17th May when Oxford University sign a [[licensing agreement]] with [[AstraZeneca]] to supply 100 million doses of a vaccine. <ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-05-17|title=Plans in place to potentially make 30m virus vaccines for public by September|url=https://www.itv.com/news/2020-05-17/coronavirus-daily-briefing-alok-sharma-stephen-powis-schools|access-date=2020-12-10|website=ITV News|language=en}}</ref> On the 18th May, wider coronavirus testing becomes available for all those aged five or older if they are showing symptoms, also expanding to a loss of taste or smell. <ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-05-18|title=Everyone over the age of five with coronavirus symptoms can now be tested|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/coronavirus-testing-availability-uk-age-five-symptoms-latest-hancock-a9520401.html|access-date=2020-12-10|website=The Independent|language=en}}</ref> On the 22nd May, [[Home Secretary]], [[Priti Patel]], announced on that people arriving from overseas into the UK would have to [[quarantine]] for 14 days, beginning on the 8th June.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Topping|first1=Sarah Marsh (now); Alexandra|last2=Weaver(earlier)|first2=Matthew|last3=Marsh|first3=Sarah|last4=Marsh|first4=Sarah|date=2020-05-22|title=UK coronavirus: travellers arriving from 8 June must self-isolate for 14 days – as it happened|language=en-GB|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/live/2020/may/22/uk-coronavirus-live-news-update-covid-19-travel-quarantine-plan|access-date=2020-12-10|issn=0261-3077}}</ref> Over the next few days, from the 23rd to 25th May, Boris Johnson's senior aide, [[Dominic Cummings]], comes under fire for allegedly breaking lockdown rules. Johnson defends him, prior to him making a public press conference to defend his innocence. <ref>{{Cite news|last=Weaver|first=Matthew|date=2020-05-22|title=Pressure on Dominic Cummings to quit over lockdown breach|language=en-GB|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/may/22/dominic-cummings-durham-trip-coronavirus-lockdown|access-date=2020-12-10|issn=0261-3077}}</ref>

On the 1st June, lockdown measures are eased again, with some school children heading back into the classroom. <ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-05-29|title=All the coronavirus measures easing in England on 1 June|url=https://inews.co.uk/news/new-lockdown-rules-uk-coronavirus-measures-easing-england-when-1-june-changes-explained-432214|access-date=2020-12-10|website=inews.co.uk|language=en}}</ref> The 15th June also showed some more easing of restrictions with high-streets reopening and places of worship also allowing for private prayer.<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-06-15|title=What are the lockdown rules now and what can you do from today?|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/home-news/coronavirus-uk-lockdown-rule-change-15-june-boris-johnson-a9566161.html|access-date=2020-12-10|website=The Independent|language=en}}</ref> However we see another government failure on the 18th June, when the government abandon their own NHS track and trace app, making way for [[Apple Inc.|Apple]] and [[Google]] to take over the design. <ref>{{Cite news|last1=Murphy|first1=Simon|last2=Sabbagh|first2=Dan|last3=Hern|first3=Alex|date=2020-06-18|title=Piloted in May, ditched in June: the failure of England's Covid-19 app|language=en-GB|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/jun/18/piloted-in-may-ditched-in-june-the-failure-of-englands-covid-19-app|access-date=2020-12-10|issn=0261-3077}}</ref> This failure comes nearly a month after track and tract was launched in England on the 28th May, and with no effective way of tracking infected cases after it was announced a system would be in place by the 1st June. The failure in government policy and practicality shows a lack of organisation and capability when executing such pivotal tasks under high-pressure conditions. On the 29th June, a local lockdown is re-imposed on [[Leicester]] due to a spike in COVID-19 cases, while the rest of the country moves to further ease restrictions for social gatherings on the 4th July. <ref>{{Cite web|title=Leicester is first city to go back into lockdown as coronavirus surges|url=https://www.expressandstar.com/news/uk-news/2020/06/30/leicester-is-first-city-to-go-back-into-lockdown-as-coronavirus-surges/|access-date=2020-12-10|website=www.expressandstar.com|language=en}}</ref> 

The UK's travel corridor list is finally published on the 3rd of July, with 73 countries where Britons can fly to and return without having the need to [[quarantine]],<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Dickinson|first1=Greg|last2=Frainier|first2=Lizzie|last3=Smith|first3=Oliver|last4=Morris|first4=Hugh|date=2020-07-03|title=Travel news: Greece in, Portugal out, as quarantine exemption list revealed|language=en-GB|work=The Telegraph|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2020/07/03/uk-travel-quarantine-countries-exempt-without-list-air-bridges-news/|access-date=2020-12-10|issn=0307-1235}}</ref> while the [[Secretary of State for Health and Social Care|Health Secretary]] announced a partial easing of restrictions in [[Leicester]] on the 16th July. <ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-07-16|title=Leicester lockdown: Measures eased after coronavirus cases drop|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-england-leicestershire-53416023|access-date=2020-12-10}}</ref> Although restrictions have eased, from the 24th July, shoppers are told that face masks are mandatory in England, with fines of £100 if the laws aren't respected, and only for Spain to be removed off the quarantine exemption list on the 26th July, suggests that cases may be on the rise. The end of July also reflects this with [[Matt Hancock]] warning of a second wave beginning to "roll across Europe" on the 30th July, and halting the further easing of restrictions supposed to be taking place on the 1st of August.

On the 3rd of August, the largely successful 'Eat Out to Help Out' scheme is launched by [[Rishi Sunak]], with half price meals Monday to Friday throughout August.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Eat Out to Help Out launches today – with government paying half on restaurant bills|url=https://www.gov.uk/government/news/eat-out-to-help-out-launches-today-with-government-paying-half-on-restaurant-bills|access-date=2020-12-10|website=GOV.UK|language=en}}</ref> The following two weeks, however, both on the 13th August and 17th August, could be the biggest government failure over the course of the entire [[pandemic]] so-far. Students are traumatised to learn that their [[A-level]] exam results in England have been downgraded, some by significant margins. It was also reported that students from disadvantaged backgrounds were hit worse than those from more privileged backgrounds, prompting Britain's equality watchdog that they might step in to investigate this issue further. <ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-08-13|title=Equalities body warns it may step in after A-level downgrades in England|url=http://www.theguardian.com/education/2020/aug/13/equalities-body-warns-it-may-step-in-after-a-level-downgrades-in-england|access-date=2020-12-10|website=the Guardian|language=en}}</ref> The failure in the [[Algorithmic bias|algorithm]] has meant that many top-achieving students had their grades unreasonably lowered, resulting in rejections from their first, and sometimes second choice universities, leaving them to either take a gap year, or apply through 'clearing' on [[UCAS]]. Many top-tier universities have their spaces filled quickly, and so those students [[Sixth form|sixth-form]] student still pursuing an education this year may have been forced to take a place on a different course, or at a different institution all-together, ruining their hopes of attending their dream university.  

===United States===
{{Anchor|United States domestic}}{{Main|COVID-19 pandemic in the United States|U.S. federal government response to the COVID-19 pandemic}}
Due to the [[2020 stock market crash|stock market crash]], high unemployment claims, and [[Financial impact of the COVID-19 pandemic|reduced economic activity]] caused by the coronavirus pandemic the [[United States Congress]] convened to create legislation to address the economic effects of the pandemic and passed the [[Coronavirus Aid, Relief, and Economic Security Act]] (CARES Act). Representative [[Thomas Massie]] attempted to maneuver for a [[roll-call vote]], but there was insufficient demand [[Procedures of the United States Congress#Quorum and vote|among the quorum present]] and the House passed the bill by [[voice vote]] on 27 March.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Hughes |first1=Siobhan |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/house-lawmakers-race-to-washington-to-ensure-coronavirus-stimulus-passes-11585318472 |title=House Passes $2 Trillion Coronavirus Stimulus Package |date=27 March 2020 |work=Wall Street Journal |access-date=27 March 2020 |last2=Andrews |first2=Natalie |language=en-US |issn=0099-9660}}</ref>

The outbreak prompted calls for the United States to adopt social policies common in other wealthy countries, including [[universal health care]], [[universal child care]], [[paid sick leave]], and higher levels of funding for public health.<ref name="NYT Calls">{{cite news |last1=Miller |first1=Claire Cain |title=Could the Pandemic Wind Up Fixing What's Broken About Work in America? |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/10/upshot/coronavirus-future-work-america.html |access-date=3 May 2020 |work=The New York Times |date=10 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="Hill5">{{cite news |last1=Swanson |first1=Ian |title=Five ways the coronavirus could change American politics |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/campaign/495761-five-ways-the-coronavirus-could-change-american-politics |access-date=3 May 2020 |work=TheHill |date=2 May 2020 |language=en}}</ref><ref name="Ddn2P">{{cite web |url=https://www.bostonglobe.com/2020/03/13/opinion/americas-botched-response-coronavirus-is-problem-bigger-than-donald-trump/ |title=America's botched response to the coronavirus is a problem bigger than Donald Trump |website=[[Boston Globe]]}}</ref> Trump was also criticized of embracing medical populism, giving medical advice on Twitter and at press conferences.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Populism and COVID-19: Where Two Pandemics Meet|url=https://www.crossfirekm.org/articles/populism-and-covid-19-where-two-pandemics-meet|access-date=2020-06-30|website=Crossfire KM|language=en-US}}</ref> Political analysts anticipated it may negatively affect Donald Trump's chances of re-election in the [[2020 United States presidential election|2020 presidential election]].<ref name="TrumpChances">{{Cite news |last1=Haberman |first1=Maggie |last2=Martin |first2=Jonathan | name-list-style = vanc |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/12/us/politics/trump-vs-biden.html |title=Trump's Re-election Chances Suddenly Look Shakier |date=12 March 2020 |work=[[The New York Times]] |access-date=15 March 2020 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref><ref name="AtlanticChances">{{cite news |last1=Lowrey |first1=Annie |title=The Economy Is Collapsing. So Are Trump's Reelection Chances. |url=https://www.theatlantic.com/ideas/archive/2020/04/most-important-number-trumps-re-election-chances/609376/ |access-date=3 May 2020 |work=The Atlantic |date=3 April 2020}}</ref> Some state emergency orders have waived [[open meeting law]]s that require the public have physical access to the meeting location, allowing meetings to be held by public teleconference.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bostonglobe.com/2020/03/14/metro/local-governments-take-lead-collaborate-improvise-manage-crisis/ |title=Local governments take the lead, collaborate, and improvise to manage crisis |website=[[The Boston Globe]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.dailyfreeman.com/news/local-news/state-waives-some-provisions-of-open-meetings-law-amid-pandemic/article_a30667ac-6573-11ea-a3cf-07e97a9da6ec.html |title=State waives some provisions of Open Meetings Law amid pandemic concerns |first=William J. |last=Kemble |website=Daily Freeman}}</ref>

On 19 March, [[ProPublica]] published an article showing that Senator [[Richard Burr]] has sold between $628,000 and $1.7 million worth of stocks before the [[2020 stock market crash|stock market crash]] using [[2020 Congressional insider trading scandal|insider knowledge from a closed Senate meeting]] where Senators were briefed on how coronavirus could effect the United States. Stock transactions committed by Senators [[Dianne Feinstein]], [[Kelly Loeffler]], and [[Jim Inhofe]] were also placed under scrutiny for insider trading.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.npr.org/2020/03/19/818192535/burr-recording-sparks-questions-about-private-comments-on-covid-19?utm_campaign=storyshare&utm_source=twitter.com&utm_medium=social |title=Intelligence Chairman Raised Virus Alarms Weeks Ago, Secret Recording Shows |date=19 March 2020 |work=NPR |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320131233/https://www.npr.org/2020/03/19/818192535/burr-recording-sparks-questions-about-private-comments-on-covid-19 |archive-date=20 March 2020}}</ref> On 30 March, the Department of Justice imitated a probe into the stock transactions with the [[U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission|Securities and Exchange Commission]].<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/03/29/politics/justice-stock-trades-lawmakers-coronavirus/index.html |title=Exclusive: Justice Department reviews stock trades by lawmakers after coronavirus briefings |date=30 March 2020 |work=The Hill |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200331222559/https://www.cnn.com/2020/03/29/politics/justice-stock-trades-lawmakers-coronavirus/ |archive-date=31 March 2020}}</ref>

Captain [[Brett Crozier]] wrote a four-page memo requesting help for his crew, as a [[COVID-19 pandemic on USS Theodore Roosevelt|viral outbreak had occurred on board his ship]], the [[USS Theodore Roosevelt (CVN-71)|USS ''Theodore Roosevelt'']].<ref name=Bor-uno/><ref name=mac-ansq/> However, he was soon relieved from his command over the ship, because the memo was leaked to the public.<ref name=Bor-uno/><ref name=mac-ansq/> The Acting Navy Secretary [[Thomas Modly]] initially justified his actions to fire Crozier, saying that the captain was "too naive or too stupid" to be a commanding officer if he did not think that the information would get out to the public in this information age, but later issued an apology in which he acknowledged that Crozier intended to draw public attention to the circumstances on his ship.<ref name=Bor-uno>{{cite web |last1=Borger |first1=Julian |title=US navy official apologises for calling captain behind coronavirus memo 'naive or stupid' |url=https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2020/apr/06/navy-coronavirus-ship-theodore-roosevelt-thomas-modly |website=The Guardian |date=7 April 2020}}</ref><ref name=mac-ansq>{{cite web |last1=Macias |first1=Amanda |title=Acting Navy secretary quits after he ripped captain pleading for help over coronavirus |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2020/04/07/acting-navy-secretary-modly-quits-after-he-ripped-captain-pleading-for-help-over-coronavirus-outbreak-report-says.html |website=CNBC |date=7 April 2020}}</ref> Several members of Congress called for Modly's resignation for his handling of the situation,<ref name=Bor-uno/> which he did on 7 April.<ref name=mac-ansq/>

====State====
{{Main|U.S. state and local government responses to the COVID-19 pandemic}}

[[File: Open Ohio Rally IMG 0910 (49799974031).jpg|thumb|Several hundred anti-lockdown protesters rallied at the [[Ohio Statehouse]] 20 April.<ref name="Columbus Dispatch">{{cite news |last1=Rouan |first1=Rick |title=Protesters at Statehouse demand state reopen as DeWine announces schools to remain closed |url=https://www.dispatch.com/news/20200420/protesters-at-statehouse-demand-state-reopen-as-dewine-announces-schools-to-remain-closed |access-date=3 May 2020 |work=[[The Columbus Dispatch]] |date=20 April 2020 |language=en}}</ref>]]Multiple U.S. states suspended legislative activity including Colorado, Kentucky, Delaware, Georgia, Illinois, New Hampshire, and Vermont.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.ncsl.org/research/about-state-legislatures/coronavirus-and-state-legislatures-in-the-news.aspx |title=Coronavirus and State Legislatures in the News |date=13 March 2020 |work=NCSL |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314123927/https://www.ncsl.org/research/about-state-legislatures/coronavirus-and-state-legislatures-in-the-news.aspx |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://vtdigger.org/2020/03/13/legislature-to-temporarily-adjourn-due-to-coronavirus-concerns/ |title=Legislature to temporarily adjourn due to coronavirus concerns |date=13 March 2020 |work=NCSL |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314123913/https://vtdigger.org/2020/03/13/legislature-to-temporarily-adjourn-due-to-coronavirus-concerns/ |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nbcboston.com/news/local/seven-cases-coronavirus-new-hampshire-schools-close/2091229/ |title=7th Case of Coronavirus in NH as State House Suspends Legislative Activities for a Week |date=14 March 2020 |work=NBC |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200315014116/https://www.nbcboston.com/news/local/seven-cases-coronavirus-new-hampshire-schools-close/2091229/ |archive-date=15 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.courier-journal.com/story/news/2020/03/19/coronavirus-kentucky-general-assembly-temporarily-suspend/2879317001/ |title=Beshear rips into Senate budget proposal as Kentucky lawmakers hit pause on session |date=19 March 2020 |work=Courier Journal}}</ref>

On 11 March 2020, New Mexico Governor [[Michelle Lujan Grisham]] vetoed $150 million worth on infrastructure projects due to the state losing $22 million in its general fund for every $1 decrease in the price of a barrel of oil as a result of the [[2020 Russia–Saudi Arabia oil price war|Russia–Saudi Arabia oil price war]]. The Alaska Department of Revenue delayed its release of its budget forecast due to Alaska's dependence on oil prices.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.rollcall.com/2020/03/13/states-expecting-big-revenue-hit-as-covid-19-slows-the-economy/ |title=States expecting big revenue hit as COVID-19 slows the economy |date=13 March 2020 |work=Roll Call |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314000216/https://www.rollcall.com/2020/03/13/states-expecting-big-revenue-hit-as-covid-19-slows-the-economy/ |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref>

On 10 March, Georgia state senator [[Brandon Beach]] started showing symptoms of COVID-19 and was tested on 14 March. However, he attended a special session of the legislature on 16 March before his test results arrived on 18 March showing that he had tested positive. The entire Georgia state senate, their staffs, and Lieutenant Governor [[Geoff Duncan]] went into quarantine until 30 March.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/state-watch/488385-entire-georgia-legislature-urged-to-self-quarantine-after-senator-tests |title=Entire Georgia state legislature urged to self-quarantine after positive coronavirus test |date=19 March 2020 |work=Hill |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320053110/https://thehill.com/homenews/state-watch/488385-entire-georgia-legislature-urged-to-self-quarantine-after-senator-tests |archive-date=20 March 2020}}</ref>

Coronavirus restrictions also disrupted thousands of political campaigns across America, limiting the canvassing and in-person fundraising candidates have long-relied on to win office. Political insiders believe that could give incumbents a bigger advantage than normal.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Pransky |first1=Noah |title=Politicking in a Pandemic |url=https://www.lx.com/politics/throw-out-the-playbook-candidates-have-had-to-adapt-on-the-fly-politicking-in-a-pandemic/17852/ |access-date=19 August 2020 |agency=NBCLX |publisher=NBCLX |date=19 August 2020}}</ref>

=== Venezuela ===
{{See also|Negotiations during the Venezuelan crisis}}
[[Reuters]] reported that during the pandemic, allies of both [[Nicolás Maduro]] and [[Juan Guaidó]] had secretly begun exploratory talks, according to sources on both sides.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-venezuela-politics-idUSKCN2232NX|title=Exclusive: Venezuela Socialists, opposition leaders begin secret talks amid pandemic – sources|date=21 April 2020|work=[[Reuters]]|access-date=21 April 2020|language=en}}</ref> Guaidó and [[Ambassadors of the United States|U.S. Special Representative]] for [[2019 Venezuelan presidential crisis|Venezuela]] [[Elliott Abrams]] have denied that negotiations have taken place.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://efectococuyo.com/politica/guaido-no-hay-ningun-tipo-de-negociacion-o-mediacion-con-regimen-de-maduro/|title=Guaidó: No hay ningún tipo de negociación o mediación con régimen de Maduro|date=23 April 2020|website=[[Efecto Cocuyo]]|language=es|access-date=25 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://elpitazo.net/politica/elliot-abrams-no-existe-negociacion-entre-oposicion-y-el-oficialismo/|title=Elliott Abrams: No existe negociación entre oposición y el oficialismo|last=Batiz|first=César|date=22 April 2020|website=[[El Pitazo]]|language=es|access-date=25 April 2020}}</ref>

==Impact on elections==
===Bolivia===

On 21 March 2020, President [[Jeanine Áñez]] announced the interim government's decision to postpone the [[2020 Bolivian general election|snap election]]. Other presidential candidates had suggested postponing the election to prevent the spread of coronavirus through the congregation of large groups of people.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.france24.com/en/20200321-bolivia-delays-presidential-elections-mandates-14-day-quarantine-against-virus |title=Bolivia delays presidential elections, mandates 14-day quarantine against virus |date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200405223510/https://www.france24.com/en/20200321-bolivia-delays-presidential-elections-mandates-14-day-quarantine-against-virus |archive-date=5 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.outlookindia.com/newsscroll/electoral-court-postpones-bolivia-general-election-over-virus/1775807 |title=Electoral court postpones Bolivia general election over virus |date=22 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200405223630/https://www.outlookindia.com/newsscroll/electoral-court-postpones-bolivia-general-election-over-virus/1775807 |archive-date=5 April 2020}}</ref>

===Chile===

A [[2020 Chilean national plebiscite|plebiscite]] on a new constitution and the convention that would write it was scheduled on 25 April, but on 19 March, political parties reached an agreement on postponing the plebiscite to 25 October.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cooperativa.cl/noticias/pais/politica/constitucion/acuerdo-politico-por-elecciones-del-2020-plebiscito-se-postergara-para/2020-03-19/155155.html |title=Acuerdo político por elecciones del 2020: Plebiscito se postergará para el 25 de octubre |work=Cooperativa |date=23 March 2020 }}</ref> This agreement also postponed municipal and regional elections, from 25 October to 4 April 2021, with the primaries and second rounds of elections being postponed too.{{citation needed|date=March 2020}}

===Dominican Republic===

On April 13, 2020, the electoral body of Dominican Republic decided to postpone the presidential and legislative elections which were originally scheduled for May 17 of the same year. The new selected date was July 5, 2020, and, in case none of the presidential candidates reached the absolute majority (50% + 1 vote), the second round will be held on July 26.<ref>{{cite web |title=Resolución 042-2020 sobre posposición a causa de fuerza mayor por emergencia sanitaria de las elecciones ordinarias generales presidenciales y legislativas del 17 de mayo |url=https://jce.gob.do/DesktopModules/Bring2mind/DMX/Download.aspx?EntryId=17643&Command=Core_Download&language=es-ES&PortalId=1&TabId=190}}</ref>

===Ethiopia===

On 31 March, the National Electoral Board of Ethiopia delayed the [[2020 Ethiopian general election|House of Representatives elections]] that were originally scheduled for 29 August, due to the outbreak of coronavirus in Ethiopia.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.fanabc.com/english/nebe-says-impossible-to-hold-election-as-per-scheduled-due-to-covid-19/|title=NEBE Says Impossible To Hold Election As Per Scheduled Due To COVID-19|date=31 March 2020|work=fanabc.com|access-date=1 April 2020|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200522035630/https://www.fanabc.com/english/nebe-says-impossible-to-hold-election-as-per-scheduled-due-to-covid-19/|archive-date=22 May 2020}}</ref>

===France===

President [[Emmanuel Macron]] declared coronavirus as the "biggest health crisis in a century". On 12 March he stated that the first round of [[2020 French municipal elections|local elections]] would not be rescheduled.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-51862828 |title=France's Macron defies coronavirus lockdown with elections |date=13 March 2020 |work=BBC |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314013943/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-51862828 |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> The choice to maintain the elections, which took place on 15 March, generated significant controversy.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.liberation.fr/politiques/2020/03/14/le-maintien-des-municipales-de-plus-en-plus-polemique_1781718 |title=Le maintien des municipales fait de plus en plus polémique |work=Libération |date=14 March 2020 }}</ref> On 16 March, he stated that the second round, originally scheduled for 22 March, would be delayed until 21 June.<ref>{{Cite news |url=http://www.leparisien.fr/elections/municipales/coronavirus-vers-un-report-du-second-tour-des-municipales-au-21-juin-16-03-2020-8281371.php |title=Coronavirus : le second tour des municipales reporté |work=Le Parisien|date=16 March 2020 }}</ref>

===Hong Kong===
{{main|Postponement of the 2020 Hong Kong legislative election}}
The 2020 Hong Kong Legislative Council election was originally scheduled on 6 September 2020 until it was postponed by the government for a whole year to [[2021 Hong Kong legislative election|5 September 2021]]. On 31 July 2020, [[Chief Executive of Hong Kong|Chief Executive]] [[Carrie Lam]] announced that she was invoking the [[Emergency Regulations Ordinance]] to postpone the election under its emergency powers, citing the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Hong Kong|recent resurgence of the COVID-19 cases]], adding that the move was supported by Beijing.<ref name="govtstat">{{cite news|title=LegCo General Election postponed for a year|url=https://www.info.gov.hk/gia/general/202007/31/P2020073100898p.htm|date=2020-07-31|work=Hong Kong Government}}</ref>

===Indonesia===
The [[2020 Indonesian local elections]] were scheduled to be held on 23 September was postponed, and the Indonesian [[General Elections Commission]] proposed postponement to 9 December at the earliest, which was then approved by the [[People's Representative Council]] and then signed into law by President [[Joko Widodo]] on 5 May. The election's previous budget of around US$550 million was reallocated towards pandemic management and control.<ref>{{cite news |title=Govt, House agree to reschedule 2020 regional elections' voting day to Dec. 9 |url=https://www.thejakartapost.com/news/2020/04/15/govt-house-agree-to-reschedule-2020-regional-elections-voting-day-to-dec-9.html |access-date=10 May 2020 |work=The Jakarta Post |date=15 April 2020 |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Prasetia |first1=Andhika |title=Jokowi Resmi Terbitkan Perppu, Pilkada 2020 Digeser ke Desember |url=https://news.detik.com/berita/d-5003710/jokowi-resmi-terbitkan-perppu-pilkada-2020-digeser-ke-desember |access-date=10 May 2020 |work=detiknews |date=5 May 2020 |language=id-ID}}</ref>

===Italy===

A [[2020 Italian constitutional referendum|referendum]] on a constitutional amendment to decrease the number of members of parliament from 630 to 400 in the [[Chamber of Deputies (Italy)|Chamber]] and from 315 to 200 in the [[Senate of the Republic (Italy)|Senate]] was initially scheduled to be held on 29 March, but was postponed to 20 and 21 September following the outbreak of the virus in Italy.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.interno.gov.it/it/notizie/rinviato-referendum-29-marzo-sul-taglio-dei-parlamentari |title=inviato il referendum del 29 marzo sul taglio dei parlamentari |access-date=15 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314100154/https://www.interno.gov.it/it/notizie/rinviato-referendum-29-marzo-sul-taglio-dei-parlamentari |archive-date=14 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>
<ref>{{cite web|url=https://dait.interno.gov.it/elezioni/notizie/decreto-di-indizione-del-referendum-per-riduzione-dei-parlamentari|title=Decreto di indizione del referendum per la riduzione dei parlamentari|access-date=19 August 2020}}</ref>

===Kiribati===

The first round of the [[2020 Kiribati parliamentary election|parliamentary elections]] was originally planned to be held on 7 April 2020, but was later moved to 15 April, with the second round planned for the next week due to the coronavirus pandemic although there were no cases in the country at the time.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/international/pacific-news/411125/kiribati-to-go-to-polls-for-elections-in-april |title=Kiribati to go to polls for elections in April |access-date=6 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200410113923/https://www.rnz.co.nz/international/pacific-news/411125/kiribati-to-go-to-polls-for-elections-in-april |archive-date=10 April 2020 |url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/international/pacific-news/413994/delayed-start-for-kiribati-elections |title=Delayed start for Kiribati elections |access-date=10 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200410114020/https://www.rnz.co.nz/international/pacific-news/413994/delayed-start-for-kiribati-elections |archive-date=10 April 2020 |url-status=live}}</ref>

===Latvia===

On 6 April 2020, [[minister-president]] [[Krišjānis Kariņš]] announced the government's decision to postpone the snap Rīga City Council's elections. Originally, the snap elections were scheduled for 25 April, and election posters had already started appearing, but as the COVID-19 crisis broke out, the elections were rescheduled for 6 June, without ruling out a possibility to move the election date closer to the fall, reported the LETA newswire. Krišjānis Kariņš said: "Considering the uncertainty regarding the COVID-19 crisis, most probably, we will move the elections to the beginning of September."<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://eng.lsm.lv/article/politics/politics/riga-municipal-elections-postponed-until-september.a354925/|title=Rīga municipal elections postponed until September|website=eng.lsm.lv}}</ref>

===New Zealand===

On 17 August 2020, [[Prime Minister of New Zealand|Prime Minister]] [[Jacinda Ardern]] announced that the [[2020 New Zealand general election|upcoming election]] would be delayed by almost 4 weeks from September 19 to October 17. The country's biggest city, [[Auckland]], had seen a recent rise in cases of COVID-19 and was placed on a restrictive 3 week lockdown. Due to safety concerns and an inability for political parties to campaign properly, Ardern agreed to a call from opposition and government parties to delay the election.

===Philippines===
{{further|COVID-19 pandemic in Mimaropa|2020 Palawan partition plebiscite}}
On 10 March 2020, the [[Commission on Elections (Philippines)|Commission on Elections]] (COMELEC) suspended nationwide voter registration until the end of the month due to the COVID-19 pandemic. The registration period began 20 January and is scheduled to run until 30 September 2021.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Patinio |first1=Ferdinand |title=Comelec suspends voter registration amid Covid-19 threat |url=https://www.pna.gov.ph/articles/1096013 |access-date=27 March 2020 |agency=Philippine News Agency |date=9 March 2020}}</ref> The suspension was later extended to last until the end of April. The issuance of voter's certification is also suspended until further notice. The next nationwide elections scheduled in the Philippines is in [[2022 Philippine presidential election|May 2022]].<ref>{{cite news |title=COMELEC extends suspension of voter registration to April 30 |url=https://cnnphilippines.com/news/2020/3/27/comelec-extends-suspension-voter-registration-april-30.html |access-date=27 March 2020 |work=CNN Philippines |date=27 April 2020}}</ref>

The [[2020 Palawan partition plebiscite|plebiscite]] to ratify legislation which proposes the partition of [[Palawan]] into three smaller provinces scheduled for May 2020 may be delayed due to the COVID-19 pandemic. The province provincial legislature has called for a special session and is expected to pass a resolution allowing their governor to ask the COMELEC to postpone the plebiscite.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Magdayao |first1=Aira Genesa |title=Postponement of Palawan division plebiscite sought |url=https://palawan-news.com/postponement-of-palawan-division-plebiscite-sought/ |access-date=27 March 2020 |work=Palawan News Online |date=26 March 2020}}</ref>

===Poland===

Initially the Polish government chose to not delay the [[2020 Polish presidential election|presidential election]], a decision which caused controversy.<ref name=":4">{{Cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/europe/2020/04/16/a-postal-vote-in-poland-could-entrench-populists|title=A postal vote in Poland could entrench populists|work=The Economist|access-date=20 April 2020|issn=0013-0613}}</ref> Polling has shown 78% of the population to prefer postponing the election.<ref name=":4" /> The opposition to the ruling party [[Law and Justice]] has argued that the pandemic conditions prevent effective campaigning, and hence reduce the competitiveness of the election.<ref name=":4" /> On 27 March, some candidates for the presidential election failed to collect 100,000 signatures due to the coronavirus pandemic with only twelve presidential candidates having successfully collected over 100,000 signatures. Seven candidates submitted petitions with less than 100,000 signatures, but plan to appeal the central election commission's refusal to register them in the presidential election citing the coronavirus pandemic hampering the signature collection process.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.urdupoint.com/en/world/most-polish-presidential-candidates-fail-to-c-876183.html |title=Most Polish Presidential Candidates Fail To Collect Signatures Due To COVID-19 – Reports |date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200328192548/https://www.urdupoint.com/en/world/most-polish-presidential-candidates-fail-to-c-876183.html |archive-date=28 March 2020}}</ref>

A change to Poland's election laws was proposed to allow postal voting for those over 60 and those under quarantine but not abroad, which was criticized as favoring the incumbent Law and Justice Party.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2020/03/29/polands-coronavirus-crisis-election-unleashes-political-warfare-154852|title=Poland's coronavirus-crisis election unleashes political warfare|website=POLITICO|language=en|access-date=2 April 2020}}</ref> Laws under discussion by parliament in mid-April define the entire [[Postal voting|vote to be postal]] and weaken the role of the electoral commission, despite postal workers unions saying this would be impossible.<ref name=":4" />

On 6 May, the Polish governing coalition announced the presidential election would be postponed due to the pandemic.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://apnews.com/908a36d593e86ae089a2f717371e99c9|title=Polish ruling coalition postpones Sunday presidential vote|date=6 May 2020|website=AP NEWS}}</ref> On 3 June 2020 [[Marshal of the Sejm]] [[Elżbieta Witek]] announced that first round of the delayed election would occur on 28 June 2020, with 12 July 2020 scheduled for the runoff, if it is necessary.<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-06-03|title=Poland's postponed presidential election to be held June 28|url=https://apnews.com/39e5b76457ce8db4d69ac39bf8c89f93|access-date=2020-06-08|website=AP NEWS}}</ref>

===Russia===

On 25 March, President [[Vladimir Putin]] announced the postponement of the [[2020 Russian constitutional referendum|constitutional referendum]] scheduled for 22 April to a later date. At the moment, a new date for the referendum has not yet been determined.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.kommersant.ru/doc/4301235 |title=Путин перенес голосование по Конституции из-за коронавируса|date=25 March 2020|website=Коммерсантъ|language=ru|access-date=3 May 2020}}</ref>

Also, the [[Central Election Commission of Russia|Central Election Commission]] postponed about a hundred local elections scheduled for the period from 29 March to 21 June.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.kommersant.ru/doc/4314450 |title=Коронавирус перенес выборы|date=3 April 2020|website=Коммерсантъ|language=ru|access-date=3 May 2020}}</ref>

Regional elections in more than 20 regions are due to be held on a "single election day" on 13 September. However, the campaign must start no later than 15 June. According to media reports, depending on the epidemiological situation, the Federal government allows the postponement of a single election day to December 2020 or the holding of these regional elections on a 2021 single election day.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.vedomosti.ru/politics/news/2020/05/05/829594-edinomu-dnyu-golosovaniya |title=В ЦИК назвали допустимые сроки кампании по единому дню голосования|date=5 May 2020|website=Ведомости|language=ru|access-date=5 May 2020}}</ref>

===Serbia===

On 16 March 2020, the electoral commission postponed the [[2020 Serbian parliamentary election|parliamentary election]] that was initially planned for 26 April.<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-03-16|title=Serbia Delays Elections After Virus Triggers Emergency|url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-03-16/serbia-delays-elections-after-virus-triggers-state-of-emergency|access-date=2020-09-24|website=Bloomberg.com}}</ref>

=== Singapore ===
The [[2020 Singaporean general election]] was held on 10 July 2020. The Elections Department had rolled out a series of measures in response to the pandemic to ensure that the elections can be held. No rallies and TV screenings pertaining to the election are to be held. Nomination centres will not admit members of the public and walkabouts, though allowed, should have safe distancing and minimal physical contact. Candidates are also not be allowed to make speeches, including during the campaigning, from campaigning vehicles, meaning that there will be no parades by the candidates held post-election.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Rules out: A Phase 2 general election will have no physical rallies, no screenings at coffee shops|url=https://mothership.sg/2020/06/general-election-in-phase-2/|access-date=2020-06-18|website=mothership.sg|language=en}}</ref>

===Spain===

The [[2020 Basque regional election]], scheduled for 5 April, were delayed, after an agreement between all the political parties represented in the Basque parliament; the [[2020 Galician regional election|Galician elections]] were also suspended.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://elpais.com/espana/2020-03-16/urkullu-aplaza-las-elecciones-vascas-hasta-superar-la-crisis-del-coronavirus.html|title=Urkullu aplaza las elecciones vascas hasta superar la crisis del coronavirus|last=Gorospe|first=Pedro|date=16 March 2020|website=EL PAÍS|language=es|access-date=16 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://elpais.com/espana/2020-03-16/urkullu-aplaza-las-elecciones-vascas-hasta-superar-la-crisis-del-coronavirus.html|title=Galicia y País Vasco aplazan las elecciones hasta superar la crisis del coronavirus|last=Vizoso|first=Pedro Gorospe, Sonia|date=16 March 2020|website=EL PAÍS|language=es|access-date=16 March 2020}}</ref>

===Sri Lanka===

On 19 March, Election Commissioner [[Mahinda Deshapriya]] announced that the [[2020 Sri Lankan parliamentary election]] will be postponed indefinitely until further notice due to the coronavirus pandemic.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://newsin.asia/sri-lankas-general-election-postponed/|title=Sri Lanka's General Election postponed till country is freed from COVID-19|date=19 March 2020|website=NewsIn.Asia|language=en-US|access-date=19 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.asiantribune.com/node/93497|title=Sri Lanka's General Election postponed: Until the polls Country comes under Election Commission {{!}} Asian Tribune|website=asiantribune.com|access-date=19 March 2020}}</ref> Sri Lankan President [[Gotabaya Rajapaksa]] initially insisted that scheduled forthcoming the election would proceed as planned on 25 April despite the coronavirus pandemic, and the authorities banned election rallies and meetings.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://colombogazette.com/2020/03/15/president-tells-saarc-leaders-april-election-will-go-ahead/|title=President tells SAARC leaders April election will go ahead|date=15 March 2020|website=Colombo Gazette|language=en-GB|access-date=16 March 2020}}</ref>

===Syria===

The [[2020 Syrian parliamentary election|parliamentary elections]] originally scheduled for 13 April were delayed to 20 May to protect Syria from coronavirus.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://news.yahoo.com/syria-elections-postponed-over-coronavirus-183333853.html|title=Syria elections postponed over coronavirus|date=14 March 2020|work=Yahoo News|access-date=1 April 2020}}</ref>

===Trinidad and Tobago===

The [[2020 Trinidad and Tobago general election|general election]] originally scheduled for September might be delayed but "will be held when constitutionally due" despite the coronavirus.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.looptt.com/content/pm-general-election-must-adhere-covid-19-rules|title=PM: General election must adhere to COVID-19 rules
