|date=28 May 2020|work=Loop News|access-date=28 May 2020}}</ref> Pre-campaigning was partially suspended on 13 March following news of the first reported case of [[2020 coronavirus pandemic in Trinidad and Tobago|COVID-19 in Trinidad and Tobago]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Political parties halt activities over covid19 |url=https://newsday.co.tt/2020/03/14/political-parties-halt-activities-over-covid19/ |access-date=15 March 2020 |work=Trinidad and Tobago Newsday |date=14 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Two major parties put election campaigning on hold |url=https://trinidadexpress.com/news/local/two-major-parties-put-election-campaigning-on-hold/article_c5ec536a-6593-11ea-8e9f-bf713f154ca5.html |access-date=15 March 2020 |work=Trinidad Express Newspapers |language=en}}</ref>

===United Kingdom===

On 13 March 2020, the [[2021 United Kingdom local elections|United Kingdom local elections]] that were meant to be held on 7 May were rescheduled by Prime Minister [[Boris Johnson]] to 6 May 2021 following the advice of the [[Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)|Electoral Commission]] and in agreement with [[Labour Party (UK)|Labour]] and the [[Liberal Democrats (UK)|Liberal Democrats]].<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-51876269 |title=Coronavirus: English local elections postponed for a year |date=13 March 2020 |work=BBC |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200313194513/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-51876269 |archive-date=13 March 2020}}</ref>

On 27 March, the [[Liberal Democrats (UK)|Liberal Democrats]] postponed their [[2021 Liberal Democrats leadership election|leadership election]], at first to May 2021, before moving it back to July 2020.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-52062239|title=Lib Dems suspend leadership contest until 2021|work=BBC News|date=27 March 2020|access-date=28 March 2020}}</ref>

===United States===
{{Anchor|Election impacts on the United States}} 

====Presidential====
{{Main|2020 United States presidential election}}
[[File:Electionsaltered.svg|thumb|right|States with at least one local, state, or federal primary election date or method of voting altered as of August 5, 2020.]]

=====Campaign=====

Political campaigns switched to online and virtual activities in mid-March to either avoid the spreading of coronavirus or to be in compliance with statewide social distancing rules.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.marketwatch.com/story/2020-presidential-campaigns-go-digital-during-coronavirus-outbreak-2020-03-20 |title=2020 presidential campaigns go digital during coronavirus outbreak |date=20 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403201145/https://www.marketwatch.com/story/2020-presidential-campaigns-go-digital-during-coronavirus-outbreak-2020-03-20 |archive-date=3 April 2020}}</ref> Former [[Vice President of the United States|Vice President]] [[Joe Biden]] and [[United States Senate|Senator]] [[Bernie Sanders]] started giving online town halls and virtual fundraisers.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.npr.org/2020/03/25/820741876/a-grounded-biden-campaign-is-trying-to-reach-voters-in-the-cloud |title=A Grounded Biden Campaign Is Trying To Reach Voters In The Cloud |date=25 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403201747/https://www.npr.org/2020/03/25/820741876/a-grounded-biden-campaign-is-trying-to-reach-voters-in-the-cloud |archive-date=3 April 2020}}</ref> President [[Donald Trump]]'s presidential campaign also shifted from in-person to virtual campaigning due to stay-at-home orders and social distancing rules made after his 2 March rally and both his and other Republican leadership offices based in Virginia were closed due to stay-at-home orders issued by Governor [[Ralph Northam]].<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.npr.org/2020/04/02/825467802/with-rallies-off-the-table-trumps-reelection-moves-to-virtual-campaigning |title=His Signature Rallies Are Off, So Here's How Trump's Campaign Has Moved Online |date=2 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403202343/https://www.npr.org/2020/04/02/825467802/with-rallies-off-the-table-trumps-reelection-moves-to-virtual-campaigning |archive-date=3 April 2020}}</ref>

On 15 March, the first one-on-one debate of the [[2020 Democratic presidential primaries]] took place between Joe Biden and Bernie Sanders in [[CNN]]'s [[Washington, D.C.]] studios and without an audience, as a result of the ongoing [[COVID-19 pandemic in the United States|COVID-19 pandemic]]. The debate was moved from [[Arizona]], which is under a state of emergency and had 12 confirmed cases of COVID-19 on that date.<ref>[https://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-usa-election/amid-coronavirus-crisis-biden-and-sanders-go-head-to-head-in-democratic-debate-idUKKBN2120DK Results or revolution? Biden, Sanders present dueling visions while blasting Trump's coronavirus response] Reuters, 16 March 2020</ref><ref>[https://www.livescience.com/coronavirus-arizona.html Arizona: Latest updates on coronavirus] ''Live Science'', 15 March 2020</ref>

On 2 April, the [[2020 Democratic National Convention|Democratic National Convention]], which was originally scheduled to be held from 13 to 16 July, was delayed to the week of 17 August after the Democratic National Committee communicated with the presidential campaigns of [[Joe Biden]] and [[Bernie Sanders]].<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/04/02/politics/dnc-postponed-coronavirus/index.html |title=Democratic National Convention pushed back to August |date=2 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200402234044/https://www.cnn.com/2020/04/02/politics/dnc-postponed-coronavirus/ |archive-date=2 April 2020}}</ref> On 5 April Biden suggested  "a virtual convention" may be necessary;<ref>[https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2020-election/biden-suggests-democrats-hold-virtual-convention-amid-coronavirus-crisis-n1177076 Biden suggests Democrats may hold 'virtual convention' amid coronavirus crisis] NBC News, 5 April 2020</ref> Trump told Fox News' [[Sean Hannity]] there was "no way" he would cancel the [[2020 Republican National Convention|Republican National convention]], scheduled to begin on 24 August in Charlotte, NC.<ref>[https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2020-election/trump-biden-trade-barbs-over-possible-virtual-democratic-convention-n1177656 Trump, Biden trade barbs over possible virtual Democratic convention] By Adam Edelman, NBC News, 6 April 2020</ref>

House Speaker [[Nancy Pelosi]] (D-CA) and Senators [[Amy Klobuchar]] (D-MN) and [[Ron Wyden]] (D-OR) expressed concern in early April that the pandemic might lower voter turnout in November. Closings of churches, universities, and driver's license centers will make it more difficult for voters to register and the Democracy Project at the [[Brennan Center for Justice]] expect turnout to be low, as it was during the 17 March [[2020 Illinois Democratic primary|Illinois Democratic primary]]. Georgia state House Speaker David Ralston (R), predicted that mailing absentee ballot request forms to all voters in the state during the coronavirus crisis would be "devastating" for GOP candidates, and President Trump said that some of the election reforms would make it harder for Republicans to win office.<ref>[https://thehill.com/homenews/house/490944-democrats-fear-coronavirus-impact-on-november-turnout Democrats fear coronavirus impact on November turnout] The Hill, 3 April 2020</ref>

There have been calls to postpone the 2020 U.S. presidential election to 2021, but many constitutional scholars, lawmakers have said it would be very difficult to do without amending the Constitution.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.bostonglobe.com/2020/04/03/nation/can-president-cancel-2020-election-over-coronavirus/|title=Can the president cancel the 2020 election over coronavirus? – The Boston Globe|website=BostonGlobe.com}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.vox.com/2020/3/21/21188152/trump-cancel-november-election-constitution-coronavirus |title=Can Trump cancel the November election because of coronavirus? |publisher=Vox |date=7 April 2020 |access-date=21 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/opinion/2020/03/26/coronavirus-pandemic-trump-cannot-cancel-2020-election-column/2898418001/ |title=Trump can't cancel the 2020 election, even in a coronavirus pandemic |publisher=Usatoday.com |access-date=21 April 2020}}</ref>

=====Primaries=====

{{update|date=April 2020}}
On 12 March 2020, the [[North Dakota Democratic–Nonpartisan League Party|North Dakota Democratic-NPL]] cancelled its state convention that was meant to be held from 19 to 22 March where statewide candidates would have been nominated and delegates to the [[2020 Democratic National Convention|Democratic National Convention]] would have been selected.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.inforum.com/news/government-and-politics/4995662-ND-Dem-NPL-cancels-state-convention-due-to-virus-concerns-Republicans-going-ahead-for-now |title=ND Dem-NPL cancels state convention due to virus concerns; Republicans going ahead for now |date=12 March 2020 |work=Inforum |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314122351/https://www.inforum.com/news/government-and-politics/4995662-ND-Dem-NPL-cancels-state-convention-due-to-virus-concerns-Republicans-going-ahead-for-now |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> On 13 March, the presidential primary [[2020 Louisiana Democratic primary|in Louisiana]] was postponed to 20 June by Secretary of State [[Kyle Ardoin]] and [[2020 Wyoming Democratic caucuses|Wyoming]] had its in-person portion of its caucus and all county conventions suspended and replaced with mail-in ballots.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2020/03/13/louisiana-postpones-democratic-primary-over-coronavirus-the-first-state-to-do-so.html |title=Louisiana postpones Democratic primary over coronavirus, the first state to do so |date=13 March 2020 |work=CNBC |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200313235821/https://www.cnbc.com/2020/03/13/louisiana-postpones-democratic-primary-over-coronavirus-the-first-state-to-do-so.html |archive-date=13 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://k2radio.com/wyoming-democratic-party-suspends-in-person-caucus-conventions/ |title=WYOMING DEMOCRATIC PARTY SUSPENDS IN-PERSON CAUCUS, CONVENTIONS |date=13 March 2020 |work=K2 Radio |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314000534/https://k2radio.com/wyoming-democratic-party-suspends-in-person-caucus-conventions/ |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref>

On 14 March, the presidential primary in [[2020 Georgia Democratic primary|Georgia]] was moved from 24 March to 19 May;<ref>{{Cite news |url=http://ballot-access.org/2020/03/14/georgia-moves-presidential-primary-from-march-24-to-may-19/ |title=Georgia Moves Presidential Primary from March 24 to May 19 |date=14 March 2020 |work=Ballot March 2020}}</ref> on 9 April, the entire primary was again moved to 9 June.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.ajc.com/news/state--regional-govt--politics/georgia-primary-delayed-again-june-during-coronavirus-emergency/W5ElsYWTsP5clpNAVTYXnO/|title=Georgia primary delayed again to June 9 during coronavirus emergency|first1=Mark|last1=Niesse|first2=The Atlanta|last2=Journal-Constitution|website=ajc}}</ref> On 16 March, Secretary of State [[Michael Adams (Kentucky politician)|Michael Adams]] announced that the [[2020 Kentucky Democratic primary|Kentucky primaries]] would be moved from 19 May to 23 June and Governor [[Mike DeWine]] postponed the [[2020 Ohio Democratic primary|Ohio primaries]] despite legal challenges.<ref>{{Cite news |url=http://ballot-access.org/2020/03/16/kentucky-moves-primary-for-all-office-from-may-19-to-june-23/ |title=Kentucky Moves Primary for All Office from May 19 to June 23 |date=17 March 2020 |work=Ballot Access News |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200317112527/http://ballot-access.org/2020/03/16/kentucky-moves-primary-for-all-office-from-may-19-to-june-23/ |archive-date=17 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite 2020}}</ref> On 19 March, Governor [[Ned Lamont]] moved the [[2020 Connecticut Democratic primary|Connecticut Democratic primary]] from 28 April to 2 June.<ref>{{Cite news |url=http://ballot-access.org/2020/03/19/connecticut-postpones-presidential-primary-from-april-28-to-june-2/ |title=Connecticut Postpones Presidential Primary from April 28 to June 2 |date=19 March 20 March, Indiana Governor [[Eric Holcomb]], Secretary of State [[Connie Lawson]], Republican state chairman Kyle Hupfer, and Democratic state chairman [[John Zody]] announced that Indiana's primaries were rescheduled from 5 May to 2 June.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://wsbt.com/news/local/watch-live-governor-state-officials-to-give-update-on-indianas-primary-election |title=Governor announces Indiana primary moved from May 5 to June 2 |date=20 March 2020 |url-status=live On 21 March, Governor [[Wanda Vázquez Garced]] postponed the Puerto Rico [[2020 Puerto Rico Democratic primary|presidential primary]] from 29 March to 26 April. The [[Alaska Democratic Party]] canceled in-person voting for its [[2020 Alaska Democratic primary|presidential primary]] and extended its mail-in voting time to 10 April. Governor [[John Carney (politician)|John Carney]] postponed the Delaware [[2020 Delaware Democratic primary|presidential primary]] from 28 April to 2 June. The [[Democratic Party of Hawaii]] canceled in-person voting for its [[2020 Hawaii Democratic primary|presidential primary]] and delayed it from 4 April to sometime in May. Governor [[Gina Raimondo]] postponed the Rhode Island [[2020 Rhode Island Democratic primary|presidential primary]] at the request of the board of elections from 28 April to 2 June.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2020/03/20/state-elections-primaries-changes-coronavirus-138393 |title=Which states are changing their primaries over coronavirus |date=24 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200325110749/https://www.politico.com/news/2020/03/20/state-elections-primaries-changes-coronavirus-138393 |archive-date=25 March 2020}}</ref> On 27 March, Governor [[Tom Wolf]] signed into law legislation passed by the state legislature to postpone Pennsylvania's primaries from 28 April to 2 June.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://temple-news.com/pennsylvania-primary-postponed-to-june-amid-covid-19-outbreak/ |title=Pennsylvania primary postponed to June amid COVID-19 outbreak |date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327161536/https://temple-news.com/pennsylvania-primary-postponed-to-june-amid-covid-19-outbreak/ |archive-date=27 March 2020}}</ref> On 28 March, Governor [[Andrew Cuomo]] announced at a news conference that New York's [[2020 New York Democratic primary|presidential primary]] would be postponed from 28 April to 23 June.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/03/28/politics/cuomo-new-york-presidential-primary/index.html |title=New York Gov. Andrew Cuomo moves state's presidential primary |date=28 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200328191724/https://www.cnn.com/2020/03/28/politics/cuomo-new-york-presidential-primary/ |archive-date=28 March 2020}}</ref> On 8 April, Governor [[Phil Murphy]] signed an executive order to reschedule the primary election scheduled to be held on 2 June to 7 July.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nj.com/coronavirus/2020/04/murphy-officially-postpones-njs-primary-elections-to-july-due-to-coronavirus-outbreak.html|first1=Brent|last1=Johnson|title=Murphy officially postpones N.J.'s primary elections to July due to coronavirus outbreak|publisher=Advance Local Media LLC|date=8 April 2020|website=NJ.com}}</ref>

On 30 March, the Kansas Democratic Party announced that its [[2020 Kansas Democratic primary|presidential primary]] would be conducted only through mail-in ballots, and Governor [[Brad Little]] and Secretary of State [[Lawerence Denney]] also announced that Idaho's primary elections would also be conducted entirety through mail-in ballots.<ref>{{Cite news |url=http://www.kake.com/story/41953325/kansas-democratic-presidential-primaries-move-to-mail-in-only-cancel-in-person-voting |title=Kansas Democratic presidential primaries move to mail-in only, cancel in-person voting |date=30 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404203658/http://www.kake.com/story/41953325/kansas-democratic-presidential-primaries-move-to-mail-in-only-cancel-in-person-voting |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.krem.com/article/news/politics/idahocovidvoting/293-19f96702-993c-484b-b35f-fc50d67e9279 |title=Idaho primary will be conducted completely by mail |date=1 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404203653/https://www.krem.com/article/news/politics/idahocovidvoting/293-19f96702-993c-484b-b35f-fc50d67e9279 |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref> On 1 April, Governor [[Jim Justice]] signed an executive order to postpone West Virginia's primaries from 12 May to 9 June.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://governor.wv.gov/News/press-releases/2020/Pages/COVID-19-UPDATE-Gov.-Justice-signs-executive-order-to-move-Primary-Election-to-June-9-after-consultation-with-Attorney-Gen.aspx |title=COVID-19 UPDATE: Gov. Justice signs executive order to move Primary Election to June 9 after consultation with Attorney General, Secretary of State |date=1 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404204147/https://governor.wv.gov/News/press-releases/2020/Pages/COVID-19-UPDATE-Gov.-Justice-signs-executive-order-to-move-Primary-Election-to-June-9-after-consultation-with-Attorney-Gen.aspx |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref>

Polling places in Florida, Ohio, Illinois and Arizona that were located in senior living facilities were moved and other health precautions were enacted.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/states-scramble-move-polling-places-nursing-homes-stock/story?id=69587292 |title=Polling places moved from nursing homes; other changes amid coronavirus concerns |date=13 March 2020 |work=The Baltimore Sun |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314052301/https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/states-scramble-move-polling-places-nursing-homes-stock/story?id=69587292 |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> Local election directors in Maryland asked for the [[2020 Maryland Democratic primary|state's primary]] to be changed to only use mail-in ballots and former [[United States Deputy Secretary of the Treasury|Deputy Secretary of the Treasury]] [[Mary J. Miller]] asked for Governor [[Larry Hogan]] to switch to mail-in ballots.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.baltimoresun.com/coronavirus/bs-md-pol-mail-in-vote-20200313-asebi2ahqfab7a7yxhnoayy22a-story.html |title=Officials urge Maryland to hold mail-in only primary because of coronavirus |date=13 March 2020 |work=The Baltimore Sun |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314052304/https://www.baltimoresun.com/coronavirus/bs-md-pol-mail-in-vote-20200313-asebi2ahqfab7a7yxhnoayy22a-story.html |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref>

====State====
=====Campaign=====

Thirty-four Democratic and Republican candidates in New York signed a petition asking Governor [[Andrew Cuomo]] for the primary petition signature amounts to be decreased or eliminated for the primaries to prevent spreading or contracting the virus during signature collection.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://bklyner.com/state-congressional-candidates-sign-petition-to-stop-petitioning-during-coronavirus/ |title=State, Congressional Candidates Sign Petition to Stop Petitioning During Coronavirus |date=11 March 2020 |work=Bklyner |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314124431/https://bklyner.com/state-congressional-candidates-sign-petition-to-stop-petitioning-during-coronavirus/ |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> On 14 March, Cuomo reduced the signature requirement to 30% of the normal limit and moved the deadline from 2 April to 17 March.<ref>{{Cite news |url=http://ballot-access.org/2020/03/14/new-york-primary-petitions-cut-to-30-of-normal-but-petitioning-deadline-arrives-sooner/ |title=New York Primary Petitions Cut to 30% of Normal, but Petitioning Deadline Arrives Sooner |date=14 March 2020 |work=Ballot Access News |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200315012821/http://ballot-access.org/2020/03/14/new-york-primary-petitions-cut-to-30-of-normal-but-petitioning-deadline-arrives-sooner/ |archive-date=15 March 2020}}</ref>

On 26 March, the [[Green Party of the United States|Green Party]] said the pandemic would prevent third party candidates from appearing on the ballot unless petitioning requirements were reduced.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://news.yahoo.com/coronavirus-may-keep-thirdparty-presidential-candidates-off-the-ballot-come-november-002810766.html |title=Coronavirus may keep 3rd-party presidential candidates off the ballot |date=26 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403203522/https://news.yahoo.com/coronavirus-may-keep-thirdparty-presidential-candidates-off-the-ballot-come-november-002810766.html |archive-date=3 April 2020}}</ref>

=====Elections=====

from March 31 to July 14 |date=18 March 2020 |work=Ballot Access News |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200319153616/http://ballot-access.org/2020/03/18/alabama-postpones-run-off-primaries-from-march-31-to-july-14/ |archive-date=19 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=http://ballot-access.org/2020/03/18/missouri-governor-postpones-local-elections-from-april-7-to-june-2/ |title=Missouri Governor Postpones Local Elections from April 7 to June 2 |date=18 March 2020 |work=Ballot Access News |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200319152701/http://ballot-access.org/2020/03/18/missouri-governor-postpones-local-elections-from-april-7-to-june-2/ |archive-date=19 March 2020}}</ref> On 24 March, Secretary of State [[Barbara Cegavske]] and Nevada's seventeen county election officials announced that Nevada's June primaries would be conducted entirely through mail-in ballots.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.kolotv.com/content/news/Primary-Election-to-be-done-by-mail-due-to-COVID-19-concerns--569077821.html |title=Primary Election to be done by mail due to COVID-19 concerns |date=24 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326113419/https://www.kolotv.com/content/news/Primary-Election-to-be-done-by-mail-due-to-COVID-19-concerns--569077821.html |archive-date=26 March 2020}}</ref> Secretary of State [[Paul Pate]] increased the absentee voting period for Iowa's June primaries and also postponed special elections in three counties.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.desmoinesregister.com/story/news/politics/2020/03/23/iowa-secretary-state-extends-absentee-voting-period-june-primary-coronavirus-covid-19/2876215001/ |title=Iowa secretary of state extends absentee voting period for June primary due to coronavirus |date=23 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://sos.iowa.gov/news/2020_03_20.html |title=MEDIA RELEASE: Secretary Pate reschedules three special elections for July 7 |date=20 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326114143/https://sos.iowa.gov/news/2020_03_20.html |archive-date=26 March 2020}}</ref>

====== Wisconsin ======
{{see also|2020 Wisconsin Democratic primary|2020 Wisconsin Republican primary|2020 Milwaukee mayoral election}}

In Wisconsin, a [[swing state]] with a Democratic governor and a Republican legislature, an April 7 election for a state Supreme Court seat, the federal presidential primaries for both the Democratic and Republican parties, and several other judicial and local elections went ahead as scheduled. Due to the pandemic, at least fifteen other U.S. states cancelled or postponed scheduled elections or primaries at the time of Wisconsin's election.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Corasaniti|first1=Nick|url=https://www.nytimes.com/article/2020-campaign-primary-calendar-coronavirus.html|title=15 States Have Postponed Their Primaries Because of Coronavirus. Here's a List.|date=7 April 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=8 April 2020|last2=Saul|first2=Stephanie}}</ref> With Wisconsin grappling with [[COVID-19 pandemic in Wisconsin|their own pandemic]], state Democratic lawmakers made several attempts to postpone their election, but were prevented by other Republican legislators. Governor [[Tony Evers]] called the Wisconsin legislature into a 4 April [[special session]], but the Republican-controlled [[Wisconsin State Assembly|Assembly]] and [[Wisconsin State Senate|Senate]] graveled their sessions in and out within seventeen seconds.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Glauber|first1=Bill|url=https://www.jsonline.com/story/news/2020/04/04/wisconsin-legislature-adjourns-special-session-monday-voting-track-tuesday-election/2948444001/|title=In matter of seconds, Republicans stall Gov. Tony Evers' move to postpone Tuesday election|date=4 April 2020|work=Milwaukee Journal-Sentinel|access-date=7 April 2020|last2=Marley|first2=Patrick}}</ref> In a joint statement afterwards, Wisconsin's state Assembly Speaker [[Robin Vos]] and Senate Majority Leader [[Scott L. Fitzgerald|Scott Fitzgerald]] criticized Evers for attempting to postpone the election, for not calling a special session earlier, and for reversing his previous position on keeping the election date intact.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Beck|first=Molly|url=https://www.jsonline.com/story/news/politics/elections/2020/04/03/tony-evers-calls-lawmakers-into-session-stop-person-voting/2940156001/|title=Wisconsin Gov. Tony Evers calls special session to stop in-person voting, but Republican leaders say it should go forward|date=3 April 2020|work=Milwaukee Journal-Sentinel|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref>

On 6 April, Evers attempted to move the election by an [[executive order]], but was blocked by the [[Wisconsin Supreme Court]]. On the same day, a separate effort to extend the deadline for mailing [[absentee ballots]] was blocked by the [[Supreme Court of the United States]]. The only major concession achieved was that absentee ballots [[postmark]]ed by 7 April at 8 p.m. would be accepted until 13 April.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Herndon|first1=Astead W.|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/06/us/politics/wisconsin-primary-voting-coronavirus.html|title=Wisconsin Election Fight Heralds a National Battle Over Virus-Era Voting|date=6 April 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=7 April 2020|last2=Rutenberg|first2=Jim}}</ref> However, local media outlets reported that many voters had not received their requested absentee ballots by election day or, due to [[social distancing]], were unable to satisfy a legal requirement that they obtain a witness' signature.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Molly|first=Beck|url=https://www.jsonline.com/story/news/politics/elections/2020/04/07/state-officials-counting-absentee-voting-reduce-risk-tuesday-election-but-problems-getting-ballots-m/2953676001/|title=As election day arrives, voters hoping to avoid coronavirus say they are still waiting for absentee ballots|date=7 April 2020|work=Milwaukee Journal-Sentinel|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last=Jannene|first=Jeramey|url=https://urbanmilwaukee.com/2020/04/06/where-are-the-missing-ballots/|title=Where Are the Missing Ballots?|date=6 April 2020|work=Urban Milwaukee|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref>

Lawmakers' decision to not delay the election was sharply criticized by the editorial board of the local ''[[Milwaukee Journal-Sentinel]]'', which had previously endorsed the Republican former governor [[Scott Walker (politician)|Scott Walker]].<ref name="NYT Reid Epstein">{{Cite news|last=Epstein|first=Reid J.|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/07/us/politics/wisconsin-pandemic-primary-republicans.html|title=Why Wisconsin Republicans Insisted on an Election in a Pandemic|date=7 April 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref> They called the election "the most undemocratic in the state's history."<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.jsonline.com/story/news/solutions/2020/04/06/editorial-wisconsin-governor-tony-evers-right-stop-person-vote-during-coronavirus/2955827001/|title=Editorial: Evers' ban on in-person voting was the right call to ensure a safe, fair election during coronavirus pandemic|date=6 April 2020|work=Milwaukee Journal-Sentinel|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref> ''The New York Times'' characterized the election as "almost certain to be tarred as illegitimate," adding that the inability of the state's lawmakers to come to an agreement on moving the election was "an epic and predictable failure." The newspaper placed the political maneuvering as part of another chapter in "a decade of bitter partisan wrangling that saw [state Republicans] clinically attack and defang the state's Democratic institutions, starting with organized labor and continuing with voting laws making it far harder for poor and black residents of urban areas to vote."<ref name="NYT live">{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/07/us/politics/wisconsin-primary-election.html|title=Wisconsin Election: Voters Forced to Choose Between Protecting Their Health and Their Civic Duty|date=7 April 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref> Republicans believed that holding the election on 7 April, when Democratic-leaning urban areas were hard-hit by the pandemic, would help secure them political advantages like a continued 5–2 conservative majority on the Wisconsin Supreme Court (through the elected seat of [[Daniel Kelly (Wisconsin judge)|Daniel Kelly]]).<ref name="NYT Reid Epstein"/><ref name="Lines Masks Fear">{{Cite news|last1=Herndon|first1=Astead W.|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/07/us/politics/wisconsin-election-coronavirus.html|title=Voting in Wisconsin During a Pandemic: Lines, Masks and Plenty of Fear|date=7 April 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=8 April 2020|last2=Burns|first2=Alexander}}</ref>

When the election went ahead on 7 April, access to easy in-person voting heavily depended on where voters were located. In smaller or more rural communities, which tend to be whiter and vote Republican, few issues were reported.<ref name="Lines Masks Fear"/><ref name="Turned Out To Vote">{{Cite news|last=Herndon|first=Astead W.|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/07/us/politics/wisconsin-democratic-voters.html|title=They Turned Out to Vote in Wisconsin During a Health Crisis. Here's Why.|work=The New York Times|access-date=8 April 2020}}</ref> In more urbanized areas, the pandemic forced the closure and consolidation of many polling places around the state despite the use of 2,500 [[United States National Guard|National Guard]] members to combat a severe shortage in poll workers.<ref name="MJS live blog">{{Cite news|url=https://www.jsonline.com/story/news/politics/2020/04/07/wisconsin-april-7-presidential-primary-election-updates-voting-pandemic-milwaukee-polling-places/2959757001/|title=Election day live blog|date=7 April 2020|work=Milwaukee Journal-Sentinel|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="Madison Milwaukee poll workers">{{Cite news|last=Jannene|first=Jeramey|url=https://urbanmilwaukee.com/2020/04/07/why-does-madison-have-more-voting-sites-than-milwaukee/|title=Why Does Madison Have More Voting Sites Than Milwaukee?|date=7 April 2020|work=Urban Milwaukee|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref> The effects were felt most heavily in [[Milwaukee]], the state's largest city with the largest minority population and the center of the state's ongoing pandemic.<ref name="Lines Masks Fear"/> The city's government was only able to open 5 of 180 polling stations after being short by nearly 1,000 poll workers.<ref name="Madison Milwaukee poll workers"/> As a result, lengthy lines were reported, with some voters waiting for up to 2.5 hours and through rain showers.<ref name="MJS live blog"/><ref>{{Cite news|last=Jannene|first=Jeramey|url=https://urbanmilwaukee.com/2020/04/07/photo-gallery-long-lines-at-milwaukees-polling-places/|title=Long Lines at Milwaukee's Polling Places|date=7 April 2020|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref> The lines disproportionately affected Milwaukee's large Hispanic and African-American population; the latter had already been disproportionately afflicted with the pandemic, forming nearly half of Wisconsin's documented cases and over half its deaths at the time the vote was conducted.<ref name="NYT live"/><ref name="Turned Out To Vote"/> However, by the time the election concluded, Milwaukee Election Commissioner Neil Albrecht said that despite some of the problems, the in-person voting ran smoothly.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.wuwm.com/post/milwaukee-election-chief-despite-some-issues-person-voting-went-smoothly|title=Milwaukee Election Chief: Despite Some Issues, In-Person Voting Went Smoothly|first=Marti|last=Mikkelson|website=wuwm.com}}</ref>

Similar problems with poll station closures and long lines were reported in [[Waukesha, Wisconsin|Waukesha]], where only one polling station was opened for a city of 70,000, and [[Green Bay, Wisconsin|Green Bay]], where only 17 poll workers out of 270 were able to work.<ref name="NYT live"/> Other cities were able to keep lines much shorter, including the state capital of [[Madison, Wisconsin|Madison]], which opened about two-thirds of its usual polling locations, and [[Appleton, Wisconsin|Appleton]], which opened all of its usual 15.<ref name="MJS live blog"/><ref>{{Cite news|last=Bill|first=Ruthhart|url=https://www.chicagotribune.com/election-2020/ct-wisconsin-primary-election-20200407-ge26ymidnje65iqdrfcvnziixm-story.html|title=In battleground Wisconsin, long voter lines, no election results and a missed opportunity to build toward November|date=7 April 2020|work=Chicago Tribune|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref>

Voters across the state were advised to maintain social distancing, wear face masks, and bring their own pens.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Shabad|first1=Rebecca|url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2020-election/wisconsin-set-vote-national-guard-called-out-many-polling-places-n1178206|title=Wisconsin voters face long waits, lines amid coronavirus outbreak|date=7 April 2020|work=NBC News|access-date=7 April 2020|last2=Egan|first2=Lauren}}</ref> Vos, the state Assembly Speaker, served as an election inspector for in-person voting on 7 April. While wearing medical-like [[personal protective equipment]], he told reporters that it was "incredibly safe to go out" and vote, adding that voters faced "minimal exposure."<ref name="Lines Masks Fear"/><ref>{{Cite news|last=Kate|first=Sullivan|url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/04/07/politics/wisconsin-robin-vos-protective-gear/index.html|title=Republican Wisconsin assembly speaker wears protective gear while telling voters they are 'incredibly safe to go out'|date=7 April 2020|work=CNN|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref>

=== Venezuela ===
The Committee of Electoral Candidacies, in charge of appointing a new [[National Electoral Council (Venezuela)|National Electoral Council of Venezuela]] (CNE), announced that it would suspend its meetings until further notice because of the pandemic.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.eluniversal.com/politica/64502/comite-para-designar-nuevo-cne-suspendera-reuniones|title=Comité para designar nuevo CNE suspenderá reuniones|last=Murillo|first=Yuskerli|date=16 March 2020|website=[[El Universal (Caracas)]]|language=es|access-date=17 March 2020}}</ref>

===Armenia===

On 1 June 2020, Armenian Prime Minister [[Nikol Pashinian]] and his family were infected with COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.newindianexpress.com/world/2020/jun/01/armenian-prime-minister-his-family-test-covid-19-positive-2150730.html |title=Armenian Prime Minister, his family test COVID-19 positive |date=1 June 2020 }}</ref>

On 20 November 2020, former first lady [[Rita Sargsyan]] died from COVID-19 at the age of 58.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Մահացել է Ռիտա Սարգսյանը|url=https://armeniatoday.news/armenia/200645/|date=20 November 2020|website=Armenia Today|language=hy-AM}}</ref>

===Australia===

On 13 March 2020, [[Peter Dutton]], the [[Minister for Home Affairs (Australia)|Minister for Home Affairs]], stated that he was infected with COVID-19 and went into isolation in a hospital after having attended a [[Five Eyes]] security pact in Washington, D.C. where he met with United States President [[Donald Trump]], [[United States Attorney General]] [[William Barr]], and [[Ivanka Trump]].<ref name="USA Today">{{Cite news |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2020/03/13/coronavirus-australian-politician-who-met-ivanka-trump-attorney-general-william-barr-infected/5040253002/ |title=Australian politician who met Ivanka Trump, Attorney General William Barr infected with coronavirus |date=13 March 2020 |work=USA Today |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200313104738/https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2020/03/13/coronavirus-australian-politician-who-met-ivanka-trump-attorney-general-william-barr-infected/5040253002/ |archive-date=13 March 2020}}</ref>

===Austria===

On 17 October 2020, the Foreign Minister [[Alexander Schallenberg]] tested positive for the coronavirus.<ref name="auto1">{{cite web |title=Two foreign ministers test positive for COVID-19 after EU meeting |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-austria-minister/austrian-foreign-minister-tests-positive-for-covid-19-after-eu-meeting-idUSKBN272092 |website=Reuters |access-date=18 October 2020 |date=17 October 2020}}</ref> On 29 November 2020, the Defense Minister [[Klaudia Tanner]] tested positive for the coronavirus.<ref>{{cite web |title=Austria's Defense Minister Contracts Coronavirus |url=https://see.news/austrias-defense-minister-contracts-coronavirus/ |access-date=1 December 2020 |date=30 November 2020}}</ref>

=== Belgium ===

=== Bulgaria ===

On 25 October 2020, the Prime Minister [[Boyko Borisov]], stated that he was infected with COVID-19.<ref>{{cite web |title=Bulgarian Premier Tests Positive for Covid, Recovering at Home |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-10-25/bulgarian-premier-tests-positive-for-covid-recovering-at-home |website=Bloomberg.com |access-date=26 October 2020 |language=en |date=25 October 2020}}</ref> [[Krasen Kralev]], the country's Minister of Youth and Sports, had previously tested positive for the virus on August 23.<ref>{{cite news |title=Minister of Sports Krasen Kralev tests positive for Covid-19 |url=https://bnr.bg/en/post/101330066/minister-of-sports-krasen-kralev-tests-positive-for-covid-19 |access-date=18 December 2020 |agency=Radio Bulgaria |date=23 August 2020}}</ref>

=== Burundi ===

President of Burundi [[Pierre Nkurunziza]] died  on 8 June 2020 of a heart attack at age 55 and was later reported to have tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Burundi leader Nkurunziza died of Covid-19 — diplomats|url=https://www.the-star.co.ke/news/2020-06-10-burundi-leader-died-of-covid-19-diplomats/|access-date=2020-06-17|website=The Star|language=en-KE}}</ref> He is the first world leader to have died with the disease.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Salo|first=Jackie|date=2020-06-10|title=Burundi's President Pierre Nkurunziza may be first world leader to die of COVID-19|url=https://nypost.com/2020/06/10/burundis-pierre-nkurunziza-may-have-died-from-covid-19/|access-date=2020-06-17|website=New York Post|language=en-US}}</ref> The country's former President [[Pierre Buyoya]] also died on December 17 in Paris, where he had been flown for medical treatment after testing positive for the virus.<ref>{{cite news |title=Burundi's Pierre Buyoya dies from Covid-19 |url=https://www.iol.co.za/news/africa/burundis-pierre-buyoya-dies-from-covid-19-e47a69b8-8c26-40ce-b338-90a7bd7929d1 |access-date=18 December 2020 |agency=IOL |date=18 December 2020}}</ref>

===Canada===

On 12 March 2020, Prime Minister [[Justin Trudeau]] and his wife [[Sophie Grégoire Trudeau]] went into isolation while Sophie underwent testing that later showed that she tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-51860702 |title=Canadian PM Trudeau's wife tests positive for coronavirus |date=13 March 2020 |work=BBC |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200313124216/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-51860702 |archive-date=13 March 2020}}</ref>

On 25 March, the liberal MP from Brampton West, [[Kamal Khera]], announced that she has tested positive for COVID-19 and would be self-isolating. She was the first federal politician to test positive.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://toronto.ctvnews.ca/liberal-mp-tests-positive-for-covid-19-after-developing-flu-like-symptoms-1.4867771|title=Liberal MP tests positive for COVID-19 after developing flu-like symptoms|date=25 March 2020|website=Toronto|language=en|access-date=29 March 2020}}</ref>

===Croatia===

Several other government ministers have also tested positive for the virus during the course of the pandemic, including Justice Minister [[Ivan Malenica]] on 21 July, Tourism Minister [[Nikolina Brnjac]] on 26 October and Health Minister [[Vili Beroš]] on November 19.<ref>{{cite news |title=Ministar Ivan Malenica pozitivan na koronavirus |url=http://hr.n1info.com/Vijesti/a528783/Ministar-Ivan-Malenica-pozitivan-na-koronavirus.html |access-date=18 December 2020 |agency=N1 Hrvatska |date=21 July 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Tourism Minister Positive for Coronavirus, Two Ministers Self-isolating |url=https://www.total-croatia-news.com/politics/47675-tourism-minister-positive-for-coronavirus-two-ministers-self-isolating |access-date=18 December 2020 |agency=Total Croatia News |date=26 October 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Croatian health minister positive for coronavirus |url=https://www.croatiaweek.com/croatian-health-minister-positive-for-coronavirus/ |access-date=18 December 2020 |agency=Croatia Week |date=19 November 2020}}</ref>

===Czech Republic===

Je v izolaci, příznaky nemá |url=https://www.idnes.cz/zpravy/domaci/koronavirus-v-cesku-martin-nejedly-ma-covid-19-poradce-prezidenta-milose-zemana.A201019_102755_domaci_chtl |website=iDNES.cz |access-date=19 October 2020 |date=19 October 2020}}</ref>

===Hungary===
On 20 October 2020, Judit Varga, the Justice Minister, stated that he was infected with COVID-19.<ref>{{cite web |title=Hungarian justice minister tests positive for coronavirus |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-hungary-minister/hungarian-justice-minister-tests-positive-for-coronavirus-idUSKBN2752MM |website=Reuters |access-date=21 October 2020 |date=20 October 2020}}</ref> On 4 November, the Foreign Minister [[Péter Szijjártó]] tested positive for the virus during an official visit to [[Thailand]] and was flown home.<ref>{{cite news |title=Hungary's foreign minister tests positive for coronavirus while on state visit to Thailand |url=https://www.euronews.com/2020/11/04/hungary-s-foreign-minister-tests-positive-for-coronavirus-while-on-state-visit-to-thailand |access-date=18 December 2020 |agency=Euronews |date=4 November 2020}}</ref>

===Ireland===
{{Main|Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on politics in the Republic of Ireland}}
[[President of Sinn Féin]] [[Mary Lou McDonald]] was the first high-profile Irish politician affected by the spread of COVID-19, with her party cancelling events and her family entering self-isolation for a period, after McDonald confirmed on 2 March that her children attended the same school as the student with the first recorded case of COVID-19 in Ireland.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.newstalk.com/news/mary-lou-mcdonald-cancels-meetings-children-attend-coronavirus-hit-dublin-school-976286|title=Mary Lou McDonald cancels meetings as children attend coronavirus-hit Dublin school|website=[[Newstalk]]|date=2 March 2020|access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref> On 16 March, [[Thomas Pringle (politician)|Thomas Pringle]], an independent [[Teachta Dála|TD]] representing the [[Donegal (Dáil constituency)|Donegal]] constituency, entered isolation due to previous contact with someone in Dublin and the high risk to his own personal health.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.thejournal.ie/thomas-pringle-coronavirus-isolation-5049206-Mar2020/|title=TD Thomas Pringle in isolation after potentially coming into contact with coronavirus|work=[[TheJournal.ie]]|first=Ceimin|last=Burke|date=17 March 2020|access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.irishexaminer.com/breakingnews/ireland/donegal-td-in-isolation-amid-coronavirus-fears-988415.html|title=Donegal TD in isolation amid coronavirus fears|work=[[Irish Examiner]]|first=Stephen|last=Maguire|date=17 March 2020|access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref>

On 18 March, [[Luke 'Ming' Flanagan]], the independent [[Member of the European Parliament|MEP]] representing the [[Midlands–North-West (European Parliament constituency)|Midlands–North-West]] constituency, announced that he and his family would begin self-isolating after his daughter exhibited symptoms of COVID-19.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twitter.com/lukeming/status/1240218656241483776|title=Luke 'Ming' Flanagan|date=18 March 2020}}</ref>

On 21 August, it was announced that [[Minister for Agriculture, Food and the Marine]] [[Dara Calleary]] and [[Seanad Éireann|Seanad]] [[Cathaoirleach|Leas-Chathaoirleach]] [[Jerry Buttimer]] resigned after they attended an [[Oireachtas]] Golf Society event which contravened regulations under the Health Act.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.rte.ie/news/politics/2020/0821/1160425-politics-dara-calleary/|title=Calleary, Buttimer resign over attending Clifden event |publisher=[[RTÉ News and Current Affairs]] |first=Mary |last=Regan |date=21 August 2020 |access-date=21 August 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.thejournal.ie/dara-calleary-resigns-5181639-Aug2020/ |title=Government plunged into turmoil as Calleary resigns in wake of golf dinner controversy |publisher=[[TheJournal.ie]] |first1=Sean |last1=Murray |first2=Órla |last2=Ryan |first3=Orla |last3=Dwyer |date=21 August 2020 |access-date=21 August 2020}}</ref> The resulting scandal became known as ''[[Oireachtas Golf Society scandal|Golfgate]]''. [[European Commissioner for Trade]] [[Phil Hogan]] who also attended the dinner, resigned on 26 August 2020.

[[Leo Varadkar]], the [[Tánaiste]], re-registered as a doctor in 2020 to assist with the COVID effort.<ref name="guardian-5apr2020">{{cite news |last1=Carroll |first1=Rory |title=Irish taoiseach Leo Varadkar to work a day a week as a doctor |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/05/irish-taoiseach-leo-varadkar-to-work-a-day-a-week-as-a-doctor |access-date=5 April 2020 |work=[[The Guardian]] |date=5 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200405205033/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/05/irish-taoiseach-leo-varadkar-to-work-a-day-a-week-as-a-doctor |archive-date=5 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

===Libya===

On 24 March 2020, [[Mahmoud Jibril]], the leader of the [[National Forces Alliance]] who had served as the Minister of Foreign Affairs and Prime Minister of Libya in 2011, tested positive for coronavirus and later died on 5 April.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.mercurynews.com/2020/04/05/libyan-revolution-premier-jibril-dies-from-coronavirus-2/ |title=Libyan revolution premier Jibril dies from coronavirus |date=5 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200407163249/https://www.mercurynews.com/2020/04/05/libyan-revolution-premier-jibril-dies-from-coronavirus-2/ |archive-date=7 April 2020}}</ref>

===Italy===

On 7 March 2020, [[Nicola Zingaretti]], the [[List of Secretaries of the Democratic Party (Italy)|Secretary]] of the [[Democratic Party (Italy)|Democratic Party]] and [[List of presidents of Lazio|President of Lazio]], announced that he was infected with COVID-19 and [[Anna Ascani]], vice minister of Education, also stated that she was infected by the virus on 14 March.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/07/italy-democratic-leader-nicola-zingaretti-coronavirus |title=Leader of Italian Democratic party has coronavirus |date=7 March 2020 |work=The Guardian |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314060513/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/07/italy-democratic-leader-nicola-zingaretti-coronavirus |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus, positiva il viceministro Pd Anna Ascani. Era da giorni in isolamento |url=https://www.lanazione.it/umbria/cronaca/anna-ascani-coronavirus-1.5068092 |access-date=14 March 2020 |work=[[La Nazione]] |date=14 March 2020}}</ref>

On 4 September 2020, Italy's former Prime Minister [[Silvio Berlusconi]] was hospitalized after positive coronavirus.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Leali|first=Giorgio|date=2020-09-04|title=Silvio Berlusconi in hospital after positive coronavirus test|url=https://www.politico.eu/article/silvio-berlusconi-coronavirus-hospital/|access-date=2020-09-18|website=POLITICO}}</ref> "It has been the most dangerous test of my life," Berlusconi told reporters after leaving the hospital, adding that he "dodged a bullet once again." <ref>{{Cite web|last=Leali|first=Giorgio|date=2020-09-14|title=Silvio Berlusconi leaves hospital after coronavirus treatment|url=https://www.politico.eu/article/silvio-berlusconi-to-leave-hospital-after-coronavirus-treatment/|access-date=2020-09-18|website=POLITICO}}</ref>

On 5 October 2020, former Health Minister Beatrice Lorenzin announced that she was infected with COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-10-05|title=Covid, positivi l'ex ministra della Salute Lorenzin e il sottosegretario agli Esteri Merlo|url=https://www.repubblica.it/politica/2020/10/05/news/covid_positiva_la_deputata_dem_lorenzin-269516364/|access-date=2020-10-05|website=la Repubblica|language=it}}</ref>

On 16 October 2020, Mariastella Gelmini, a prominent member of Forza Italia, announced that she was infected with COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.repubblica.it/politica/2020/10/16/news/coronavirus_gelmini_sono_positiva_supereremo_anche_questa_-270740234/|title=Camera, tre capigruppo positivi: Gelmini, Crippa, Lollobrigida. Ceccanti: "Serve il voto a distanza"|date=16 October 2020|website=la Repubblica}}</ref>

Other positives includes: Alberto Cirio, governor of Piemonte; Pier Paolo Sileri, vice minister of Health; Andrea Orlando, vice secretary of Partito Democratico; Stefano Bonaccini, governor of Emilia Romagna; Rocco Casalino, spokesman of the prime minister Giuseppe Conte; Virginia Raggi, mayor of Rome.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://roma.repubblica.it/cronaca/2020/11/04/news/roma_la_sindaca_virginia_raggi_positiva_al_coronavirus-273147608/|title=Roma, la sindaca Virginia Raggi positiva al coronavirus|date=4 November 2020|website=la Repubblica}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.open.online/2020/09/03/i-politici-positivi-al-coronavirus/|title=Silvio Berlusconi e gli altri: la lunga lista di politici trovati positivi al Coronavirus|date=3 September 2020|website=Open}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.iodonna.it/personaggi/star-italiane/2020/10/16/coronavirus-star-e-politici-contagiati-seconda-ondata/|title=Coronavirus, tutte le star e i politici contagiati|first=Concetta|last=Desando|date=16 October 2020}}</ref>

===Monaco===

On 15 March 2020, [[Albert II, Prince of Monaco]] tested positive for coronavirus becoming the first head of state to test positive, but later recovered.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-health-coronavirus-monaco/prince-albert-of-monaco-tests-positive-for-coronavirus-idUKKBN2162WF |title=Prince Albert of Monaco tests positive for coronavirus |date=19 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404050530/https://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-health-coronavirus-monaco/prince-albert-of-monaco-tests-positive-for-coronavirus-idUKKBN2162WF |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://nypost.com/2020/03/21/prince-albert-of-monaco-first-head-of-state-to-test-positive-for-coronavirus/ |title=Prince Albert of Monaco first head of state to test positive for coronavirus |date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404050818/https://nypost.com/2020/03/21/prince-albert-of-monaco-first-head-of-state-to-test-positive-for-coronavirus/ |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://pagesix.com/2020/03/31/prince-albert-of-monaco-recovers-from-coronavirus/ |title=Prince Albert of Monaco recovers from coronavirus |date=31 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404050722/https://pagesix.com/2020/03/31/prince-albert-of-monaco-recovers-from-coronavirus/ |archive-date=4 April 2020}}</ref>

===Netherlands===

During a debate in the [[House of Representatives (Netherlands)|House of Representatives]] on the COVID-19 pandemic on 18 March 2020, [[List of Ministers of Health of the Netherlands|Minister for Medical Care]] [[Bruno Bruins]] suffered from a fainting, which was attributed to overtiredness. One day later, the king honorably discharged him at his own request. Minister [[Hugo de Jonge]] took over the tasks relating to the fight against the corona pandemic.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nu.nl/coronavirus/6038856/minister-bruins-treedt-af-de-jonge-neemt-coronadossier-over.html|title=Minister Bruins treedt af, De Jonge neemt coronadossier over|date=19 March 2020|website=NU|access-date=27 March 2020}}</ref>

===Philippines===
{{see also|COVID-19 testing controversy in the Philippines}}

Several Filipino politicians and their relatives have tested for COVID-19 causing public backlash since some of them allegedly bypassed the [[Department of Health (Philippines)|Department of Health]]'s protocol to only test symptomatic individuals or expedited the conduct and releasing of their COVID-19 testing results during a shortage on testing kits in the Philippines.<ref name="interaksyonPoliticiansFamilies">{{cite news |last1=Malasig |first1=Jeline |title=Politicians and their families get tested for COVID-19, but some people are not having it |url=https://www.interaksyon.com/politics-issues/2020/03/18/164524/politicians-families-get-tested-some-not-having/ |publisher=[[Interaksyon]] |date=18 March 2020}}</ref><ref name="gmaDuqueRITM">{{cite news |last1=Rita |first1=Joviland |title=Duque clarifies RITM director was not replaced amid alleged VIP testing for COVID-19 |url=https://www.gmanetwork.com/news/news/nation/730851/duque-clarifies-ritm-director-was-not-replaced-amid-alleged-vip-testing-for-covid-19/story/ |publisher=[[GMA News Online]] |date=23 March 2020}}</ref><ref name="No to VIP testing">{{Cite news |last=Robles |first=Alan |url=https://www.scmp.com/week-asia/politics/article/3076788/coronavirus-philippines-leak-shows-politicians-and-relatives |title=Coronavirus: in Philippines, leak shows politicians and relatives received 'VIP' testing |date=25 March 2020 |website=South China Morning Post}}</ref>

Two members of [[President of the Philippines|President]] [[Rodrigo Duterte]]'s [[Cabinet of the Philippines|Cabinet]] tested positive for COVID-19; [[Secretary of the Interior and Local Government (Philippines)|Interior Secretary]] [[Eduardo Año]]<ref>{{cite news |title=DILG chief Año positive for COVID-19 |url=https://www.gmanetwork.com/news/news/nation/732098/dilg-chief-ano-positive-for-covid-19/story/?just_in |access-date=31 March 2020 |work=GMA News |date=31 March 2020}}</ref> and [[Secretary of Education (Philippines)|Education Secretary]] [[Leonor Briones]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Hallare |first1=Katrina |title=DepEd's Briones tests positive for COVID-19 |url=https://newsinfo.inquirer.net/1256360/depeds-briones-tests-positive-for-covid-19 |access-date=9 April 2020 |work=Philippine Daily Inquirer |date=9 April 2020}}</ref>

Members of both the lower and upper chambers of the [[Congress of the Philippines]] have been confirmed to have contracted COVID-19. In the [[Senate of the Philippines|Senate]], four out of 24 Senators have contracted the disease. On 18 March 2020, Senate Majority Leader [[Juan Miguel Zubiri]] tested positive for COVID-19 after attending a meeting with a resource person at the Senate, who later tested positive as well. He and his family went into self-isolation.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.cnnphilippines.com/news/2020/3/16/Migz-Zubiri-COVID-19-positive.html|title=Senator Zubiri tests positive for COVID-19|date=16 March 2020|work=[[CNN Philippines]]}}</ref> Senators [[Koko Pimentel]]<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Rey|first1=Aika|title=Pimentel tests positive for coronavirus|url=https://www.rappler.com/nation/255806-koko-pimentel-tests-positive-coronavirus|access-date=25 March 2020|work=[[Rappler]]|date=25 March 2020}}</ref> and [[Sonny Angara]]<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rappler.com/nation/255962-sonny-angara-tests-positive-coronavirus|title=Sonny Angara tests positive for coronavirus|date=26 March 2020|work=[[Rappler]]}}</ref> tested positive for the virus on 25 and 26 March respectively. On 9 August, Senator [[Bong Revilla]] announced that he had contracted COVID-19 as well.<ref>{{cite news |title=Senator Bong Revilla tests positive for COVID-19 |url=https://cnnphilippines.com/news/2020/8/9/Senator-Bong-Revilla-coronavirus-positive.html |access-date=19 August 2020 |work=CNN Philippines |date=9 August 2020}}</ref>

The [[House of Representatives of the Philippines|House of Representatives]] has eight members who have contracted COVID-19.<ref name="daza55">{{cite news |last1=Luci-Atienza |first1=Charissa |title=Rep. Daza is 55th COVID-19 case at House of Representatives |url=https://mb.com.ph/2020/08/26/rep-daza-is-55th-covid-19-case-at-house-of-representatives/ |access-date=26 August 2020 |work=Manila Bulletin |date=26 August 2020}}</ref> The first member confirmed oto have contracted the disease was [[Bulacan]] [[Legislative districts of Bulacan#4th District|4th District]] representative Henry Villarica on 26 March.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://cnnphilippines.com/news/2020/3/27/Henry-Villarica-tests-positive-for-COVID-19-.html???|title=Bulacan congressman tests positive for COVID-19|date=26 March 2020|work=[[CNN Philippines]]}}</ref> Other members who tested COVID-19 positive are Deputy Speaker and Surigao del Sur 2nd District representative [[Johnny Pimentel]], Deputy Speaker and Basilan lone district representative [[Mujiv Hataman]], Sulu 1st District representative Samier Tan and Northern Samar 1st District representative Paul Ruiz Daza.<ref name="daza55"/> At least two legislators died from the disease; Sorsogon 2nd District representative [[Bernardita Ramos]] and [[Senior Citizens Partylist]] representative Francisco Datol Jr.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Rosario |first1=Ben |title=Sorsogon representative dies from COVID-19 |url=https://mb.com.ph/2020/09/08/sorsogon-representative-dies-from-covid-19/ |access-date=September 8, 2020 |work=Manila Bulletin |date=September 8, 2020}}</ref>

[[ACT-CIS Partylist]] representative [[Eric Go Yap]] was initially reported to have tested positive for the virus, but later announced that he had actually tested negative, with the initial erroneous result attributed to an encoding error by the testing laboratory.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Cepeda|first1=Mara|title=House appropriations panel chair Eric Yap tests positive for coronavirus|url=https://www.rappler.com/nation/255883-house-appropriations-panel-chair-eric-yap-tests-positive-coronavirus|access-date=25 March 2020|work=[[Rappler]]|date=25 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.gmanetwork.com/news/news/nation/731592/ritm-says-yap-negative-for-covid-19-apologizes-for-error/story/|title=RITM says Yap negative for COVID-19, apologizes for error|publisher=GMA News|date=27 March 2020}}</ref>

In the provincial level, [[Rebecca Ynares]], the [[Governor of Rizal]], announced on 26 March to have tested positive for the virus.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Lalu|first1=Gabriel Pabico|title=Rizal Governor Nini Ynares tests positive for COVID-19|url=https://newsinfo.inquirer.net/1248499/rizal-governor-nini-ynares-tests-positive-for-covid-19|access-date=26 March 2020|work=[[Philippine Daily Inquirer]]|date=25 March 2020}}</ref> In the municipal level, Ferdinand Estrella, Mayor of [[Baliuag, Bulacan|Baliuag]], announced on 17 March that he had tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Magsambol|first1=Bonz|title=Baliuag, Bulacan mayor tests positive for coronavirus|url=https://www.rappler.com/nation/254901-baliuag-bulacan-mayor-tests-positive-coronavirus|access-date=26 March 2020|work=[[Rappler]]|date=17 March 2020}}</ref> On 20 March, [[Caba, La Union|Caba]], [[La Union]] Mayor Philip Crispin announced that both he and Donna Crispino, his wife and a councilor of the town, had contracted the virus.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Fonbuena|first1=Carmela|title=La Union mayor, councilor test positive for coronavirus|url=https://www.rappler.com/nation/255298-la-union-coronavirus-cases-march-20-2020|access-date=26 March 2020|work=[[Rappler]]|date=20 March 2020}}</ref> Batangas City Council Julian Pedro Pastor died from COVID-19 on 4 April.<ref>{{cite news |title=Batangas City councilor who tested positive for COVID-19 dies |url=https://www.cnnphilippines.com/regional/2020/4/5/Batangas-City-councilor-COVID-19-positive-dies.html |access-date=5 April 2020 |work=CNN Philippines |date=5 April 2020}}</ref> [[Lapu-Lapu, Philippines|Lapu-Lapu]] City Mayor [[Junard Chan]] tested positive for COVID-19 on June 11 although he is asymptomatic at the time of confirmation.<ref name=lapulapumayor>{{cite news |title=Lapu-Lapu City Mayor tests positive for COVID-19 |url=https://cnnphilippines.com/regional/2020/6/12/Lapu-Lapu-City-Mayor-Junard-Ahong-Chan-COVID-19.html |access-date=12 June 2020 |work=CNN Philippines |date=12 June 2020}}</ref>

At least two members of the regional [[Bangsamoro Parliament]] tested positive for COVID-19; Bangsamoro regional health minister [[Saffrullah Dipatuan]]<ref>{{cite news |last1=Ranada |first1=Pia |title=Bangsamoro health minister tests positive for COVID-19 |url=https://rappler.com/nation/bangsamoro-health-minister-tests-positive-covid-19 |access-date=3 September 2020 |work=Rappler |date=2 September 2020}}</ref> and Marjanie Mimbantas-Macasalong<ref>{{cite news |last1=Fernandez |first1=Edwin |title=Another BARMM parliament member test positive for COVID-19 |url=https://newsinfo.inquirer.net/1333682/another-barmm-parliament-member-test-positive-for-covid-19 |access-date=10 September 2020 |work=Philippine Daily Inquirer |date=10 September 2020}}</ref>

=== Poland ===

On 24 October 2020, the president [[Andrzej Duda]] tested positive for coronavirus.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/health-coronavirus-poland-idUSL8N2HF03L|title=Polish President Duda infected with coronavirus, feels good -minister|first=Reuters|last=Staff|date=24 October 2020|via=www.reuters.com}}</ref> Several other ministers have also tested positive during the course of the pandemic, including Environment Minister [[Michał Kurtyka]] on 20 August, former Health Minister [[Łukasz Szumowski]] on 29 September, Education Minister [[Przemysław Czarnek]] on 5 October (which delayed Czarnek's swearing-in as minister) and Defence Minister [[Mariusz Błaszczak]] on 25 October.<ref>{{cite news |title=Michał Kurtyka, minister klimatu jest zarażony koronawirusem COVID-19 |url=https://portalkomunalny.pl/michal-kurtyka-minister-klimatu-zarazony-koronawirusem-covid-19-409024/# |access-date=18 December 2020 |agency=Portal Komunalny |date=20 August 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Koronawirus w Polsce. Łukasz Szumowski zakażony. Znamy szczegóły |url=https://www.o2.pl/informacje/koronawirus-w-polsce-lukasz-szumowski-zakazony-znamy-szczegoly-6559160296680288a |access-date=18 December 2020 |agency=O2 |date=29 September 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Poland's new education minister tests positive for COVID, swearing-in postponed |url=https://reuters.com/article/idUSKBN26Q1FQ |access-date=18 December 2020 |work=Reuters |date=5 October 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Polish defence minister tests positive for COVID-19 after quarantine |url=https://www.thefirstnews.com/article/polish-defence-minister-tests-positive-for-covid-19-after-quarantine-17044 |access-date=18 December 2020 |agency=The First News |date=25 October 2020}}</ref>

===Russia===

On 30 April 2020, [[Prime Minister of Russia|Prime Minister]] [[Mikhail Mishustin]] told President [[Vladimir Putin]] that he had tested positive for coronavirus. He temporarily left his position to recover and asked for First Deputy Prime Minister [[Andrey Belousov]] to serve as acting prime minister.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-russia-mishustin/russian-prime-minister-mikhail-mishustin-tells-putin-he-has-coronavirus-idUSKBN22C357 |title=Russian Prime Minister Mikhail Mishustin tells Putin he has coronavirus |date=30 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://archive.today/20200430183428/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-russia-mishustin/russian-prime-minister-mikhail-mishustin-tells-putin-he-has-coronavirus-idUSKBN22C357 |archive-date=30 April 2020}}</ref> The next day, the Construction Minister [[Vladimir Yakushev]] also tested positive for the coronavirus.<ref>{{cite news |title= Владимир Якушев госпитализирован с коронавирусом |url= https://tass.ru/obschestvo/8386125 |access-date= 1 May 2020 |work= [[TASS]] |date= 1 May 2020}}</ref>  On 6 May, the Culture Minister [[Olga Lyubimova]] tested positive for the coronavirus.<ref>{{cite news |title= Министр культуры Ольга Любимова заразилась коронавирусом |url= https://ria.ru/20200506/1571029307.html |access-date= 6 May 2020 |work= РИА Новости |date= 6 May 2020}}</ref>

===Slovakia===
On 12 October, the Deputy Speaker of the National Council Gábor Grendel tested positive for the coronavirus.<ref>{{cite web |title=Grendel mal koronavírus. Konal maximálne nezodpovedne, tvrdí Pellegrini |url=https://slovensko.hnonline.sk/2228128-grendel-mal-koronavirus-konal-maximalne-nezodpovedne-tvrdi-pellegrini |website=hnonline.sk |access-date=18 October 2020 |date=12 October 2020}}</ref> Prime Minister [[Igor Matovič]] tested positive for the virus on December 18.<ref>{{cite news |title=Slovak prime minister Matovic tests positive for COVID-19 |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-slovakia-matovic/slovak-prime-minister-matovic-tests-positive-for-covid-19-idUSKBN28S1P3?il=0 |access-date=18 December 2020 |work=Reuters |date=18 December 2020}}</ref>

===South Africa===
[[Kenneth Meshoe]], leader of the [[African Christian Democratic Party]], had been tested for COVID-19 on 22 March 2020 after he participated in a religious gathering in the [[Free State]] where five international guests also tested positive for the virus.<ref>{{cite web |title=ACDP leader Kenneth Meshoe tested for coronavirus |url=https://www.iol.co.za/news/politics/acdp-leader-kenneth-meshoe-tested-for-coronavirus-45370006 |website=IOL |access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref> The ACDP deputy leader [[Wayne Thring]] announced on 27 March that Meshoe and fellow ACDP MP [[Steven Swart]] had tested positive for the virus.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Thring |first1=Wayne |title=ACDP statement on COVID 19 test results of Rev Kenneth Meshoe and Steve Swart MP |url=https://www.acdp.org.za/2020/03/27/acdp-statement-on-covid-19-test-results-of-rev-kenneth-meshoe-and-steve-swart-mp/ |website=ACDP |access-date=27 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Madia |first1=Tshidi |title=Coronavirus in SA: ACDP's Kenneth Meshoe and Steve Swart test positive |url=https://www.news24.com/SouthAfrica/News/coronavirus-in-sa-acdps-kenneth-meshoe-and-steve-swart-test-positive-20200327 |access-date=27 March 2020 |newspaper=News24 |date=27 March 2020}}</ref>

[[Gladys Bakubaku-Vos]], [[Member of the Western Cape Provincial Parliament]] for [[African National Congress]], tested positive for the virus on 5 May.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Gerber |first1=Jan |title=Western Cape ANC MPL tests positive for Covid-19 |url=https://www.news24.com/news24/southafrica/news/western-cape-anc-mpl-tests-positive-for-covid-19-20200505 |access-date=7 July 2020 |newspaper=News24 |date=5 May 2020}}</ref> [[Mlungisi Mvoko]], Eastern Cape Finance MEC, and his wife both tested positive for the virus on 19 June.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Shange |first1=Naledi |title=Eastern Cape finance MEC Mlungisi Mvoko and his wife test positive for Covid-19 ===Spain===
On 8 March 2020, [[Vox (political party)|Vox]] held a political rally that was attended by over 9,000 people and later apologised after [[Santiago Abascal]], its president, [[Javier Ortega Smith]], its secretary general, and multiple members of its party in the Congress of Deputies  tested positive for COVID-19.<ref name="vox infections"/> On 12 March, [[Ministry of Equality (Spain)|Minister of Equality]] [[Irene Montero]] and [[Minister of Territorial Policy and Civil Service (Spain)|Minister of Territorial Policy]] [[Carolina Darias]] tested positive for COVID-19. On 14 March, the wife of [[Prime Minister of Spain|Prime Minister]] [[Pedro Sánchez]] tested positive, therefore leading to place a quarantine in the Prime Minister. On 16 March, [[President of the Community of Madrid]] [[Isabel Díaz Ayuso]] and [[President of the Government of Catalonia|President of Catalonia]] [[Quim Torra]] tested positive.

===United Kingdom===

On 5 March 2020, [[Department of Health and Social Care|Under-Secretary of State for Mental Health, Suicide Prevention and Patient Safety]] and parliamentarian [[Nadine Dorries]] showed symptoms of COVID-19 after meeting with Prime Minister [[Boris Johnson]] and later tested positive. [[Shadow Secretary of State for Work and Pensions]] and parliamentarian [[Rachael Maskell]] went into isolation due to coming in contact with Dorries.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-51827356 |title=Coronavirus: Health minister Nadine Dorries tests positive |date=11 March 2020 |work=BBC |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314054919/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-51827356 |archive-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> [[Kate Osborne]], a Labour MP, was the second MP to test positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.itv.com/news/2020-03-16/kate-osborne-mp-coronavirus-covid-19/|title=Second MP Kate Osborne diagnosed with coronavirus following self-isolation|work=ITV News|date=16 March 2020|access-date=16 March 2020}}</ref> [[Lloyd Russell-Moyle]] was the third MP to test positive.

On 25 March, [[Charles, Prince of Wales]] became the first member of the British royal family to test positive for coronavirus.<ref name="ReferenceA">{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-52033845?at_custom4=10BCF49A-6E85-11EA-9B57-05D7923C408C&at_custom1=%5Bpost+type%5D&at_custom2=twitter&at_custom3=%40BBCBreaking&at_medium=custom7&at_campaign=64 |title=Coronavirus: Prince Charles tests positive but 'remains in good health' |date=26 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326123230/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-52033845?at_custom4=10BCF49A-6E85-11EA-9B57-05D7923C408C&at_custom1=%5Bpost+type%5D&at_custom2=twitter&at_custom3=%40BBCBreaking&at_medium=custom7&at_campaign=64 |archive-date=26 March 2020}}</ref>

[[Boris Johnson]] went into isolation in [[10 Downing Street]] and on 27 March, he announced that he had tested positive for coronavirus.<ref name="bbc.com">{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-52060791 |title=PM Boris Johnson tests positive for coronavirus |date=27 March 2020 |work=BBC}}</ref> The [[Secretary of State for Health and Social Care]] [[Matt Hancock]] announced he had also tested positive hours later.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.itv.com/news/2020-03-27/health-secretary-matt-hancock-tests-positive-for-coronavirus|title=Health Secretary Matt Hancock tests positive for coronavirus|work=ITV News|date=27 March 2020|access-date=24 August 2020}}</ref> On 5 April, Johnson was admitted to [[St Thomas' Hospital]] in Westminster and was later moved to the intensive care unit the following day.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/04/06/uk/boris-johnson-coronavirus-hospital-gbr-intl/index.html |title=Boris Johnson moved to intensive care unit as coronavirus symptoms have 'worsened' |date=6 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406132613/https://www.cnn.com/2020/04/06/uk/boris-johnson-coronavirus-hospital-gbr-intl/index.html |archive-date=6 April 2020}}</ref>

===United States===
{{further|White House COVID-19 outbreak}}
The [[Conservative Political Action Conference]] (CPAC) was held from 26 to 29 February 2020, and it was later discovered that one of the attendants with a gold-level VIP ticket had met with multiple high level politicians. These included Senators [[Ted Cruz]], [[Rick Scott]], and [[Lindsey Graham]]; and Representatives [[Mark Meadows (North Carolina politician)|Mark Meadows]], [[Paul Gosar]], [[Doug Collins (politician)|Doug Collins]], and [[Matt Gaetz]] all of whom later went into self-quarantine along with other members of the [[Republican Party (United States)|Republican Party]].<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/03/09/politics/coronavirus-lawmakers-quarantine-isolation/index.html |title=Ted Cruz to extend self-quarantine after second interaction with individual who tested positive for coronavirus |date=13 March 2020 |work=CNN |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200313010159/https://www.cnn.com/2020/03/09/politics/coronavirus-lawmakers-quarantine-isolation/index.html |archive-date=13 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2020/03/09/cpac-coronavirus-attendees-124808 |title=CPAC scrambles to contain coronavirus fallout |date=9 March 2020 |work=Politico |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200313153353/https://www.politico.com/news/2020/03/09/cpac-coronavirus-attendees-124808 |archive-date=13 March 2020}}</ref>

On 20 June, President Trump held a [[2020 Trump Tulsa rally|rally]] in Tulsa, Oklahoma, and afterwards multiple attendees tested positive for COVID-19 and Oklahoma saw its second highest single-day increase in COVID-19 cases.<ref>{{Cite news|date=July 11, 2020 |title=Three Weeks After Trump's Tulsa Rally, Oklahoma Reports Record High COVID-19 Numbers |work=[[Time (magazine)|Time]] |url=https://time.com/5865890/oklahoma-covid-19-trump-tulsa-rally/ |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/pVKba |archive-date=July 12, 2020}}</ref> On 15 July, Oklahoma Governor [[Kevin Stitt]] announced that he had tested positive, becoming the first governor in the United States to do so.<ref>{{Cite news|date=July 16, 2020 |title=Watch Now: Kevin Stitt 'pretty shocked' to be first governor to test positive for COVID-19 |work=[[Tulsa World]] |url=https://tulsaworld.com/news/local/watch-now-kevin-stitt-pretty-shocked-to-be-first-governor-to-test-positive-for-covid/article_781a1f60-e4d1-5158-85e8-b89b1a6fb510.html |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/H2SkW |archive-date=July 12, 2020}}</ref> On 29 June, former Republican presidential candidate [[Herman Cain]] tested positive for COVID-19 and was hospitalized for treatment on 1 July. On 30 July, Cain died of complications of COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news|date=July 2, 2020 |title=Herman Cain hospitalized after testing positive for coronavirus |work=[[Fox News]] |url=https://www.foxnews.com/politics/herman-cain-hospitalized-after-testing-postive-for-coronavirus |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/D9bTq |archive-date=July 30, 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|date=July 30, 2020 |title=Herman Cain dies from coronavirus after being hospitalised following Trump's Tulsa rally |work=[[The Independent]] |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/herman-cain-death-coronavirus-age-cause-hospital-covid-update-a9646186.html |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/URxxC |archive-date=July 30, 2020}}</ref>

On October 1, President [[Donald Trump]] and First Lady [[Melania Trump]] tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Singh|first=Maanvi|date=2020-10-02|title=Donald Trump and first lady Melania test positive for coronavirus|language=en-GB|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2020/oct/01/hope-hicks-covid-19-reports-trump|access-date=2020-10-02|issn=0261-3077}}</ref> On October 2, Donald was admitted to [[Walter Reed National Military Medical Center]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Beckett |first1=Lois |title=Trump taken to hospital by helicopter after Covid diagnosis |url=https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2020/oct/02/trump-hospital-covid-coronavirus-diagnosis |access-date=3 October 2020 |agency=The Guardian}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last1=Liptak |first1=Kevin |title=Trump taken to Walter Reed medical center and will be hospitalized 'for the next few days' |url=https://edition.cnn.com/2020/10/02/politics/president-donald-trump-walter-reed-coronavirus/index.html |website=CNN |access-date=3 October 2020}}</ref>

On November 9, 2020, [[Ben Carson]], Secretary of Housing and Urban Development, tested positive for [[Coronavirus disease 2019|COVID-19.]]<ref>{{Cite web|last=Pramuk|first=Kevin Breuninger,Jacob|date=November 9, 2020|title=HUD Secretary Ben Carson tests positive for coronavirus|url=https://www.cnbc.com/2020/11/09/hud-secretary-ben-carson-tests-positive-for-coronavirus.html|access-date=November 9, 2020|website=CNBC|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|title= Ben Carson is the latest Trump official to test positive for coronavirus | work=CNN |url= https://www.cnn.com/2020/11/09/politics/ben-carson-coronavirus/index.html | access-date=November 9, 2020}}</ref>

to test positive for coronavirus |date=18 March 2020 |work=Politico |url-status=live
