|url=https://www.thedailybeast.com/rep-ben-mcadams-second-member-of-congress-tests-positive-for-covid-19?source=articles&via=rss |title=Second Member of Congress Tests Positive for COVID-19 |date=18 March 2020 |work=Politico |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200319004710/https://www.thedailybeast.com/rep-ben-mcadams-second-member-of-congress-tests-positive-for-covid-19?source=articles&via=rss |archive-date=19 March 2020}}</ref> On 22 March, Senator [[Rand Paul]] (R-KY) became the first member of the Senate to test positive for coronavirus, but despite having taken the test he did not go into isolation causing Senators [[Mitt Romney]] and [[Mike Lee (American politician)|Mike Lee]] to go into isolation after having made contact with Paul.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://nypost.com/2020/03/24/rand-paul-defends-decision-to-not-self-quarantine-while-awaiting-coronavirus-test/ |title=Rand Paul defends decision to not self-quarantine while awaiting coronavirus test |date=24 March 2020 |work=New York Post |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200325105052/https://nypost.com/2020/03/24/rand-paul-defends-decision-to-not-self-quarantine-while-awaiting-coronavirus-test/ |archive-date=25 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.npr.org/sections/coronavirus-live-updates/2020/03/23/819980899/3-gop-senators-in-self-quarantine-will-be-unable-to-vote-on-coronavirus-relief |title=3 GOP Senators In Self-Quarantine Will Be Unable To Vote On Coronavirus Relief |date=23 March 2020 |work=NPR |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200325105148/https://www.npr.org/sections/coronavirus-live-updates/2020/03/23/819980899/3-gop-senators-in-self-quarantine-will-be-unable-to-vote-on-coronavirus-relief |archive-date=25 March 2020}}</ref> On 19 March, [[Joe Cunningham (American politician)|Joe Cunningham]] (D-[[South Carolina's 1st congressional district|SC-1]]) went into isolation after coming into contact with another member of Congress who tested positive and on 27 March he announced that he tested positive for the virus.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://abcnews4.com/news/local/rep-joe-cunningham-goes-into-self-quarantine |title=Rep. Joe Cunningham goes into self-quarantine |date=19 March 2020 |work=NPR |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327175410/https://abcnews4.com/news/local/rep-joe-cunningham-goes-into-self-quarantine |archive-date=27 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.live5news.com/2020/03/27/rep-cunningham-says-he-tested-positive-covid-/ |title=Rep. Cunningham says he tested positive for COVID-19 |date=27 March 2020}}</ref> On 27 March, Representative [[Mike Kelly (Pennsylvania politician)|Mike Kelly]] (R-[[Pennsylvania's 16th congressional district|PA-16]]) tested positive for COVID-19, but later tested negative on May 6.<ref>{{Cite news|date=May 12, 2020 |title=Kelly Defeats COVID-19, Donates Convalescent Plasma to Aid Others in the Fight |url=https://kelly.house.gov/press-release/kelly-defeats-covid-19-donates-convalescent-plasma-aid-others-their-fight |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/9g9zc |archive-date=August 1, 2020}}</ref> On 6 April, Representative [[Neal Dunn]] (R-[[Florida's 2nd congressional district|FL-2)]] announced that he had tested positive for COVID-19 after going to the emergency room due to him not feeling well and went into quarantine.<ref>{{Cite news|date=April 9, 2020 |title=North Florida Congressman Neal Dunn Tests Positive For COVID-19 |work=News Service of Florida |url=https://news.wfsu.org/wfsu-local-news/2020-04-09/north-florida-congressman-neal-dunn-tests-positive-for-covid-19 |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/CaWOg |archive-date=August 1, 2020}}</ref> On 15 June, Representative [[Tom Rice]] (R-[[South Carolina's 7th congressional district|SC-7)]] announced that he, his wife, and his son had tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news|date=June 15, 2020 |title=U.S. Rep. Tom Rice, 2 family members have COVID-19 |work=[[NBC]] |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/politics-news/u-s-rep-tom-rice-2-family-members-have-covid-n1231134 |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/UD7Wo |archive-date=August 1, 2020}}</ref> On 14 July, [[Morgan Griffith]] (R-[[Virginia's 9th congressional district|VA-9]]) announced that he had tested positive for COVID-19 and went into isolation.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/07/14/politics/morgan-griffith-tests-positive-coronavirus/index.html |title=Virginia Republican congressman tests positive for coronavirus |date=14 July 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://archive.today/20200714191247/https://www.cnn.com/2020/07/14/politics/morgan-griffith-tests-positive-coronavirus/index.html |archive-date=14 July 2020 |access-date=14 July 2020 }}</ref>

On 25 March, Representative [[Seth Moulton]] (D-[[Massachusetts's 6th congressional district|MA-6)]] announced that he was going into quarantine after suffering from mild symptoms of COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news|date=March 25, 2020 |title=Seth Moulton is self-quarantining after reporting symptoms of potential COVID-19 |url=https://www.boston.com/news/politics/2020/03/25/seth-moulton-coronavirus |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/BQsgO |archive-date=August 1, 2020}}</ref> On 30 March, Representative [[Nydia Velázquez]] (D-[[New York's 7th congressional district|NY-7)]] announced that she had the common symptoms of COVID-19 and that her doctor stated that she had the virus.<ref>{{Cite news|date=June 15, 2020 |title=Congresswoman Nydia Velazquez Announces Coronavirus Infection |work=[[WLNY-TV]] |url=https://newyork.cbslocal.com/2020/03/31/congresswoman-nydia-velazquez-announces-coronavirus-infection/ |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/b4D3P |archive-date=August 1, 2020}}</ref>

On 29 July, [[Louie Gohmert]] (R-[[Texas's 1st congressional district|TX-1]]) announced that he had tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news|date=July 29, 2020 |title=Louie Gohmert, who refused to wear a mask, tests positive for coronavirus |work=[[Politico]] |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2020/07/29/louis-gohmert-who-refused-to-wear-a-mask-tests-positive-for-coronavirus-386076 |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/bJCtK |archive-date=July 29, 2020}}</ref> Prior to testing positive Gohmert had his office be full of people and allegedly criticized staffers who wore masks.<ref>{{Cite news|date=July 29, 2020 |title=Gohmert Aide Alleges Staffers Are 'Berated' For Wearing Masks, Office Is Regularly Full |work=[[Forbes]] |url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/andrewsolender/2020/07/29/gohmert-aide-alleges-staffers-are-berated-for-wearing-masks-office-is-regularly-full/#250dd63577f2 |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/pJXxn |archive-date=August 1, 2020}}</ref> On 31 July, Representative [[Raúl Grijalva]] (D-[[Arizona's 3rd congressional district|AZ-3]]) announced that he had tested positive for COVID-19. Grijalva had went into quarantine after Representative Gohmert tested positive due to Gohmert refusal to wear a mask at public meetings.<ref>{{Cite news|date=August 1, 2020 |title=Arizona Congressman Raúl Grijalva Tests Positive For COVID-19 |work=[[NPR]] |url=https://www.npr.org/sections/coronavirus-live-updates/2020/08/01/898159910/arizona-congressman-ra-l-grijalva-tests-positive-for-covid-19 |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/tkUUx |archive-date=August 1, 2020}}</ref>

On 12 November, [[Don Young]] (R-[[Alaska's at-large congressional district|AK-at-large]]) tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news|date=November 12, 2020 |title=Arizona Congressman Raúl Grijalva Tests Positive For COVID-19 |work=[[Alaska Public Media]] |url=https://www.alaskapublic.org/2020/11/12/alaska-rep-don-young-campaign-staff-diagnosed-with-covid-19/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://archive.vn/coKu2 |archive-date=November 12, 2020}}</ref>

====United States Senate====

On 7 April, Sen. [[Rand Paul]] announced that he had recovered from the coronavirus and would start volunteering at a local hospital.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.foxnews.com/politics/rand-paul-recovers-from-coronavirus |title=Rand Paul recovers from coronavirus, tests negative |date=7 April 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200407223846/https://www.foxnews.com/politics/rand-paul-recovers-from-coronavirus |archive-date=7 April 2020}}</ref> In March, Senators [[Tim Kaine]] (D-VA) and [[Bob Casey Jr.]] (D-PA) announced that both of them had tested positive for coronavirus antibodies.<ref>{{Cite news|date=May 29, 2020 |title=Second senator tests positive for coronavirus antibodies |work=[[The Hill (newspaper)|The Hill]] |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/senate/500109-second-senator-tests-positive-for-coronavirus-antibodies |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.vn/9l6qD |archive-date=August 1, 2020}}</ref> On October 1, Sen. [[Mike Lee (American politician)|Mike Lee]] of (R-UT) tested positive for the virus after meeting with President Trump's [[Supreme Court of the United States|Supreme Court]] nominee, [[Amy Coney Barrett]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2020/10/02/mike-lee-tests-positive-covid-425172|title=Sens. Tillis and Lee test positive for Covid|first=Burgess|last=Everett|website=POLITICO}}</ref> A day later, on October 2, Sen. [[Thom Tillis]] announced he had tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news|date=October 2, 2020|title=GOP Sen. Thom Tillis tests positive for coronavirus|work=[[The Hill (newspaper)|The Hill]] |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/senate/519443-gop-sen-thom-tillis-tests-positive-for-coronavirus}}</ref>
